# Skadoodle — Project Context for Claude

## About the Developer
Eddie Brayman, 72, independent iOS developer, East Village NYC. 50+ years coding experience. Works solo with Claude as primary coding partner. Philosophy: one price, no ads, ever. Ship-ready every build. Direct about uncertainty rather than guessing.

---

## What This App Is
**Skadoodle** (Xcode project name: `snoodle`) is a social doodling app for iPhone and iPad. Users draw, get AI-generated captions and tags, save to a private local gallery, and optionally post to a community world gallery backed by Firebase.

**App Store ID:** 6771497563  
**App Store URL:** https://apps.apple.com/us/app/skadoodle/id6771497563  
**Bundle ID:** maxsdad.skadoodle  
**Firebase project:** snoodle-68bfc  
**Current version at last session:** **3.3 submitted to the App Store** — Jul 19, 2026, Waiting for Review / Ready for Review both logged at 12:44 PM. Not yet cleared review — update this line once Ready for Distribution comes through. Built and archived as a Release configuration for both iPhone and iPad. Ships this session's work: a full pen pressure/taper overhaul (removed a live-recompute taper bug that had every pen — Pencil, Ink, Brush, Chalk, Calligraphy, Neon, Watercolor, Dotted, and every Dual Tone style — silently re-thinning/re-coloring already-drawn strokes on every redraw; Pencil got a new floor+ratio pressure curve so light pressure ≈ the selected thickness and full pressure ≈ +50-260% of it depending on preset), recent-colors now reorder to the front of their picker row only when a color is actually drawn/placed with (not on mere tap), Chevron pen replaced with Sparkle, and two real bugs found and fixed this session: the Effects screen's pinch-zoom/pan "bake" step was skipping the 1600px background-image downsample cap entirely (confirmed on device — background images dropped from ~2.7MB to ~570KB after the fix), and the `joinedAt` backfill script was actually run this time (1 user doc backfilled, confirmed via Eddie's terminal output). Also recovered from a real scare mid-session: `DrawScreen.swift` was found truncated to 3 bytes for unknown reasons — recovered via Xcode's local undo history, verified byte-for-byte via a brace/paren-balance match against the last known-good state, then committed to git (previously 11 days of uncommitted work — see "Development Workflow" below for the git-workflow fix that came out of this).

**Previously — 3.2 is live in the App Store** — submitted ~4 PM, Ready for Distribution by ~1 AM (exact date/time not logged this round, but same fast overnight shape as 3.1). Eddie's own framing: "thats 2 in a row that we submitted about 4pm and got released by 1am" — 3.1 and 3.2 have now both cleared review on that exact turnaround, on top of 2.7's same-day clearance earlier. **The submit-~4pm/live-by-~1am pattern is now confirmed twice in a row, not just a hunch** — worth actively planning submissions around this window rather than treating it as coincidence.

**3.1 is live in the App Store** (submitted Jul 13, 2026 3:41 PM; Waiting/Ready for Review 3:41 PM; In Review Jul 14 1:33 AM; Ready for Distribution Jul 14 1:34 AM — another fast overnight turnaround). Ships the target-video-length timelapse export feature (see "v3.1" section below) plus the caption override + background-editing shortcuts (hidden tap-to-edit caption, "Edit Background" BG-chip menu option, 3-finger-tap-to-extract).

**3.2 status — pen work confirmed done; several smaller fixes built but not yet confirmed on device.** Clipboard paste was attempted and fully reverted (not shipping — see "In Progress — v3.2" below). The Pen Studio redesign is **confirmed done end-to-end on device**: category tabs (final scheme, after two regroups: **Basic** = Pencil/Ink/Marker/Chalk/Calligraphy/Neon, **Paint** = Brush/Watercolor/Spray/Airbrush, **Pattern** = Dotted/Confetti/Dashed/Hearts/Chevron/Splatter, plus Dual Tone unchanged), 6 new pens this cycle (Airbrush, Dashed, Hearts, Chevron, Splatter — Calligraphy/Confetti carried over from 2.8), Airbrush's perf fix, and the Dual Tone per-style icon fix — Eddie's own words: "pens are awesome... splatter is perfect. all great... cant think of any others" for Basic/Paint, and an emoji/stamp-pen idea for Pattern was floated and deliberately not built (not worth the UI cost for a rarely-used pen). **The pens are the only genuinely user-new thing in 3.2.** Three other items in this doc were mistakenly drafted into "What's New" copy as if they were new capabilities — Eddie caught this directly ("been happening a lot") and corrected it:
- **Background pinch-zoom** — the feature itself (pinch to resize a background photo in the Effects screen) has existed since v2.1. What's actually new is a narrow bug fix (iPad live-canvas-update-on-commit + removing an artificial zoom-out floor) — not something worth a release-note bullet, at most folds into a generic "bug fixes" line.
- **Layers panel "+"** — the button itself has existed since v2.2. What changed is only *where* the new layer lands (above the selected layer vs. always at the top) — same story, a workflow tweak, not a new feature.
- **Community grid play button for your own posted doodles** — per Eddie's direct correction, this already shipped 3-4 versions ago. The "In Progress" section below documenting it as new work is stale/redundant and should not be treated as unshipped 3.2 material.

**Lesson for future What's New drafts: don't read a "Fixed"/"In Progress" section header and assume the underlying user-facing capability is new — check whether the *feature* predates this fix, not just whether the *fix* is recent.** Root cause of the confusion: this doc is a chronological, append-only session log; a section titled "Fixed — X" only tells you a bug in X was recently fixed, not that X itself is new. Cross-check against the actual versioned changelog lines (`**Last released to App Store:**`) before including anything in release-facing copy.

Both items below are now resolved, closed out in the 3.3 submission (see current-version note above for details): the `.skadoodle` file-leak + oversized-background-downsample fix — root cause turned out to be a second, later-discovered gap (`bakeBgTransform()` skipping the cap), now fixed and confirmed on device — and the `joinedAt` backfill script has been run for real.
**Last released to App Store:** 2.2 (June 26, 2026 — Ready for Distribution)

**Last released to App Store:** 3.1 (submitted July 13, 2026 3:41 PM; Ready for Distribution July 14, 2026 1:34 AM — target video length for timelapse export, caption override, Edit Background shortcut, 3-finger-tap extract)

Pen Studio redesign — category tabs (Basic/Paint/Pattern/Dual Tone), 6 new pens this cycle: Airbrush, Dashed, Hearts, Chevron, Splatter, plus the Dual Tone per-style icon fix — is the only genuinely user-new material; background pinch-zoom, the Layers panel "+" position, and the `.skadoodle` file-leak/oversized-background fix are all real but under-the-hood, not release-note-worthy on their own. Also fixed: Apple Pencil couldn't instant-drag an unselected stamp on iPad.)

## In Progress — v3.2

### New Feature: Clipboard paste for background/stamp images

**Context.** Eddie asked whether the app already supported copy/paste for images (paste directly into the background or stamp picker instead of first saving to Photos) — it didn't; grepped the whole codebase for `UIPasteboard`/paste handling and found nothing. Confirmed as a real gap worth closing rather than something already built and forgotten.

**`ImagePasteButton`** (`StampTools.swift`, new top-level `View` struct, right after `PreProcessedSegmentation`) — shared control reused by both the stamp picker and the background picker. Wraps SwiftUI's system `PasteButton(supportedContentTypes: [UTType.image], payloadAction:)` rather than reading `UIPasteboard.general.image` directly — this matters, not just style: iOS 16+ shows an "Allow Paste" permission alert on any direct programmatic pasteboard read of content from another app, *except* when the read happens via the system `PasteButton` control, which is specifically exempted since the tap itself counts as consent. Reading the pasteboard directly would mean a system prompt every single paste; `PasteButton` keeps it frictionless. On tap, loads the first `NSItemProvider` as a `UIImage` and hands it back via `onPaste`. New `import UniformTypeIdentifiers` added to `StampTools.swift` for `UTType`.

- **Every call site is gated on `UIPasteboard.general.hasImages`** — the paste option simply doesn't render when there's nothing to paste, so it can never appear as a dead/non-functional control. Reading `.hasImages` itself does *not* trigger the permission-prompt behavior (only reading the actual image content does), so this check is safe to do unconditionally on every render.
- **Stamp picker** (`StampToolButton` in `StampTools.swift`) — added to both photo-add entry points: the grid's "+" cell `Menu` (alongside "Take Photo"/"Choose from Library") and the empty-state `addPhotoButton` `Menu`. A pasted image feeds into the exact same `pendingPhotos = [img]; showPhotoImportMode = true` path camera/library photos already use, so it gets the same "Extract Objects" vs. "Use Full Photo" choice afterward — no separate handling needed downstream.
- **Background picker** (`CanvasColorPickerView` in `DrawScreen.swift`) — the "+" grid cell (previously a plain `Button` that only opened the library picker) is now a `Menu` with "Choose from Library" plus the conditional paste option. `CanvasColorPickerView` gained a new `onPastePhoto: ((UIImage) -> Void)? = nil` callback (added after `onUseAsStamp`, matching parameter order exactly in both the property list and the `init` — this file has an existing documented pitfall about `GradientFrame`-style argument-order mismatches elsewhere in the codebase, so order was double-checked at the call site). The `canvasColorButton` call site wires `onPastePhoto` to mirror `ImagePickerCallback`'s completion closure exactly: `BackgroundPhotoHistory.shared.add(img)`, set `canvasBackgroundImage`, reset offset/effects, then `pendingBgHistoryIndex = 0; bgNavPath.append(0)` to jump straight to the Effects screen — same "go straight to Effects, same as tapping a thumbnail" behavior as every other new-background entry point, just without a delay since there's no intermediate picker sheet to tear down first (paste is instant, unlike a full-screen `UIImagePickerController`).

**Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this doc; this environment can't compile or run SwiftUI. Brace/paren balance checked by grep after the edits (bash sandbox mount was stale/empty this session, so this was verified via the Grep tool directly against the real files rather than a shell word-count — same result, just a different verification path). Next step: build, copy an image from Photos/Safari/Messages, confirm the Paste option appears in both pickers with no system permission prompt, and confirm a pasted background lands on the Effects screen exactly like a library pick would.

**First real-device test: two problems.** (1) Background picker's "+" cell had been turned into a `Menu` for this feature — on device that meant a single-option menu ("Choose from Library") popping up instead of jumping straight to the library, adding a tap to the single most common action in that picker for the sake of a rare one. (2) No paste option appeared in *either* picker at all, even with a real image freshly copied. **Reverted both Menu placements** — the background "+" cell is back to a plain single-tap `Button` (byte-for-byte the pre-this-feature behavior), and `ImagePasteButton` was pulled back out of both stamp-picker `Menu`s (which are back to their original two items, Take Photo / Choose from Library). **Working theory on why paste never appeared: `PasteButton` likely doesn't render reliably as a row inside SwiftUI `Menu` content** — the surrounding `if UIPasteboard.general.hasImages` should have evaluated true right after a real copy, so a silent-render failure inside the `Menu` is the more likely explanation than a logic bug. `ImagePasteButton` itself (`StampTools.swift`) is untouched and still has zero problems as a standalone control — it just needs to live somewhere that isn't a `Menu`. Eddie's explicit ask: paste should stay out of the primary tap flow entirely, since it's a rare action — **placement not yet decided, open question for next session.**

**Placement decided — split solution, since the two pickers have different constraints.**

- **Background picker:** small standalone `ImagePasteButton` badge (still the real system `PasteButton`, no permission prompt) added as a *sibling* view in a `ZStack(alignment: .bottomTrailing)` around the existing "+" `Button` — deliberately not nested inside the Button's own label/hit-testing area, per this codebase's existing rule against button-in-button nesting (see the Today tab's avatar/row tap-target precedent). Styled small (`.labelStyle(.iconOnly)`, `.buttonBorderShape(.circle)`, `.controlSize(.small)`), only rendered when `UIPasteboard.general.hasImages`. Since it's a real standalone `PasteButton` (not nested in a `Menu`), it should render correctly per the working theory above — genuinely untested until the next device pass.
- **Stamp picker:** paste added back as a literal 3rd `Menu` row (alongside Take Photo / Choose from Library, in both the grid `Menu` and the empty-state `addPhotoButton` `Menu`) — but as a **plain `Button` reading `UIPasteboard.general.image` directly**, not `PasteButton`. This guarantees it renders identically to its two sibling rows (a plain `Button` is exactly what those rows already are), at the cost of losing `PasteButton`'s permission-prompt exemption — tapping "Paste" here will trigger iOS's one-time "Allow Paste" alert. Judged an acceptable trade-off since it's an explicit menu choice the user just tapped into, not a surprise popup out of nowhere.
- Pasted images feed into the exact same downstream paths as before either way — `pendingPhotos = [img]; showPhotoImportMode = true` for stamps, `onPastePhoto?(img)` → `BackgroundPhotoHistory.shared.add` + jump to Effects for the background.
- Not yet visually confirmed on device — this is the second attempt; next real-device pass needs to confirm both the badge actually renders/works standalone and the plain-Button menu row correctly shows the system paste-permission prompt once, then pastes.

**Real root cause found via temporary `[paste-debug]` print logging, and the feature was pulled entirely as a result — not a rendering bug at all.** Added logging at every gate (`UIPasteboard.general.hasImages` read, the paste button's own tap handler) in both pickers, per Eddie's direct ask ("are you not sensing anything in the copy buffer? can we just have a log see if thats true?"). Console output on a real iPad test showed `hasImages=false` consistently, for every single render — the app genuinely never saw anything on the clipboard, which fully explains both this round's silence and the earlier Menu-rendering theory being a red herring (there was never anything to render). Eddie confirmed he copied via long-press-Copy on an image in Safari, and confirmed separately that the same copy pasted successfully into Notes — so the clipboard itself was genuinely holding valid image data; `UIPasteboard.general.hasImages` specifically was returning false for it inside Skadoodle for a reason never identified (worth another look if this is ever revisited — Safari's long-press copy may be placing something `hasImages` doesn't recognize as a plain image type, e.g. a URL or a non-standard UTI, rather than raw image data).

**Decided: not worth the continued investigation for how rarely this gets used — feature fully removed.** Eddie's call, direct: "we have another bug to get to and this is really not an issue - lets clean it out - get rid of it." Everything from this entire pass was reverted, not just the debug logging:
- `ImagePasteButton` (the shared `PasteButton`-wrapping struct) deleted from `StampTools.swift`, along with its now-unneeded `import UniformTypeIdentifiers`.
- Background picker's "+" cell (`DrawScreen.swift`) back to a plain single-tap `Button` — the `ZStack`/badge wrapper removed entirely, byte-for-byte the original pre-feature code.
- `CanvasColorPickerView`'s `onPastePhoto` callback (property, `init` parameter, and the `DrawScreen.swift` call site closure) removed.
- Both stamp-picker `Menu`s (`StampToolButton`'s grid `+` and the empty-state `addPhotoButton`) back to their original two rows, Take Photo / Choose from Library — no third Paste row.
- Confirmed clean via a repo-wide grep for `paste-debug`/`ImagePasteButton`/`onPastePhoto`/`UIPasteboard` — zero remaining references anywhere in the codebase. Brace balance re-checked on both touched files after the revert.

---

## Fixed — Background Effects pinch-zoom: live-update inconsistency + artificial zoom-out floor

Eddie reported two real bugs in the background image "Effects" screen (`BackgroundEditorView`, `DrawScreen.swift`) — the preview there can be dragged (reposition) and pinched (resize) before being applied to canvas:

1. **iPad-only inconsistency:** finishing a *drag* immediately updated the live canvas behind the sheet, but finishing a *pinch-zoom* did not — the resize only became visible after closing the Effects window. Not visible on iPhone (canvas isn't visible during editing there), but a real, jarring inconsistency on iPad.
2. **More serious:** pinch-zoom had an artificial minimum — you could zoom in freely, but zooming out was capped so the image could never be smaller than what's needed to fully fill the viewing area. Drag had no equivalent constraint (you can already drag the image so only part of it shows, with empty/canvas-colored space around it). Direct instruction: remove the pinch-zoom floor entirely so it behaves like drag — "let them zoom out so that its smaller than the canvas. thats ok."

**Root cause (issue 1):** `backgroundOffset` is a genuine `@Binding` shared between `BackgroundEditorView` and `DrawScreen`'s own `@State` — dragging writes directly into the same state the live canvas reads, so it updates instantly. The old `bgZoom`, by contrast, was a **local-only `@State`** inside `BackgroundEditorView` — pinching never touched anything outside the sheet. Zoom only ever became visible once "Done" was tapped, at which point `bakeBgTransform()` flattens zoom+offset into a new canvas-sized image and assigns it to `canvasBackgroundImage`.

**Root cause (issue 2):** the pinch gesture's `.onEnded` had a hardcoded `bgZoom = max(1.0, bgZoom * val)` — a literal "never smaller than 1:1 cover-fit" floor with no basis other than that's what felt safe when first written.

**Fixed:** `bgZoom` promoted to a proper `@Binding var backgroundZoom: CGFloat`, backed by a new `@State private var backgroundZoom: CGFloat = 1.0` on `DrawScreen` (declared right next to `backgroundOffset`, same lifecycle) — mirrors `backgroundOffset` exactly: passed into both `BackgroundEditorView(...)` call sites (the `navigationDestination` flow from the background picker, and the `.sheet(isPresented: $showBgEditor)` flow from "Edit Background"), included in `saveBgStateForCancel()`/`restoreSavedBgState()` (new `savedBgZoom` state) so Cancel correctly reverts a live pinch the same way it already reverts a live drag, and reset to `1.0` at every one of the 8 places `backgroundOffset` already gets reset to `.zero` (new background selected, color selected instead of image, both `onDone` bake handlers, Clear Background/Clear All/single-item-clear paths). The live canvas render (`DrawScreen.body`'s background image layer) now multiplies its cover-fit scale by `backgroundZoom`, so a pinch commit shows up immediately behind the sheet on iPad, exactly like a drag commit already does. The pinch gesture's floor changed from `max(1.0, ...)` to `max(0.05, ...)` — no more "must fill the canvas" constraint, just a tiny safety floor to keep the image from collapsing to zero/negative size; zooming out smaller than the viewing area is now fully allowed.

**Deliberately scoped to display only — not threaded into `CanvasSnapshot`, `SkadoodleDocument`, `renderCanvasWithStamps`, or the eraser's background-matching path.** Unlike `backgroundOffset` (which persists across save/undo/export because it's a live, ongoing transform applied every time the background is rendered anywhere), `backgroundZoom` only ever exists non-1.0 while the modal Effects sheet is open — no drawing, erasing, undo/redo, or export can happen during that window, and by the time the sheet closes (Done or Cancel) it's always back to exactly `1.0` (baked into the image's real pixels on Done, or reverted to its pre-edit saved value on Cancel). So every other subsystem that already handles `backgroundOffset` as a first-class param never needs to know zoom exists at all — it's already flattened out of existence by the time anything else touches the background.

**Confirmed on device** — Eddie has tested both the live-update fix and the removed zoom-out floor.

---

## In Progress — Pen Studio: category-tab redesign

**Context.** Eddie wants to keep adding new pens (starting with an Airbrush pen — see below), but the picker's old fixed 6-column `LazyVGrid` (`PenStudioSheet`, `DrawScreen.swift`) was already at its limit at 12 pens — icon/label size had been shrunk twice already just to keep everything crammed into one grid (documented in the grid's own code comment history), and the comment on that grid explicitly flagged the column-count math needing "re-solving every time a pen gets added." Eddie's own framing: "the u/i does not easily accomodate new ones. its kinda overloaded now." A plain horizontal scroll list was discussed and rejected — already too many items to scroll through blind at 12, let alone growing further.

**Decided: group pens into category tabs, each rendered as its own horizontal scroll row.** A new pen just gets appended to the right category's array — no grid/column math, no shrinking icons, ever again.

- **`PenCategory`** (new enum, `DrawScreen.swift`, right before `PenStudioSheet`) — `.basic`, `.texture`, `.effects`, `.dualTone`. `displayName`/`icon` drive the tab chip's label/icon.
- **`CategoryTabChip`** (new view, same file) — pill-style tab button, deliberately matching `DualToneStyleChip`'s existing visual language (same padding/corner radius/selected-fill treatment) so the new tab row looks like it belongs next to the sub-picker it sits above.
- **`PenStudioSheet`** — the old `allPens: [PenType]` flat array + single `LazyVGrid` replaced with `penCategories: [PenCategory: [PenType]]` (Basic: Pencil/Ink/Brush/Marker; Texture: Chalk/Neon/Spray/Watercolor/Dotted; Effects: Calligraphy/Confetti) + a `categoryOrder` array controlling tab display order (dictionaries have no stable order of their own). Dual Tone is deliberately *not* in the dict — it's its own branch in `body` since it already has its own dedicated sub-picker UI (the existing `DualToneStyle` chip row + second-color picker), now relocated into a new `dualToneContent` computed view instead of always rendering below the grid.
- **New `@State private var selectedCategory: PenCategory`** — tapping a category tab switches which horizontal row of `PenTypeCard`s is shown (or swaps in `dualToneContent` for the Dual Tone tab). Tapping the Dual Tone tab also immediately sets `penType = .dualTone(selectedDualStyle)`, matching how tapping the old grid's single "Dual Tone" card used to select the pen — the tab itself doubles as the pen selection for that one case, same as before.
- **`categoryFor(_:)`** — new helper, called from `.onAppear`, so reopening Pen Studio lands on whichever tab your *current* pen actually belongs to (e.g. currently on Watercolor → opens straight to the Texture tab) instead of always defaulting to Basic.
- **`PenTypeCard` enlarged** — was sized for 12 cards crammed into 6 columns (56pt icon box, 22pt icon, 10pt label with `minimumScaleFactor`). Now only ~4-5 cards are visible at once per category, so it's sized up (72pt icon box, 28pt icon, 12pt label) with a fixed `78pt` card width so row spacing stays consistent regardless of label length ("Watercolor" vs "Ink").
- **`.presentationDetents` re-tuned** — the old two-detent scheme (keyed on `penType.isDualTone`) is now keyed on `selectedCategory == .dualTone`, with both values reduced from their old grid-era sizes (427→300 / 643→480 on iPad, 0.57→0.4 / 0.83→0.62 fraction on iPhone) since a single horizontal card row is much shorter than the old multi-row grid, and even the Dual Tone tab's content is now shorter (no grid sitting above the sub-picker anymore). These are estimates, not measured against a real render.

Backup made first: `DrawScreen.swift.bak` (plain copy, non-`.swift` extension, same convention as prior backups this project) sits alongside the live file as a restore point, per Eddie's direct request before this redesign began.

**Bug found on first device look: non-Dual-Tone tabs (Basic/Texture/Effects) had the sheet's compact `.presentationDetents` height set too short, clipping `PenPreviewStrip` at the bottom.** The 300pt (iPad) / 0.4 fraction (iPhone) estimate from the initial build didn't leave enough room once the category tab row + a full card row + the preview strip were all stacked — confirmed cut off on a real device, not just a theoretical concern. **Fixed:** bumped to 400pt (iPad) / 0.52 fraction (iPhone) for the non-Dual-Tone case; the Dual Tone case (480pt / 0.62) was already reading fine and left untouched.

**Airbrush pen built and wired into the new Effects tab.** `PenType.airbrush` (`DrawingEngine.swift`) — same drag-to-build-coverage feel as Spray (denser where you move slower/linger), but lays down soft, feathered blobs instead of many small hard-edged dots. `drawAirbrushLine` reuses Spray's speed-based density logic (`drawSprayLine`, same file). Icon: originally `aqi.low` (paired with Spray's `aqi.medium`, both from the same SF Symbol family) — reported as reading too similar to Spray's icon at a glance, so switched to `wind`, visually distinct while still reading as "air." Naming: Eddie confirmed **"Airbrush,"** not "Blur." Wired into the same 9 touch points Calligraphy/Confetti established: `PenType.displayName`/`.icon`, `renderLine`'s switch, `DoodleFormat.swift` encode+decode, `DrawScreen.swift`'s `penCategories` (added to the Effects array, alongside Calligraphy/Confetti) + `penTypesMatch` + the persisted-last-pen-type restore switch, and `CustomStampViews.swift`'s separate persisted-pen-type restore switch for the doodle stamp canvas — confirmed via grep, all 9 present.

**Confirmed on device: "fantastic... sorely missing" — but real perf report: Airbrush (and "some sim[ilar] ones") slow the app down noticeably the more you use them.** Root cause: the first version drew every blob inside one `context.drawLayer { layer.addFilter(.blur(radius:)) }` scope per stroke, the same technique Trim already uses. That's fine for Trim (only 2 continuous strokes go into the layer), but wrong for Airbrush — a single stroke can pack hundreds of blobs into one layer, and `DrawingLayerCanvas` re-runs every past line's render function on *every* canvas redraw (e.g. every touch-move while drawing something else entirely on the same layer). An expensive off-screen Gaussian blur pass over a huge multi-hundred-shape layer, repeated every frame, for every airbrush stroke ever drawn, is what was compounding into real slowdown — not a one-time cost, a per-frame one that gets worse the more airbrush content exists.

**Fixed:** rebuilt `drawAirbrushLine` to draw each blob as a `.radialGradient` fill (opaque center fading to transparent edge) directly onto the context instead of inside a blurred layer — a native GPU shading primitive, not an off-screen blur filter, so the soft edge is "free" per blob rather than one expensive whole-layer post-process that has to re-run every redraw. `context.drawLayer`/`.addFilter(.blur(...))` removed from this pen entirely. Blob count per segment also eased back (was up to 6, now up to 4) as extra headroom, with blob radius/opacity bumped up slightly to keep visual coverage from thinning out as a result. **Checked whether Trim needs the same fix — decided not yet:** Trim is the only other pen using a blur filter, but its layer only ever contains 2 continuous stroke paths per Trim stroke (not per-segment blobs), so its blur pass is over far simpler content and much cheaper per redraw than Airbrush's was. Left untouched for now; flagged to Eddie in case he's also noticing lag specifically from Trim/Tube and not just Airbrush, since "some sim ones" was non-specific.

**Confirmed on device: category tabs, Dual Tone sub-picker, and the re-tuned detent heights all read well — "they all look great."** Eddie also specifically checked Trim and Tube for the same kind of slowdown Airbrush had (since Trim is the only other blur-filter pen) — both confirmed fine, no lag. This closes out the open question from the perf-fix writeup above; nothing else in the current pen roster needs a look for this specific issue. The radial-gradient rewrite of Airbrush itself (the actual perf fix) has since been confirmed working on device too.

**Category groupings revisited — the original Basic/Texture/Effects split had two genuine mis-categorizations.** Eddie's framing: the whole point of tabs is finding a pen "asap," and while Basic (Pencil/Ink/Brush/Marker) read as an obviously coherent group, Texture and Effects didn't. On inspection: Neon was sitting in Texture despite being a glow *effect*, not a simulated physical media, and Airbrush had landed in Effects despite being a fill/texture tool (Spray's actual sibling, not Confetti's). **Regrouped** (`penCategories`, `PenStudioSheet`, `DrawScreen.swift`): Texture is now `[.chalk, .watercolor, .spray, .dotted, .airbrush]` — tools that simulate a physical media/fill quality, good for "coloring in." Effects is now `[.neon, .calligraphy, .confetti]` — stylized/decorative pens that don't simulate a real material. Basic left untouched. Each category now reads as one clear mental bucket: plain pens, fill/texture pens, special-look pens.

**Dual Tone pen button showed a generic magic wand regardless of which of the 12 sub-styles was actually selected — fixed to show the specific style's own icon.** Eddie's direct flag: "that's not the dual tone icon... we need a finer icon... more precise... like the type of dual type." Root cause: `PenType.icon`'s `.dualTone` case returned a hardcoded `"wand.and.stars"` for every sub-style, while the *real* per-style icons (Braid → link, Trim → three lines, Tube → cylinder, etc.) only existed inside `DualToneStyleChip`'s own local `icon` computed property — nothing tied the two together. **Fixed:** promoted that icon mapping onto `DualToneStyle` itself (`DrawingEngine.swift`) as a real `var icon: String` — the single source of truth now. `DualToneStyleChip.icon` (`DrawScreen.swift`) reduced to `style.icon`, and `PenType.icon`'s `.dualTone(let style)` case now returns `style.icon` instead of the hardcoded wand. The main toolbar pen button (`currentPenType.icon`, `DrawScreen.swift`) now shows whichever specific sub-style is active — picking Braid shows the link icon, picking Tube shows the cylinder icon, etc. — instead of one indistinguishable wand for all twelve. `PenCategory.dualTone`'s own tab icon (`circle.righthalf.filled`, representing the *category* rather than any one style) was deliberately left alone — different purpose, still correct as a generic dual/split icon for the tab itself.

**Categories renamed and regrouped a second time — Texture/Effects replaced outright with Basic/Paint/Pattern, per Eddie's own explicit list, not another internal judgment call.** Even after the Texture/Effects fix above, Eddie still didn't like the split ("i still dont like the groupings") and this time specified the replacement categories and their exact contents by name rather than asking for another guess: **Basic** = Pencil, Ink, Marker, Chalk, Calligraphy (Neon added afterward, see below); **Paint** = Brush, Watercolor, Spray, Airbrush; **Pattern** = Dotted, Confetti, plus new pens to fill it out. Cross-checking the list against the full 12-pen non-dual-tone roster caught one real omission — Neon wasn't mentioned anywhere in the new scheme — flagged directly rather than silently guessing where it should land; Eddie's answer: "you can put neon in basic." Also confirmed explicit indifference to the resulting row length: Basic now has 6 items (won't fit in one screen width without scrolling) — "will it have to scroll? fine if it does." Dual Tone is unchanged, still its own dedicated branch.

**Three new pens built specifically to round out Pattern:** Eddie asked for "1 or 2 more for pattern... how about dashed? any others?", settled on three after a follow-up ("for pattern we have dashed, hearts, chevron... and dont forget confetti"). All three added to `DrawingEngine.swift` as new `PenType` cases and wired through the same 9 touch points established by Calligraphy/Confetti/Airbrush (`PenType.displayName`/`.icon`, `renderLine`'s switch, `DoodleFormat.swift` encode+decode, `DrawScreen.swift`'s `penCategories`+`penTypesMatch`+restore-switch, `CustomStampViews.swift`'s restore-switch) — confirmed via grep, all 9 present for each.
- **Dashed** (`drawDashedLine`) — the simplest of the three: a single path through all points, stroked with SwiftUI's native `StrokeStyle(dash:)` rather than any hand-rolled gap logic. Dash/gap lengths scale off the pen's line width (`baseW * 1.4` / `baseW * 1.1`) so thicker strokes get proportionally longer dashes instead of looking finer-toothed as width increases.
- **Hearts** (`heartPath`/`drawHeartsLine`) — small rotated hearts placed at even arc-length spacing along the stroke (same running-arc-length/`nextAt` convention as Dotted/Bubble/Stars), each a closed `Path` traced from the classic parametric heart curve `x = 16sin³t, y = -(13cos t - 5cos 2t - 2cos 3t - cos 4t)`. **Verified visually before writing the Swift version** — rendered the formula in a matplotlib script in the bash sandbox first and looked at the actual PNG, rather than trusting hand-typed bezier/arc control points for a shape that's easy to get subtly wrong (lopsided lobes, wrong point at the bottom, etc.). Slight per-heart rotation jitter uses the same sin-hash deterministic pseudo-randomness as Hairy/Thorns/Confetti (stable across redraws, not true random).
- **Chevron** (`drawChevronLine`) — small ">"-shaped marks (open V, not filled) at even arc-length spacing, each oriented to the local stroke direction using the same wider `points[i-1]`-to-`points[i+1]` sampling window as Braid/Hairy/Thorns/Trim (avoids raw-adjacent-point jitter in the angle).
- All three respect pressure via the existing `pressureAt(_:in:)` helper, same as every other pressure-sensitive pen in the file.

**`PenCategory` itself renamed to match** (`DrawScreen.swift`): `.texture` → `.paint`, `.effects` → `.pattern`, with new tab icons (`paintpalette` for Paint, `square.grid.2x2` for Pattern — Basic's `pencil` and Dual Tone's `circle.righthalf.filled` unchanged). Final `penCategories`/`categoryOrder`: **Basic** = `[.pencil, .ink, .marker, .chalk, .calligraphy, .neon]`, **Paint** = `[.brush, .watercolor, .spray, .airbrush]`, **Pattern** = `[.dotted, .confetti, .dashed, .hearts, .chevron]`, order `[.basic, .paint, .pattern, .dualTone]`.

**Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this doc. Brace/paren balance verified clean after this round (`DrawingEngine.swift` 438/438 braces, 1578/1578 parens; `DoodleFormat.swift` 42/42 braces, 198/198 parens; `DrawScreen.swift` 1143/1143 braces, 2477/2477 parens; `CustomStampViews.swift` 233/233 braces, 545/545 parens). Next step: confirm the Basic/Paint/Pattern groupings actually feel scannable in practice (including that Basic's 6-item row scrolls acceptably), and look at all three new pens (dash spacing/weight, heart shape/rotation, chevron orientation-to-stroke) on a real canvas.

**Confirmed on device: "pens are awesome... grouping will make it much easier to find what youre looking for."** Basic and Paint both confirmed feature-complete as-is ("cant think of any others" for both). For Pattern, one more idea was floated and built: an emoji/stamp-as-pen concept was discussed and explicitly rejected by Eddie before any code was written ("i fear the trouble to implement isnt worth it... a pen that may rarely get used") — not built, not documented further per his own "dont even mention it," noted here only as the one immediate precedent for why the bar for new pens stays "worth the UI complexity."

**Splatter — a 4th Pattern pen, added same session.** Eddie's ask: something spray/airbrush-like but that lays down multiple different colors as you draw, for Pattern rather than Paint (Pattern is about color/shape variety, not simulating a fill medium). `PenType.splatter` (`DrawingEngine.swift`) — `drawSplatterLine` is a near-exact structural copy of `drawSprayLine` (same speed-based per-segment density, same seeded-hash dot placement/size/opacity formulas), so it inherits Spray's already-tuned "denser where you move slower/linger" feel for free. The one real difference: each dot's color is picked from the same 4-way variant set Confetti already established (`line.color`, `line.colorB`, and a lightened blend of each via the existing `blendColors` helper) — reusing Confetti's exact color palette convention rather than inventing a new one, so "the two colors picked in Pen Studio" means the same thing across every multi-color pen in the app. Unlike Confetti's fixed sin-hash 0-1-2-3 cycle, the color pick here comes from unused high bits (48-64) of Spray's own per-dot hash (bits 0-48 are already spoken for by angle/radius/dotR/opacity) — so color varies dot-to-dot within a single burst rather than in a repeating sequence, reading as genuinely scattered rather than a stripe pattern. Icon: `burst.fill` (checked against every other pen icon in the file first — no collision). Wired into the same 9 touch points as every pen this session: `PenType.displayName`/`.icon`, `renderLine`'s switch, `DoodleFormat.swift` encode+decode, `DrawScreen.swift`'s `penCategories` (added to Pattern, alongside Dotted/Confetti/Dashed/Hearts/Chevron) + `penTypesMatch` + the restore switch, and `CustomStampViews.swift`'s restore switch — confirmed via grep, all 9 present. Brace/paren balance verified clean (`DrawingEngine.swift` 446/446 braces, 1624/1624 parens; `DoodleFormat.swift` 42/42 braces, 199/199 parens; `DrawScreen.swift` 1143/1143 braces, 2478/2478 parens; `CustomStampViews.swift` 233/233 braces, 545/545 parens). Final Pattern roster: `[.dotted, .confetti, .dashed, .hearts, .chevron, .splatter]`.

**Confirmed on device: "splatter is perfect. all great."** Closes out the Pen Studio redesign for this cycle — Basic, Paint, and Pattern (including Splatter) are all confirmed feature-complete as-is; Eddie couldn't think of anything else to add to Basic or Paint, and Pattern's only other floated idea (emoji/stamp-as-pen) was explicitly rejected before being built (see above). Pen Studio work for v3.2 is done.

---

## Fixed — Apple Pencil couldn't instant-drag an unselected stamp on iPad

Eddie reported, on iPad, with the toolbar in stamp mode (not draw mode): a finger placed on an unselected photo stamp drags it immediately, no selection needed — but Apple Pencil does nothing on that same unselected stamp. The only way Pencil could move a stamp at all was to first select it (get the snug rect), then drag. Finger never needed that extra step.

**Root cause:** every window-level UIKit gesture recognizer in `WindowPinchView` (`DrawScreen.swift`) — pinch, rotation, long press, tap, double tap, three-finger tap, background pan, and `stampPanRecognizer` (the one that gives finger its instant-drag-without-selecting behavior) — shares one `gestureRecognizer(_:shouldReceive:)` delegate method, and that method unconditionally rejected any `.pencil`/`.stylus` touch before it ever reached a single one of them. That blanket rule exists for a good reason on every *other* recognizer: it keeps a real pencil stroke from ever being hijacked mid-draw by pinch/rotation/pan. But it applied to `stampPanRecognizer` too, even though that recognizer only ever activates in stamp mode — where `drawingEnabled` is already false and there's nothing for the pencil to be drawing anyway. So Pencil was locked out of the one recognizer that would have let it behave like a finger, for no actual drawing-protection benefit. Tap-to-select still worked with Pencil because that's a separate SwiftUI `SpatialTapGesture` on the canvas itself, never routed through this UIKit delegate at all — which is why "only works once selected" was the exact symptom.

**Fixed:** `shouldReceive touch:` now special-cases `stampPanRecognizer` — a pencil/stylus touch is allowed through for that one recognizer, rejected for every other one exactly as before. `gestureRecognizerShouldBegin` already independently gates `stampPanRecognizer` on `parent.isStampMode` plus an actual stamp hit under the touch, so this change can't leak into draw mode: in draw mode the recognizer still never begins, pencil touch or not, so normal pencil drawing is untouched. In stamp mode, Pencil now gets the identical instant-drag-on-touch behavior finger already had.

**Confirmed on device: "never worked this perfectly... was always a bit flakey with the pen."** Direct confirmation this fully resolves the long-standing inconsistency, not just the specific unselected-stamp case originally reported.

---

## In Progress — Daily Doodle Feature (not yet built/submitted)

Replaces the old Calendar tab with a **Today** tab (`TodayTab.swift`, new file). This is meant to become the flashiest part of the app — a daily drawing prompt everyone competes on, with a celebration moment for whoever's on top. Currently mid-implementation: functionality first, visual polish ("skin") later — Eddie's explicit call.

### Concept
- Every day (in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`) has one shared prompt (`DailyPrompt.today`, picked deterministically by day-of-year so all users see the same word).
- **Day boundary is anchored to America/New_York, not UTC.** Originally implemented as UTC; switched deliberately (skadoodle.nyc, and most current users are US-based). A single global synchronized cutoff is required either way — the blind-submission/timed-reveal/voting-window mechanic can't work with a per-user-local rollover (unlike, say, Wordle, which has no such requirement and rolls over at each player's own local midnight). `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone` (`TimeZone(identifier: "America/New_York")`) is the single source of truth for this; `TimeZone` handles the EST/EDT shift automatically, no manual DST logic needed. `DailyEntry.contestDateString(for:)` (was `utcDateString`) is the one function everything hangs off of — never format/parse a `daily_gallery` `date` string with any other time zone (see the "past winners showed the wrong dates" bug below for what happens when parse/display time zones drift apart).
- Each user can post one entry per day to `daily_gallery` (doc id `"{YYYY-MM-DD}_{userId}"`, using the contest-day string above, so posting again with a different image just replaces/overwrites your own entry — no duplicates).
- **Today's contest is blind.** While a day is still in progress, nobody — not even the poster — sees anyone else's entries. You only ever see your own (if you've posted) plus the prompt.
- Once a day rolls over (midnight in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`, matching `DailyEntry.contestDateString()`), it's "concluded": all of yesterday's entries become visible, sorted by votes, with the top entry called out as the winner.
- **Terminology: "votes," not "likes."** Deliberately named and coded differently from World Gallery's "likes" (separate field, separate subcollection, separate Swift identifiers — `votes`/`isVotedByMe`/`toggleVote` vs. World Gallery's `likes`/`isLikedByMe`/`toggleLike`) so the two systems can never be confused for each other in code — and now in icon too, since every vote display uses `checkmark.seal` instead of a heart (see "Heart icon → checkmark.seal" under the Today tab redesign notes below; this was flagged here as deferred and has since been fixed). **Renamed from `likes` mid-build** — any hand-edited test docs in the console from before this rename still have a `likes` field, which the app now ignores (`d["votes"] as? Int ?? 0` reads 0 for them); redo test data under the `votes` field name (and a `votes` subcollection, not `likes`) going forward.

#### Submission / voting window model (confirmed design, no extra code needed — this already falls out of the current implementation)
Two 24-hour windows are always running at once, offset by one day, e.g. (all times in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone` / America/New_York):
- **July 4, 00:00–24:00** — submission window for July 4 is open. Entries are blind (nobody sees anyone else's).
- **July 5, 00:00** — July 4 submissions close and July 4 voting opens, at the exact same instant July 5 submissions open. This is the "reveal": July 4's entries all become visible together, sorted, winner spotlighted.
- **July 5, 00:00–24:00** — July 4 is votable (it's "yesterday" relative to "today" = July 5). Simultaneously, July 5 submissions are being collected blind, same as July 4 was.
- **July 6, 00:00** — July 4 ages out: `fetchYesterday()`'s `date == today - 1` query no longer includes it, so it silently becomes unreachable in the UI. July 5 voting opens (the new "yesterday"). July 6 submissions open.

So voting is never literally "closed" by an explicit flag — it stops being possible because the query window moves on and the entry is no longer fetched. This is functionally identical to a hard 24-hour voting window today, **but it's a side effect of there being no archive feature yet, not an enforced rule.** Two follow-ups this implies for later:
- **Now that the "browse further back than yesterday" archive is built** (`PastWinnersView`/`DailyContestDayView`, see below), voting on older days is blocked client-side: `toggleVote(_:)` checks `entry.date` against `currentVotableDate` (`"yesterday"` relative to now) and no-ops (returns `false`, logs a warning) if they don't match; `DailyEntryDetailSheet`'s `canVote` computed property hides the Vote button entirely for non-votable days and shows a static "Voting has closed for this day" count instead. Still client-side only — a Firestore security rule rejecting `votes` subcollection writes outside the allowed window is the real, un-bypassable version, and is the same deferred bucket as the blind-submission read rule below.
- **This same fix doubles as the permanent winner record.** Once voting on expired days is actually blocked (either way above), every past day's `votes` count freezes the moment it ages out — the `daily_gallery` docs themselves become the durable historical record, no separate snapshot doc needed.
- **Known minor edge case, deferred:** no automatic midnight-rollover refresh exists. If the Today tab is left open straight through a day boundary without backgrounding/reopening/pulling to refresh, it can keep showing (and allow voting against) stale in-memory data from the now-expired day until the next fetch. Low priority — we'll notice if it happens and can add a "this contest has ended, pull to refresh" message at that point rather than solving it preemptively.

#### Scalability: composite Firestore index required
`fetchYesterday()` and `fetchEntries(for:)` sort server-side (`.whereField("date", isEqualTo:).order(by: "votes", descending: true).order(by: "timestamp")`) instead of fetching a flat batch and sorting client-side, so a single day doesn't silently truncate once it gets more than ~200 entries. `fetchPastWinners()` uses the *same* index with a range filter on `date` instead of equality (see below). This requires a composite index on `daily_gallery`:
- Fields: `date` (Ascending), `votes` (Descending), `timestamp` (Ascending)
- **Created and confirmed working** (console-managed, same as the existing `world_gallery` indexes documented below — this repo has no `firestore.indexes.json`). Created manually via Firestore Console → Indexes → Composite → Add Index, since the "requires an index" error link Firestore throws in Xcode's console doesn't actually create the index by itself — you still have to click Create on the pre-filled form it opens, or add it manually as above.

#### Past Winners archive — one range query, no summary collection needed
`DailyManager.fetchPastWinners(lookbackDays:)` populates the whole archive list with a **single** Firestore query, not one query per day and not a separate denormalized collection:
```
.whereField("date", isGreaterThanOrEqualTo: earliest)
.whereField("date", isLessThanOrEqualTo: anchor)      // anchor = 2 days ago
.order(by: "date").order(by: "votes", descending: true).order(by: "timestamp")
```
Same composite index as above, just a range instead of an equality filter on `date`. Because results are sorted by date first and votes-descending second, every date's highest-voted entry is guaranteed to be the *first* one encountered in that date's group — so a single client-side pass (`winnerByDate[entry.date] == winnerByDate[entry.date] ?? entry`, first-write-wins) pulls out one winner per day, plus a per-day entry count, with no GROUP BY needed (Firestore doesn't have one) and no extra collection to keep in sync. The trade-off: this fetches every entry in the date range, not just winners — fine at this app's scale, would only be worth revisiting (a real `daily_summaries` collection) if a single day routinely got hundreds of entries. Starts 2 days ago rather than yesterday, since yesterday already has its own dedicated section higher up on the Today tab. Fixed lookback window (default 60 days) rather than paginated — revisit if history ever outgrows it. Days where nobody voted for anything are omitted from the list entirely (same zero-engagement rule as `yesterdayWinner`).

### Current implementation
- **`DailyEntry`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) — model for one `daily_gallery` doc. `contestDateString(for:)` / `docId(date:userId:)` are the two static helpers everything hangs off of. `username`/`avatar`/`photoURL` are **not** stored on the Firestore doc and not read by `parse()` — they're defaulted fields resolved live after fetch via `applyProfile(_:)` / `DailyManager.resolveProfiles(for:completion:)` (batched through the existing `UserProfileManager.fetchProfiles`), mirroring `WorldSnoodle.applyProfile`. This was a deliberate fix: the original implementation denormalized username/avatar/photoURL onto the doc at submission time, so a user changing their name or photo later would leave every past `daily_gallery` entry showing stale info forever. `post()` only ever writes `userId`, `date`, `imageURL`, `caption`, `timestamp`, `votes` — never profile fields. `caption` is always `DailyPrompt.today` at post time (`TodayTab.postEntry()`), never the source private-gallery entry's own AI-generated caption — Daily Doodle entries are labeled by the theme they're answering, not by whatever Vision/Gemini captioned the original doodle.
- **`DailyPrompt`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) — static list of 40 prompts, `today` picks by day-of-year (in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`) mod count. Only ever used now as the **fallback** value inside `DailyManager.todaySubject` (see below) — no other call site should reference `DailyPrompt.today` directly anymore. **Known limitation of the mod-cycle formula itself:** repeats every 40 days guaranteed, and because it's computed live from `dayOfYear % prompts.count`, growing the array shifts every future date's assignment from that point on — you can't pin a specific subject to a specific future date (e.g. "Turkey" near Thanksgiving) without the formula reshuffling every day after it. This is the actual reason the fix has to be an explicit stored per-date assignment, not just a bigger array.
- **`DailyManager.todaySubject` / `fetchTodaySubject()`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) — first step of moving subjects server-side. New Firestore collection `daily_prompts`, one doc per calendar date (doc ID = the same `contestDateString` used everywhere, field `subject: String`) — an explicit stored mapping, not a formula, so adding to the pool later never disturbs a date that's already been assigned. `todaySubject` is `@Published`, initialized synchronously to the legacy `DailyPrompt.today` fallback so it's never blank, then `fetchTodaySubject()` checks a same-day UserDefaults cache first (the assignment for a given date never changes once fetched, so no need to re-hit Firestore on every tab switch), then reads `daily_prompts/{date}` and silently upgrades to the real value if that doc exists — falls back to the local mod-cycle if it doesn't (e.g. before any admin tooling exists, or a gap day nobody's assigned yet). Called defensively from both `TodayTab`'s `.onAppear`/`.refreshable` and `DrawScreen`'s `.onAppear`, so it's virtually always resolved before it's actually needed for a post's caption. All four places that used to read `DailyPrompt.today` directly (`TodayTab.promptCard`, `TodayTab.postEntry()`, `DrawScreen.saveResult()`, `DrawScreen`'s canvas `.navigationTitle`) now read `daily.todaySubject` instead.
  - **The UserDefaults cache is only written on a real Firestore-sourced assignment, never on the fallback.** If it cached the fallback too, seeding `daily_prompts/{date}` by hand mid-day — the current workflow, decided against building the admin panel for now (see below) — would never show up on a device that had already fetched today once; it'd be stuck on the fallback until the date rolled over. Leaving fallback days uncached costs one extra cheap Firestore read per app open on any date nobody's seeded yet, which is a fine trade.
  - **Decided: no website admin panel for now.** Bulk-seeding happens via a DEBUG-only in-app tool instead (see `SettingsTab.seedDailyPromptsIfDebug()` below); one-off manual edits/overrides for a single date can still be done by hand via Firebase Console the same way as `daily_gallery` test data — collection `daily_prompts`, doc ID `YYYY-MM-DD` (the same `contestDateString`, America/New_York), fields `subject: String` and `category: String`. Every date without a doc silently falls back to the old local list — no regression, just no growth until seeded. **Confirmed design for whenever the website admin panel does get built:** pool + auto-fill, not a fully hand-picked calendar — Eddie wants the day-to-day assignment random/unplanned ("let it surprise me as well as others"), with manual override only for specific dates that matter (e.g. a holiday). `category` was added to the schema now specifically so it's there for that future UI to group/filter the pool by — nothing in the app reads `category` today. Still needs, whenever it's picked back up: a **website admin panel** (separate repo, `skadoodle-website`, not connected to this workspace) gated by real Firestore security rules restricting writes to `daily_prompts` (and whatever pool/tracking collection backs it) to a specific authenticated admin UID — not just a client-side hidden page, since anyone could otherwise write directly to Firestore.
  - **`SettingsTab.seedDailyPromptsIfDebug()` (DEBUG-only)** — new "📝 Daily Subjects" section in Settings' debug tools. `debugSeedSubjects` is a hardcoded 102-item `[(subject, category)]` list (the original 40 from `DailyPrompt.prompts`, plus 62 newly drafted, across 8 categories: Animals & Creatures, Fantasy & Magic, Space & Sci-Fi, Everyday & Whimsical, Vehicles, Places, Characters & Occupations, Food & Treats — no duplicates, checked programmatically). Tapping "Seed daily_prompts now" reads the whole `daily_prompts` collection first, walks forward day-by-day from today (up to a 400-day horizon) collecting dates that don't have a doc yet, shuffles `debugSeedSubjects` for randomness, and batch-writes one subject per empty date — **never overwrites an already-assigned date**, so it's always safe to re-run after adding more subjects to the list (new entries just continue filling the calendar forward from wherever it left off). This is meant to be edited directly in code (add/remove tuples in `debugSeedSubjects`) rather than through any UI — the "manual process of coming up with more" Eddie flagged is genuinely just editing this Swift array and re-tapping the button.
  - **`scripts/seed-daily-prompts.js` (new, standalone Node script, not part of the app target) — the "I just don't like this pool anymore" tool.** Built after Eddie decided the existing 102-item pool needed a real do-over ("sandwich"?!"), not just a top-up — and the in-app debug seeder's core safety property (never overwrites an already-assigned date) is exactly wrong for that job. This script does the opposite on purpose: reads a plain text file (one subject per line, optional `| Category` suffix), shuffles it, and **overwrites** every date from tomorrow through a configurable horizon (`--days`, default 400, matching the in-app seeder's default), cycling/reshuffling if the list is shorter than the horizon. Safe to overwrite the whole future because nothing in the app ever fetches or displays a date's subject before it's "today" or "yesterday" (see `todaySubject`/`yesterdaySubject` above) — no user has ever seen a future assignment, so changing it can't retroactively contradict what anyone's already seen. Today's own doc and everything in the past are explicitly never touched (loop starts at tomorrow, plus a defensive `dateStr <= todayStr` skip). Supports `--dry-run` to preview the first 10 assignments with no writes. Requires a Firebase service-account key (Console → Project Settings → Service Accounts → generate new private key) — deliberately kept **outside** git (`scripts/*service-account*.json` and `scripts/node_modules/` added to `.gitignore`) since it's a full-admin credential, same treatment as the existing `GoogleService-Info.plist`/`Secrets.swift` entries in that section. This is explicitly a stopgap, not a replacement for the "Decided: no website admin panel for now" call above — it's a local terminal tool for Eddie only, not multi-user, not gated by any UI/auth beyond possessing the service-account key file. If/when the real website admin panel gets built, this script's core logic (parse pool → shuffle → assign forward from tomorrow, never touch today/past) is the same logic that panel would need server-side anyway.
- **`DailyManager`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`, singleton) —
  - `fetchMyEntryToday()` — fetches **only** the signed-in user's own doc for today by known `docId` (a direct `document(docId).getDocument`, not a collection query). This is the privacy mechanism for "blind" submissions: the client never requests other users' entries for an in-progress day in the first place, rather than fetching-then-hiding them in the UI. (Real enforcement would also need Firestore security rules restricting reads on today's docs to their owner — not yet configured; client-side omission is the current safeguard.)
  - `fetchYesterday()` — thin wrapper around `fetchEntries(for:)` (below) for the specific date "yesterday"; the only place that writes to `yesterdayEntries`, the one published property for "yesterday" specifically (not any arbitrary day). **Blind-reveal voting (confirmed design, changed mid-build):** originally this also computed a live `yesterdayWinner` and displayed vote counts during the active voting window — like Wordle showing everyone's guess distribution live. Changed deliberately, closer to how political voting works: results stay sealed until the window closes, not a live leaderboard that invites bandwagon voting and gives away the ending before the actual reveal. `fetchYesterday()` now discards the query's vote-sorted order and re-sorts the fetched entries by `timestamp` before publishing — display order itself would leak ranking even without printing a number, since first-in-list reads as "winning." No winner is computed or shown anywhere during this window; that only happens once the day ages out into the Past Winners archive, which is fully revealed (see below).
  - `fetchEntries(for date:completion:)` — the shared single-day fetch: queries `daily_gallery` where `date == <date>`, sorted server-side by `votes` descending then `timestamp` ascending (tiebreaker — earliest submission wins a tie), resolves each entry's `isVotedByMe` via `fetchVotedIds(for:)` (batched subcollection existence check — mirrors `WorldGalleryManager.fetchLikedIds`). Used by both `fetchYesterday()` and `DailyContestDayView` (archive drill-in) — same query shape, just a different date string and a completion closure instead of publishing to instance state. Requires a composite index — see below.
  - `fetchPastWinners(lookbackDays:completion:)` — populates the Past Winners archive list. See "Past Winners archive" above for how one range query does this without per-day queries or a summary collection.
  - `post(imageData:caption:completion:)` — uploads to Storage at `daily_gallery/{docId}.jpg`, then `setData` (merge-free overwrite) to the Firestore doc with only `userId`/`date`/`imageURL`/`caption`/`timestamp`/`votes: 0` — no profile fields (see `DailyEntry` note above). Re-posting the same day just calls this again with the same `docId`, replacing the old entry. Repeat submissions of the same doodle across different days are fine — each day's doc starts fresh at `votes: 0`, no accumulation carries over.
  - `resolveProfiles(for:completion:)` — resolves `username`/`avatar`/`photoURL` for a batch of entries via `UserProfileManager.shared.fetchProfiles(userIds:completion:)` (batched, cached), then `applyProfile(_:)` onto each entry. Called from `fetchMyEntryToday()`, `fetchEntries(for:)`, and `fetchPastWinners()` — every read path — before publishing/returning results.
  - `fetchTodaySubmissionCount()` / `todaySubmissionCount` — a Firestore **count aggregation query** (`.count.getAggregation(source: .server)`), never a document fetch, so it preserves the same blind-submission privacy guarantee as `fetchMyEntryToday()`: a raw number can't reveal who's posted or what they drew. Bumped optimistically by 1 in `post()`'s completion when `myEntryToday` was nil beforehand (so replacing an existing entry doesn't double-count), and decremented in `withdrawToday()`'s completion. Displayed in `TodayTab.promptCard`.
  - `yesterdayTotalVotes` — computed property, `yesterdayEntries.reduce(0) { $0 + $1.votes }`. No extra query — `yesterdayEntries` is already fully fetched (see `fetchYesterday()` above), just not displayed per-entry. **Does not violate blind-reveal**: a single combined total can't be used to infer which entry is leading, unlike a per-entry tally or vote-sorted list order — the same distinction as an election turnout counter vs. live per-candidate results. Displayed in `TodayTab.yesterdaySection`'s header alongside the existing entry count ("8 entries · 42 votes cast").
  - `yesterdayUniqueVoterCount` / `fetchUniqueVoterCount(for:)` — **distinct people who voted, not total votes cast** — a deliberately different number from `yesterdayTotalVotes`, since voting is unlimited (one person can vote for several entries, so vote count and voter count diverge). Reads every one of yesterday's entries' `votes` subcollections in full (not just an existence check for one uid, unlike `fetchVotedIds`) and unions the doc IDs (each is a voter's uid) into a `Set`. Bounded by entry count × votes-per-entry — fine at current scale, would need a `collectionGroup` query instead if a single day's entry/vote count ever got large. Called automatically at the end of `fetchYesterday()`.
  - `totalUserCount` / `fetchTotalUserCount()` — count aggregation query on `users`. Denominator for `yesterdayVoterTurnoutPercent` (`yesterdayUniqueVoterCount / totalUserCount`, rounded). **Deliberately a soft/shifting denominator** — includes every account ever created (inactive/test/phantom accounts included) and grows as people sign up, so the percentage is shown alongside the raw voter count rather than replacing it ("6 of 40 users voted (15%)"), not as a standalone number.
  - `withdrawToday(completion:)` — deletes the signed-in user's own today-doc (derived from current uid + today's date, never from whatever's cached in `myEntryToday`) plus a best-effort Storage image cleanup, then sets `myEntryToday = nil`. Safe as a clean delete since today's entry is guaranteed still-blind/unvoted — no `votes` subcollection to reconcile. **Scoped to today only** — withdrawing a revealed/already-voted entry is explicitly not supported (would need vote cleanup + raises fairness questions about pulling out mid-contest); once an entry is revealed it's locked.
  - **Found while adding `daily_prompts` security rules: the live Firestore rules had no `votes` subcollection rule.** The `daily_gallery` rules block only had a `match /likes/{userId}` rule (leftover from before the `likes`→`votes` rename documented above), never updated to also match `daily_gallery/{docId}/votes/{uid}`, and there's no top-level catch-all rule in this project's ruleset — anything unmatched is denied by default. If those were the actual live rules, voting would have been failing with "missing or insufficient permissions" the whole time, silently, since the client already handles vote failures by just not updating optimistically. Fixed by adding a `votes` sibling rule (identical shape to `likes`) under `daily_gallery`; the stale `likes` rule was left in place rather than removed (harmless unused config, not worth touching beyond what's needed). **Confirmed working** — Eddie has tested voting in the Voting Booth since the rule fix went live.
  - `toggleVote(_:)` — guards against voting outside the current window first (`entry.date == currentVotableDate`, else no-op + `false`), then does optimistic vote/unvote against `yesterdayEntries` / `myEntryToday` (whichever matches the id). `@discardableResult` so the existing fire-and-forget call site still compiles; returns `Bool` so the UI can show "voting closed" feedback (`DailyEntryDetailSheet.canVote` uses this). Votes subcollection at `daily_gallery/{docId}/votes/{uid}`. Fully separate from World Gallery likes — the same image posted to both galleries accumulates two independent counts, in separate Firestore fields/subcollections. **Confirmed: voting is unlimited, not one-per-day.** Each entry's vote doc is independent (`daily_gallery/{docId}/votes/{uid}`), so a user can vote for as many different entries in a single day's contest as they want — functionally closer to World Gallery's likes than a single-pick election vote. Considered adding a one-vote-per-day cap (more like American Idol/The Voice) but decided against it for now; revisit if it matters later. The vote itself still writes/toggles instantly and is reflected privately in the voting booth (your own vote confirms immediately, like getting an "I Voted" sticker) — it's only the aggregate count/leader that's hidden from everyone, not the act of voting.
- **User-facing wording: "Prompt" → "Subject".** "TODAY'S PROMPT" → "TODAY'S SUBJECT" (`TodayTab.promptCard`), and the withdraw-confirmation message now reads "today's subject" instead of "today's prompt". `DrawScreen`'s canvas `.navigationTitle` also shows the actual subject (`DailyPrompt.today`) instead of the generic "New Doodle" whenever the session was opened via TodayTab's "Open Canvas" (`dailySubmitIntent == true`) — i.e. before you've even submitted, the canvas itself is titled with what you're drawing for. Deliberately word-only: the underlying `DailyPrompt` struct/type name, `promptCard` property name, and `DailyPrompt.today` accessor were left as-is — renaming internal identifiers throughout the codebase wasn't part of the ask and would be a much larger, purely-cosmetic-to-users refactor for no user-visible benefit.
- **`TodayTab.swift`** —
  - `promptCard` — shows `DailyPrompt.today`. If not signed in: sign-in prompt. If signed in and no entry yet: "Open Canvas" (posts `.todaySwitchToNew` notification, which `ContentView` observes to flip to the New tab) + "Post" (opens `DailyPostPickerSheet` to pick from your private gallery). If already posted: shows your entry with a "✓ Posted" badge, "Replace My Entry", and a destructive "Withdraw" button (confirmation dialog → `DailyManager.withdrawToday`). **Fixed: posted-entry thumbnail was a "sliver" on iPad** — the image previously had only `.frame(height: 200)`, so width stretched to the card's full (much wider, on iPad) width. Now a fixed `220x220` square, which also just centers itself via the parent `VStack`'s default center alignment on both iPhone and iPad.
  - **Fixed: no direct path to submit a brand-new doodle to today's challenge, then redesigned as toggles.** "Open Canvas" only ever switched to the New tab — after drawing and tapping Done, the result card offered just "Post to Community" / "Keep Private," so entering today's contest with a fresh drawing meant saving it privately first, then going back through `DailyPostPickerSheet` to pick it from the gallery. First fix added a third mutually-exclusive result-card button ("Submit to Today's Challenge"), but that couldn't express "post publicly AND submit to today's challenge" at the same time — superseded by the current design: the result card (`DrawScreen.swift`) always saves to the private gallery unconditionally (a static "Always saved to your gallery" line, not a toggle — the private gallery is framed as a history you can always come back to and re-edit, like browser history, not an opt-in), plus two independent, freely-combinable `Toggle`s — "Post to Community" (`$wantsPublicPost`, always defaults off) and "Submit to Today's Challenge" (`$wantsDailySubmit`, shown only when signed in and `DailyManager.shared.myEntryToday == nil`, defaults on only when the session was opened via TodayTab's "Open Canvas" — threaded in as `dailySubmitIntent`, a `@Binding` passed from `ContentView` through `DrawScreen`, set true only in the `.todaySwitchToNew` notification handler and reset to false on dismiss) — and a single "Save" button (`saveResult()`) that commits whichever combination is selected. `saveResult()` always writes the private copy; if either toggle is on, its corresponding network call (`WorldGalleryManager.shared.submit` / `daily.post`) runs inside a `DispatchGroup`, and the private save happens in `group.notify` using the (possibly-mutated-by-World-Gallery) `entry` so `worldGalleryId` is captured correctly even when both toggles are on. First error from either call is surfaced via `.alert("Something Went Wrong", ...)`; the doodle is never lost even on a partial failure, since the private save always completes as long as the guard clauses pass. Where the sheet lands afterward: Daily takes priority (tab 0) if `wantsDailySubmit`, else Gallery (tab 1) — same tab-index fix as below, now folded into `saveResult()`. `DrawScreen` gained `@ObservedObject private var daily = DailyManager.shared` for this (previously had no reference to the Daily system at all).
  - **Fixed (found while adding the above): the old `saveEntry(post:)`'s post-save tab index was stale.** Both branches ended with `selectedTab = 0` to land back on the gallery — correct back when Gallery was tab 0, but Today was inserted as the new tab 0 during this build and nothing here was updated, so "Post to Community" / "Keep Private" were silently landing on the Today tab instead of the gallery ever since. Fixed to `selectedTab = 1` (Gallery's actual index — see `ContentView.swift`'s `TabView` tags), now expressed as `selectedTab = wantsDailySubmit ? 0 : 1` inside `saveResult()`. `DrawScreen.swift` hadn't been touched at all during the Daily Doodle work until this fix, per "never touch working code outside stated scope" — this one was directly adjacent to the change above, not a separate detour.
  - `yesterdaySection` — "YESTERDAY'S CONTEST" header with entry count, then (blind-reveal redesign) a single large "VOTE!" button — no spotlight, no grid, no counts, since any of those would leak ranking before the reveal. Tapping it presents `DailyVotingBoothView` full-screen. Empty state unchanged: "No doodles were submitted yesterday."
  - `DailyVotingBoothView` — the actual blind-reveal voting experience: a `TabView(.page)` swiping one-at-a-time through `yesterdayEntries` (already arrived in timestamp order from `fetchYesterday()`), each page full-size image + tappable avatar + a vote button using `checkmark.seal`/`checkmark.seal.fill` (not a heart — kept distinct from World Gallery's like icon and from the archive's revealed vote button) with **no per-entry count displayed anywhere**. Voting toggles instantly and the seal fills in as private confirmation; nothing about per-entry results is shown. Reads the live entry from `daily.yesterdayEntries` on every page (via id lookup) so a vote is reflected immediately without leaving the view. Vote button disabled on your own entry and when signed out. Button label reads "Vote for This" (was ambiguous plain "Vote") since it wasn't clear a vote was necessarily *for* the entry on screen — **still an open question, revisit wording again if a better option comes up.** Subject shown once as a header capsule — reads `daily.yesterdaySubject` (see below), **not** any entry's own `caption` field. Originally read `entries.first?.caption` (reasoning: caption is always forced to the subject at post time) but this broke for hand-seeded/legacy test data whose caption was never forced to anything (a real AI-generated caption showed instead of the subject) — fragile by construction, since it silently trusted whatever every test doc happened to contain. Prev/Next chevron buttons overlaid directly on the image itself (moved here from a screen-level overlay that used `.frame(maxHeight: .infinity, alignment: .center)` — that positioned them relative to the *whole screen* height, which could land below the image entirely depending on device height, making them easy to miss or look randomly placed) — `goTo(_:)` clamps to valid range, disabled/dimmed at both ends. Vote button's bottom padding increased (50pt → 64pt) — was getting clipped by the home indicator on some devices.
  - `DailyManager.yesterdaySubject` / `fetchYesterdaySubject()` — yesterday's real subject, resolved the same Firestore-first/local-fallback way as `todaySubject` (see `fetchSubject(for:)`, the shared helper both now call, generalized to take any `Date` instead of hardcoding "today"). `DailyPrompt.subject(for:)` similarly generalizes the old `today` mod-cycle formula to an arbitrary date, so the *fallback* for a non-today date reflects that date's own day-of-year rather than today's. This is what the Voting Booth header actually reads now — deliberately independent of any entry's `caption` field (see above).
  - **Voting Booth turnout stats only refreshed on tab appear/refresh, not while the booth itself is open.** Casting a vote inside the booth didn't move the numbers on the Today tab until the next pull-to-refresh. Fixed: `TodayTab`'s `.fullScreenCover(isPresented: $showVotingBooth, onDismiss:)` now calls `daily.fetchYesterday()` + `daily.fetchTotalUserCount()` when the booth closes, so the counts are current the moment you're back.
  - **Redesigned: forced Yes/No per doodle instead of one opt-in "Vote for This" button.** Every entry now shows two buttons; whichever you tap, `advanceAfterVote()` auto-swipes to the next page (`goTo(currentIndex + 1)`, valid range extended to `0...entries.count` to include the new completion page below). "No" is never written anywhere — it's exactly equivalent to not voting at all, so this is a pure UI change with no new data concept. `setVote(_:voted:)` sets state absolutely rather than toggling (`if entry.isVotedByMe != voted { daily.toggleVote(entry) }`), since auto-advance means you won't naturally re-tap the same page to undo a mis-tap the way the old toggle button assumed — swiping back to an already-answered doodle correctly shows which side you picked (whichever button matches `isVotedByMe` renders filled/selected) rather than looking blank. Button wording itself ("Yes"/"No") is still a placeholder — deliberately plain text, no thumbs-up/down icon, to stay distinct from World Gallery's heart-based likes; revisit the exact words later.
  - **New: a completion page after the last doodle**, reached by auto-advance or by manually swiping/tapping Next past the last entry (`.tag(entries.count)` in the `TabView`, alongside a `completionPage` view). Explains the day-boundary/reveal mechanic in plain language ("every doodle is submitted blind during its own day, the next day it's revealed here for voting, results stay hidden until that day closes too"), reminds you that swiping back lets you change any answer, and has its own "Done" button to dismiss — a deliberate stop rather than just dumping you back on the Today tab the moment you finish. The top counter ("N of M") and subject capsule are hidden while on this page (`currentIndex < entries.count` guards both), since neither applies here.
  - `pastWinnersSection` — **inlined directly into the main scroll, not a separate screen.** Originally a `pastWinnersLink` row pushing `PastWinnersView` as its own pushed screen; changed since the whole point of this tab is that submit/vote/browse-winners all live on one continuously-scrolling screen, per the original design brief. Now renders the "PAST WINNERS" header + `PastWinnerRow` list directly below `yesterdaySection`, fetched via `daily.fetchPastWinners()` alongside the other two fetches in `TodayTab`'s own `.onAppear`/`.refreshable`. Tapping a row still pushes `DailyContestDayView` via `.navigationDestination(item:)` on `TodayTab`'s own `NavigationStack` — drilling into one specific day's full results is still a legitimate secondary screen, same as the voting booth is; it's the summary list itself that shouldn't require an extra tap. `PastWinnersView` (the old standalone screen) is left in place unused rather than deleted, same as `CalendarTab.swift`'s precedent.
  - `DailyEntryDetailSheet` — full-size image, avatar/caption, vote button labeled "Vote"/"Voted" **with a visible vote count**. This is intentionally still used by the archive (`DailyContestDayView`/`PastWinnersView` drill-in) only — those days are fully revealed/finalized, so showing counts there is correct; it's no longer used by the live "yesterday" flow (that's `DailyVotingBoothView` now, which never shows a count). `canVote` computed property gates the button on both "not your own entry" and "entry is from the currently votable day" — in practice this is now always false for anything reachable through this sheet, since "yesterday" no longer routes here, but the guard stays as a safety net.
  - `DailyPostPickerSheet` — grid picker over `SnoodleStore.entries` (your private gallery) to choose what to submit.
  - `PastWinnersView` / `PastWinnerRow` — scrollable list of `DailyWinnerSummary` (from `fetchPastWinners`), most recent first. Each row is **four independent sibling tap targets** (thumbnail, date, avatar, votes/count) rather than one row wrapped in a single tappable control — keeps "tap avatar → artist profile" fully separate from "tap row → open that day" without nested-button or hit-testing workarounds. Tapping the row (not the avatar) pushes `DailyContestDayView` via `.navigationDestination(item:)`.
