Requires `IdentifiableString` (`GalleryTab.swift`) to conform to `Hashable` in addition to `Identifiable` — `.navigationDestination(item:)` requires both; added since `IdentifiableString` previously only conformed to `Identifiable` (fine everywhere else it's used, since `.sheet(item:)` only needs `Identifiable`).
  - `DailyContestDayView` — full detail for one specific concluded (fully revealed) date: winner spotlight + grid, own local `@State` (not `daily.yesterdayEntries`, which is specifically "yesterday" and no longer sorted/displayed by votes — see blind-reveal note above). Fetches via `DailyManager.fetchEntries(for:)`. This is the one place left that still shows a winner-card-plus-grid layout, since archive days are fully revealed and showing rank there is correct and intentional.
  - **Artist profile tap-through** — every avatar/username in the Daily flows (voting booth pages, past-winners rows, archive detail, detail sheets) is independently tappable via an `onAuthorTap: (String) -> Void` closure threaded down from `TodayTab.showAuthorProfile`, which presents `PublicProfileView(userId:isOwnProfile: false)` as a sheet — matches World Gallery's existing `onAuthorTap`/`authorProfileUserId` pattern (`GalleryTab.swift`) exactly, including reusing the same `IdentifiableString` wrapper type. Implemented as separate sibling Buttons rather than nesting a button inside another button's label, per `WorldSnoodleTile`'s established convention.
  - **Fixed: Past Winners showed every date one day early.** `PastWinnerRow`/`DailyContestDayView` each parse the `date` string with a `parseFormatter` correctly pinned to `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`, but their paired `displayFormatter` had no time zone set, defaulting to the device's local time zone. Formatting a contest-day Date with a different time zone than it was parsed with can roll it onto the adjacent calendar day — every date displayed one day earlier than the underlying `date` string. Fixed by pinning both formatters to the same `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`. General rule going forward: any formatter that touches a `daily_gallery` `date` string, for parsing or display, must use `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone` — never the device default.

### Explicitly deferred (do this after functionality is solid)
- ~~Visual "skin" / flashy redesign of the whole Today tab~~ — **Started.** See "Today tab redesign: winner-first layout" below. Past Winners list and the day-detail archive view are still plain/functional for now.
- Winner celebration moment (confetti/modal/animation when you open Today and you won) — not built yet.
- Push notification when you win — not built yet.
- Firestore security rules to actually enforce "no reading other users' today-entries server-side" and "no voting outside the allowed window server-side" (client currently just doesn't ask/doesn't allow it, which isn't the same as the server refusing).
- Auto-refresh on day rollover while the Today tab is left open — currently only refreshes on `.onAppear` / pull-to-refresh; a stale in-memory view of an expired day is possible but low priority (add a "contest ended, refresh" message if it turns out to actually bother anyone).
- Pagination for Past Winners beyond the fixed `lookbackDays` window (default 60 days) — not built yet; revisit if anyone's actually browsing back that far.

### Today tab redesign: winner-first layout

**Rationale (design discussion before building):** the whole point of Daily Doodle is naming a #1 winner each day — submit and vote are just the two steps that get you there, not the main event. The old layout put the submit card front-and-center with vote and winners buried below; this flips it so the most recently *decided* winner is the very first thing you see, with Submit and Vote as two equal CTAs underneath.

**Timing model reconsidered, then kept as-is.** Before building, we revisited whether the 2-day submit→vote→winner cycle could be compressed (e.g. 12-hour submit + 12-hour vote, same-day resolution) now that Eddie wanted the winner to feel like the main event. Conclusion: keep the current 24h submission + 24h voting model. A same-day model would cut both the submission and voting windows in half, which (a) roughly halves the reach of each window since it's anchored to a fixed America/New_York clock rather than each user's own day, excluding whoever's asleep during whichever half gets assigned, and (b) roughly halves how many votes an entry can accumulate before the window closes. Both effects compound against the fact that this feature needs a real crowd (Eddie's own estimate: 100+ users) before a "#1 winner" is a meaningful signal rather than noise from 2-3 votes. Real-time/no-blind-period was also considered and rejected outright — it reintroduces the exact bandwagon/spoiler problem the blind-reveal design was already built to avoid. This is a revisit-later knob once the active user base is large enough that a shorter window is still statistically fine, not a permanent decision.

**Most recent decided winner ≠ "yesterday."** `daily.pastWinners` is already sorted most-recent-first (see `fetchPastWinners`'s doc comment above), so `.first` is exactly the most recent day whose *voting* has closed — always 2 days back from today, never "yesterday" (still an open, blind-reveal vote in progress) and never "today" (still blind submission). The hero card is deliberately labeled with the actual date (`heroDisplayDate`, `"MMM d"` in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`), not a relative word like "yesterday," since that would be factually wrong.

- **`heroWinnerSection` / `heroWinnerCard(_:)`** (`TodayTab.swift`) — new hero at the very top of the Today scroll. Loading state (first fetch in flight), populated state (image with yellow border + vote-count badge, "DOODLE OF THE DAY · <date>" label, avatar, caption — image+badge and avatar are separate sibling tap targets, same non-nested-button convention as `PastWinnerRow`), and an empty state ("The first Doodle of the Day winner will appear here once a day's voting closes") for when the feature is brand new and no day has finished voting yet. Tapping the image opens the same `DailyContestDayView` that tapping a Past Winners row opens (via the existing `selectedPastDate` / `navigationDestination(item:)`).
- **`subjectStrip`** — today's subject, demoted from a 36pt hero card to a slim context strip between the winner and the CTAs. Still there (you need to know what you're drawing), just no longer the star.
- **`ctaSection` / `ctaButton(...)`** — SUBMIT! and VOTE! as two equal, always-visible CTAs. Submit reads "SUBMITTED ✓" (green) once you've posted today instead of hiding/replacing the button; Vote is grayed out and disabled (not hidden) when yesterday has no entries, for visual symmetry between the two rather than one button disappearing. Turnout stats (unique voters, % of total users) still shown beneath, unchanged from before.
- **`DailySubmitScreen`** (new top-level struct, mirrors `DailyVotingBoothView`'s existing full-screen pattern) — everything that used to live inline in the old subject card (subject + count, Open Canvas / Post if not yet entered, Replace / Withdraw if already posted) now lives in its own full-screen cover, opened by the SUBMIT! CTA. `showingPostPicker` and `showWithdrawConfirm` stay owned by `TodayTab` and are passed down as `@Binding`s, since their `.sheet`/`.confirmationDialog` are declared on `TodayTab`'s own `NavigationStack` — presenting from there on top of the `DailySubmitScreen` full-screen cover works the same way sheet-on-sheet presentation already does elsewhere in the app. "Open Canvas" now calls `dismiss()` on the Submit screen before posting `.todaySwitchToNew` (0.35s delay, same pattern as other sheet-transition spots in this codebase) — otherwise the New tab's own full-screen `DrawScreen` cover would stack on top of the still-open Submit screen instead of replacing it.
- **`pastWinnersSection`** now shows `remainingPastWinners` (`daily.pastWinners.dropFirst()`) instead of the full list, since the hero above already covers the most recent entry — avoids showing the same winner twice on one screen. Empty-state copy changed from "No past winners yet" to "No more past winners yet" to match (the hero may already be showing the only winner so far).
- **Old `promptCard` and `yesterdaySection` removed** — fully superseded by the above. All underlying data/fetch logic (`myEntryToday`, `yesterdayEntries`, `todaySubject`, counts, turnout) is unchanged; this was presentation-only.
- **Still plain/unstyled, deliberately out of scope for this pass:** Past Winners list rows and `DailyContestDayView`'s own winner-card-plus-grid layout. Winner celebration moment and push-on-win are still separate, not-yet-built items (see above).
- **`RibbonBadge` / `RibbonTail`** (`TodayTab.swift`, top-level structs) — the blue prize ribbon overlapping the top-left corner of the hero winner's image. Built entirely from SwiftUI shapes (`Circle` petal ring + a custom `RibbonTail: Shape` with a V-notch cut into the bottom edge), no image asset. Chosen after mocking up three treatments together: a plain circle-and-rectangle badge read as a lollipop rather than a ribbon once actually rendered; a flat single-tone version felt too quiet; this pleated two-tone version (alternating petal shades + a darker medallion) was the one that actually looked like a ribbon. Label reads "BEST", not "1st" — there's no 2nd/3rd place in this design, just one decided winner per day. Deliberately overlaps the image corner rather than framing/tilting the whole canvas — the winning artist's linework stays perfectly flat and undistorted; only the ribbon breaks the grid. The old plain yellow border around the hero image was removed in favor of this.
- **Heart icon → `checkmark.seal` for votes, everywhere in Daily Doodle.** The heart-means-likes vs. votes ambiguity flagged as a known deferred item (see "Terminology: votes, not likes" above) is now fixed: every vote display in Daily Doodle (hero winner badge, `PastWinnerRow`, `DailyContestDayView`'s winner card, `DailyEntryDetailSheet`'s vote button and read-only vote count) uses `checkmark.seal`/`checkmark.seal.fill` (green when voted/counted) instead of `heart`/`heart.fill` (pink). Matches the icon the Voting Booth already used for casting a vote, so the whole vote visual language is now consistent and visually distinct from World Gallery's heart-based likes. World Gallery itself is untouched — hearts still mean likes there.
- **`RibbonBadge` still hand-rolled SwiftUI shapes, not a real image asset.** Eddie shared a reference "1st Place" ribbon photo (real pleated fabric, gradient shading) and asked whether that was being used — it isn't; there's no tool in this environment to save a chat-pasted image to disk or generate new art, and that reference photo looks like stock art we wouldn't have the right to ship anyway. **Decided (for now): keep iterating on the vector shape** rather than source a licensed image asset — revisit if a real asset becomes available (Eddie would need to add a properly-licensed file to the project; wiring it into Assets.xcassets is straightforward whenever that happens).
- **Confirmed: single winner only, no top-3 podium.** Discussed adding 2nd/3rd place to the hero (technically cheap — `fetchEntries(for:)` already returns each day sorted by votes descending, so a podium needs no new backend work) but decided against it, keeping the original single-winner framing. Ribbon wording stays "BEST", not "1st" — reopen this if the podium idea comes back.
- **Confirmed: hero image keeps cropping to fill (`.fill`/"cover"), not letterboxed.** Doodle canvases aren't guaranteed square — `canvasSize` in `DrawScreen.swift` is set from the actual on-screen drawing area's `GeometryReader` size at draw time, which varies by device, so a non-square doodle gets center-cropped into the hero's forced 1:1 square today. Raised as a possible conflict with the "don't distort the artist's work" principle from the ribbon discussion, but Eddie chose to keep the current crop-to-fill behavior rather than switch to letterboxing.
- **Fixed: hero image was full iPad-card-width, making the square tall enough to require scrolling to see the whole thing.** `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` on the 1:1-aspect image meant its width (and therefore height, since it's forced square) equaled the entire hero card's width — comfortable on iPhone, but on a wide iPad screen this produced a square tall enough that it didn't fit on screen together with the tab bar and header above it. Fixed by capping at `.frame(maxWidth: 380)` before the existing `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` (the fixed-width child is centered within the flexible parent) — same fix shape as the earlier "posted-entry thumbnail was a sliver on iPad" bug.
- **`RibbonBadge`/`RibbonTail` fixed through three rounds of screenshot-driven feedback:** (1) tails originally angled in from the sides instead of fanning out from one shared point — root cause was each tail sitting in an `HStack` and rotating around its own default `.center` anchor independently; fixed by moving both tails into a `ZStack(alignment: .top)` and using `.rotationEffect(_:anchor: .top)` on each so they share one attachment point and fan outward from it (angles widened to −16°/+16°, frames enlarged). (2) tails were rendering on top of the "BEST" medallion instead of behind it, and the whole badge was getting clipped against the hero card's edge — fixed by restructuring `RibbonBadge.body` into one outer `ZStack` with the tails-group declared first (paints behind) and the rosette-group declared second (paints on top), and by shrinking `heroWinnerCard`'s badge offset from `(-14,-14)` to `(-2,-6)` so it stays inside the card's 16pt padding before the card's own corner-radius clip. (3) tails were barely "peeking out" below the medallion instead of hanging down visibly — root cause was the outer `ZStack`'s default `.center` alignment centering each child's full height (including the tail-group's own vertical midpoint) before any offset was applied, so most of the offset budget was spent just clearing the tail-group's own half-height; fixed by switching the outer `ZStack` to `alignment: .top` (giving both children one shared top reference line so offsets behave as literally specified) and increasing `.offset(y: 12)` → `.offset(y: 26)` plus taller tail frames (54/58pt → 64/68pt height, 24pt → 26pt width).
- **Braid-weave frame tried and rejected — replaced with a plain dark-to-light gradient ring.** The woven `BraidFrame` (gold+brown, arc-length sinusoidal weave ported from `DrawingEngine.swift`'s `.braid` pen style) was built and wired in, but once actually seen it read as taking over the doodle itself — Eddie's call: "if they want a border like that they'd create it in the doodle." `BraidFrame` was removed outright (not left in as unused code — this was same-session, never-shipped iteration, not a case where the old path is still doing anything for anyone) and replaced with **`GradientFrame`** (`TodayTab.swift`, same location, same call site).
- **`GradientFrame`'s first pass (a single `RadialGradient` centered on the square) had a real bug, caught from a screenshot: brown drifting toward yellow partway down each side.** Root cause: `RadialGradient` shades by straight-line distance from one center point, which only equals "how far into the ring" at the exact midpoint of each flat edge on a rounded *rectangle* — anywhere else along an edge, Pythagoras adds a sideways component the radial math can't discount, so distance-from-center overshoots the ring's true local depth. That pushed the gradient's inner/outer stops out of alignment well before reaching the corners (which, being farthest from center, just clamped to flat dark with no gradient at all) — the visible symptom partway down each side was the ring having already blended part-way from dark toward light when it should still have read as fully dark, which shows as a yellow-ish band. **Fixed:** replaced the single `RadialGradient` with **concentric offset rings** — `GradientFrame.body` layers 16 thin `RoundedRectangle` strokes, each padded inward slightly more than the last with a correspondingly smaller corner radius (a true parallel offset of the actual rounded-rect shape, corners included, not a distance-from-center approximation), colored via a `lerp(_:_:_:)` helper that interpolates dark → light across the steps (bridges through `UIColor.getRed` since `Color` doesn't expose its own components). Because each ring is a genuine inward offset of the real shape, "how far into the frame" is now correct at every point on the perimeter, not just the four edge midpoints. Same colors/thickness as before (dark bronze `0.42, 0.27, 0.15` outer, light gold `0.94, 0.83, 0.53` inner, 10pt thick).
- **Ribbon repositioned + given a floating shadow, both per direct feedback on the same screenshot.** `RibbonBadge` moved from overlapping the top-left corner (partially hanging outside the card) to sitting fully inside the frame at the top-right — `heroWinnerCard`'s inner `ZStack` alignment changed from `.topLeading` to `.topTrailing`, and the badge's offset changed from `(-2, -6)` to `(-14, 14)` (pulling it in from the corner far enough to clear both the rounded corner's curve and the frame's own thickness). Shadow deepened from the original tight `(radius: 2, offset: (0,2), opacity: 0.25)` to `(radius: 6, offset: (0,4), opacity: 0.35)` so it reads as floating just above the image rather than printed flat onto it.
- **Not yet visually confirmed on device/simulator** — this environment can't render SwiftUI/run the app, so all of the above (the concentric-ring fix, the new ribbon position, the shadow) is correct by construction/math but hasn't been screenshot-checked since being changed. **Next step: build and actually look at it** — confirm the ring now reads evenly dark-to-light all the way around including the corners, that the ribbon sits fully inside the frame at the top-right without being clipped, and that the shadow reads as "floating" without looking overdone.
- **Fixed: `GradientFrame` stretched across the whole screen on iPad instead of hugging the doodle square.** Root cause: the `.overlay(GeometryReader { ... })` that sizes `GradientFrame` was attached *after* `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` in the image's modifier chain — a `GeometryReader` inside an `.overlay` measures whatever view it's attached to at that exact point, and that infinity-width frame expands to fill the whole available card width on a wide iPad screen (the actual 380pt-capped image just sits centered inside it, visually unaffected, but the *container* GeometryReader saw was the full expanded width). Fixed by moving the overlay to right after `.frame(maxWidth: 380)` / `.clipShape(...)`, before the `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` — so it measures the true ~380×380 (or smaller on iPhone) image size, and the whole already-framed unit (image + bevel ring) gets centered together by the trailing infinity-width frame, same as before. iPhone was unaffected either way since there the capped width and the available width are usually close to equal.
- **Ribbon repositioned + given a floating shadow, both per direct feedback on the same screenshot.** `RibbonBadge` moved from overlapping the top-left corner of the frame to sitting fully *on the canvas* at the top-right, with breathing room between it and the frame ring — offset increased from `(-14, 14)` to `(-22, 22)` (clearing the frame's 10pt thickness plus a real gap, not just clearing the rounded corner). Shadow from the earlier round `(radius: 6, offset: (0,4), opacity: 0.35)` unchanged — already reads as floating.
- **Follow-up fix: the offset alone wasn't enough — the ribbon's actual alignment reference was wrong.** `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` had been applied to the hero image alone, as a modifier inside the `ZStack` that also contains `RibbonBadge` as a sibling. That expanded the *image's own* reported bounding box to fill the available card width, which in turn expanded the whole `ZStack`'s size to match (a `ZStack` sizes itself to its largest child) — so `.topTrailing` alignment placed the ribbon at the top-right of that expanded box, not the top-right of the true ~380pt image sitting centered inside it. On anything wider than exactly 380pt (effectively every device), the ribbon ended up pinned toward the card's outer edge instead of resting on the doodle. Fixed by moving `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` to wrap the entire `ZStack` (image + frame + ribbon) from the outside, after it, instead of being one of the `ZStack`'s children — now the `ZStack`'s own size is the true image size, `.topTrailing` aligns correctly against it, and the following `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity)` just centers that whole already-correct unit within the card.
- **`DailyContestDayView` bottom content (vote count) was getting clipped, only visible briefly before the image finished loading.** Each swipeable page (`dayPage(for:rank:)`) had no `ScrollView` — fine as long as the image + avatar + caption + vote-count block fit within the screen height, but `RetryAsyncImage`'s placeholder is shorter than the real image, so the page's total height grew once the real (full aspect-ratio) image popped in, pushing the vote-count row below the visible screen with nothing to scroll it into view (worse with a longer caption). Fixed by wrapping each page's content in its own `ScrollView` — each page still scrolls independently while `TabView(.page)` continues to page horizontally between doodles, same pattern the original (pre-redesign) grid-based `DailyContestDayView` used.
- **The same bug existed in `DailyVotingBoothView`, caught live during 2.8 b1 testing (voting on a real 2-entry day) — the fix above was never ported over when the Voting Booth was built.** `boothPage(for:)` had the identical `RetryAsyncImage(...).aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` markup as `dayPage(for:rank:)`, but no `ScrollView` wrapper — a portrait/tall doodle's real post-load aspect ratio could push the question text and Yes/No buttons below the screen with nothing to scroll them into view. Direct report: "when i hit yes and advance to the 2nd doodle, its vertically too big for the assigned area and the text and buttons falls well below the bottom of the screen... look at the details page which is sim — horiz swipe. it works perfectly" — correctly identifying `DailyContestDayView` as the working reference. First fix: `boothPage(for:)`'s content wrapped in its own `ScrollView`, matching `dayPage`'s existing pattern — superseded below.
- **`ScrollView` approach for both pages replaced with a true fixed-rect, cover-cropped image box — direct follow-up feedback: "i dont want any vertical scrolling on the voting screens... there is a fixed rect that every doodle must fit into. if the natural aspect ratio doesnt match, the cover-type-styling is used... look at the private and public gallery details page."** The `ScrollView` fix stopped content from being unreachable, but the box's actual height still varied doodle to doodle (a tall portrait canvas made for a taller box that then needed scrolling) — not what was wanted. Both `boothPage(for:)` (`DailyVotingBoothView`) and `dayPage(for:rank:)` (`DailyContestDayView`) had their `ScrollView` removed and now use a fixed image box instead: `RetryAsyncImage(url:, contentMode: .fill)` (cover-crop, not the outer `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` trick) inside `.clipped()`. `dayPage`'s caption also capped to `.lineLimit(2)` for the same reason — an unbounded caption was the other thing (besides the image) that could still push the vote count off-screen without a `ScrollView` to fall back on.
  - **First pass used a literal fixed height (300pt, picked with margin for iPhone SE) — screenshot feedback on iPad caught it looking like "a very wide narrow strip," not filling the available area "with the style thats like the cover css."** A hardcoded pixel value is safe on the smallest phone but leaves a large dead gap above/below on a taller screen, since the box doesn't know to grow with the room it actually has. **Fixed: `.frame(maxHeight: .infinity)` instead of a literal number**, on both `boothPage` and `dayPage`. This is the actual CSS-`cover`-on-a-`height:100%`-container equivalent — the image box greedily fills whatever vertical space is left after the fixed-size elements (avatar row, question, buttons) claim their own height, rather than guessing a constant. Still can't grow unbounded, since the whole page is itself bounded by the fullscreen `ZStack` behind it (the same `Color(...).ignoresSafeArea()` + sibling `TabView` structure `SnoodleDetailView`/`WorldSnoodleDetailView` already rely on for their own no-scroll layouts) — it just now correctly fills 100% of that available room on any device instead of a fixed guess. Not yet visually confirmed on device.
- **`SubjectPlacard` added — a museum-nameplate-style tag on the hero winner's frame, showing that day's subject.** Per a reference screenshot (a plaque reading "Fireworks" straddling the bottom edge of a framed picture) — cream/ivory fill, bold black serif text, black border, drop shadow, positioned via `.overlay(alignment: .bottom) { SubjectPlacard(...).offset(y: -18) }` on the hero image (declared in the same modifier chain as `GradientFrame`, so it paints on top of the frame too). Uses `summary.winner.caption` directly — no new subject fetch needed, since Daily Doodle entries always force `caption = subject` at post time (see `DailyManager.post`'s doc comment elsewhere in this file). The plain caption text that used to sit next to the avatar below the image was removed as a result — it's now redundant with the placard, so that row is just the artist avatar.
- **Idea floated, not yet built: holiday-aware subjects for specific dates (e.g. July 4 → "Fireworks", Christmas, Presidents Day).** This is exactly the "manual override only for specific dates that matter (e.g. a holiday)" case already anticipated in the `daily_prompts` design (see "Confirmed design for whenever the website admin panel does get built" above) — the plumbing already supports it with zero code changes: hand-write a `daily_prompts/{YYYY-MM-DD}` doc (fields `subject`/`category`) for a specific holiday date via Firebase Console, same as any other manual date override, and `DailyManager.fetchTodaySubject()`/`fetchSubject(for:)` will pick it up automatically over the random pool. Not yet decided: whether to also teach the DEBUG `seedDailyPromptsIfDebug()` bulk-seeder to recognize known holidays and special-case them (vs. purely manual per-date console edits, which is fine at current scale). Just a thought Eddie flagged for later, nothing requested to build yet.
- **Tab nav title changed "Today" → "Daily Doodle"; hero card's "DOODLE OF THE DAY" label now shows the actual subject instead.** Freed up that phrase from the hero card specifically so the nav title could use it — decided "Daily Doodle" instead, since that's the feature's actual established name (used throughout this doc) and reads better as a short nav title than the more sentence-like "Doodle of the Day". The hero card's crown row (`heroWinnerCard`, `TodayTab.swift`) now reads `summary.winner.caption` (the day's subject, with a "Doodle of the Day" fallback for the rare empty-caption case) instead of a fixed label — dropped the all-caps + `.tracking(1.5)` styling that suited a static label, since this is real varying content now. Both the subject and the date bumped bolder (`.bold`→`.heavy` for the subject, `.medium`→`.bold` for the date), per direct feedback.
- **Bug: hero card briefly showed an AI-generated caption instead of the day's subject — same fragility class already fixed once for the Voting Booth.** Reading `summary.winner.caption` directly (both for the crown-row label above and the new `SubjectPlacard` on the frame) assumed caption always equals the subject — true for entries posted through the real `post()` flow (which forces `caption = subject`), but not for hand-seeded/legacy test docs, which can have an actual AI-style caption sitting in that field instead. That's exactly what surfaced: a test entry's real AI caption ("My poodle is feeling a little purple today") displayed as if it were the day's theme. This is the identical bug `DailyVotingBoothView`'s `yesterdaySubject` was already built to avoid (see that section above) — just not yet applied to the hero card. **Fixed the same way:** added `DailyManager.heroWinnerSubject` (`@Published`) + `fetchHeroWinnerSubject(for:)`, which parses the hero's date string (via a new `dateOnlyFormatter`, pinned to `contestTimeZone` like every other date parse in this file) and resolves it through the same reliable `fetchSubject(for:)` helper `today`/`yesterdaySubject` already use (Firestore `daily_prompts` first, local mod-cycle fallback) — never from any entry's `caption`. Triggered automatically at the end of `fetchPastWinners()` once the most recent winner's date is known, so the view doesn't have to remember to call it separately. `heroWinnerCard`'s crown row and `SubjectPlacard` both switched from `summary.winner.caption` to `daily.heroWinnerSubject`.
- **Crown row reverted to a static "Doodle of the Day" label, crown icon removed — the subject-in-crown-row experiment above was short-lived.** Per direct feedback: showing the subject twice (once here, once via `SubjectPlacard` on the frame) was redundant, so the top row goes back to a fixed "Doodle of the Day · <date>" label, just bigger/bolder than before (13pt heavy/bold → 15pt black/heavy). `daily.heroWinnerSubject` is still fetched and still used — just only by `SubjectPlacard` now, not duplicated up here too.
- **Reported: Voting Booth's Yes/No buttons appearing blank in a running build.** Checked `voteButtons(for:)` (`TodayTab.swift`) — the source still has plain `Text("No")` / `Text("Yes")` literals, unchanged from when they were added, not driven by any state that could evaluate empty. Nothing in this session's edits touched that function. Also checked for a stray `Localizable.strings`/`.xcstrings` file that could intercept `Text("No")`/`Text("Yes")` as localization keys and remap them to empty values — none exist in this project, so that's ruled out too.
  - **Eddie confirmed this is not a stale-build artifact** (maybe 2 stale builds ever, out of thousands) — so the cause is real, not a cache issue. Not yet resolved. **Leading theory, not yet confirmed:** `voteButtons(for:)` disables both buttons and drops them to 40% opacity (`.disabled(isMe || !auth.isSignedIn).opacity(...)`) whenever the entry being voted on belongs to the currently signed-in account (`isMe`) — a deliberate rule, "can't vote on your own doodle." In a low-population test environment, if *all* of a given day's entries happen to belong to the same signed-in test account (plausible — the example screenshot showed "2 entries" for that day), every single page of the booth would render its Yes/No text at 40% opacity, which could easily read as "blank" rather than "grayed out," especially in a screenshot or under bright screen glare. Needs confirming: were the entries being voted on posted by the currently signed-in account, or a different one? If different accounts and still blank, this theory is wrong and needs a fresh look with a screenshot of the actual Voting Booth screen.
- **Hero date format expanded** — `heroDisplayFormatter` (`TodayTab.swift`) changed from `"MMM d"` ("Jul 2") to `"EEE, MMM d, yyyy"` ("Sat, Jul 3, 2026"), per direct feedback. Still pinned to `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone`, same as every other formatter touching a contest-day date string.
- **Today tab's three sections given distinct card backgrounds, so the screen reads as three clearly separated zones at a glance.** Previously only the hero winner card had a background (a light yellow/purple gradient); the subject/countdown/CTA block and the Past Winners list both sat directly on the plain scroll background with no visual boundary. Restructured `body`'s top-level `VStack` (now `spacing: 20`, was `spacing: 0` with manual per-section top-padding) into three cards:
  - **Hero card** — same yellow/purple gradient, just bumped darker (`0.15`/`0.08` → `0.24`/`0.16` opacity) so it's clearly a card, not a faint tint.
  - **`submitVoteCard`** (new) — wraps `subjectStrip` + `countdownStrip` + `ctaSection` in one card with a cool blue tint (`Color.blue.opacity(0.12)`), contrasting with the hero card's warm tone. Purely a presentation grouping — none of the three wrapped views changed internally, just composed together with shared `.padding(16)` + background + `RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 24)` (matching the hero card's own corner radius).
  - **`pastWinnersCard`** (new) — wraps the existing `pastWinnersSection` in a third, amber/parchment tint (`Color.orange.opacity(0.12)`) — reads as "archive," pairs with the trophy iconography, and is distinct from both cards above. `pastWinnersSection`'s internal per-element `.padding(.horizontal, 16)` calls (on the header row and the `ForEach` loop wrapping each `PastWinnerRow`) were removed since the new card wrapper's own `.padding(16)` already provides that inset — `PastWinnerRow` itself independently has its own baked-in `.padding(.horizontal, 16)`/`.padding(.vertical, 10)` at the end of its `body`, so removing the redundant call-site padding doesn't change its own layout, just avoids double-padding.
- **Each of the three cards given a 2pt border in a darker shade of its own tint color**, per direct feedback that the tint alone wasn't enough of a boundary. `.overlay(RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: 24).stroke(color, lineWidth: 2))` added after each card's existing `.clipShape` — hero card: `Color.yellow.opacity(0.6)`, `submitVoteCard`: `Color.blue.opacity(0.5)`, `pastWinnersCard`: `Color.orange.opacity(0.5)`. Each border color intentionally matches that card's own background hue (just more saturated/opaque), not a neutral gray, so the border reads as "this card's own edge" rather than a generic outline.
- **Turnout stat wording flagged as misleading, not yet resolved — deliberately left alone for now.** `yesterdayUniqueVoterCount` only counts users who tapped **Yes** on at least one doodle (a "No" tap writes nothing to Firestore — see `DailyVotingBoothView`'s forced Yes/No redesign above, where No is explicitly "equivalent to not voting at all"). So the displayed line ("X of Y users voted (Z%)") overclaims — a user who opened the booth and said No to everything is indistinguishable in the data from a user who never opened it at all, so this isn't really a "turnout" number, it's an affirmative-vote count. Eddie floated (and rejected) a weighted-scoring idea (Yes = +2, No = −1) as a possible fix, but that doesn't actually solve the wording problem since No still isn't tracked as a distinct event from non-participation. **Decided: leave the wording as-is for now, revisit later** — options on the table when it's picked back up: (a) reword to state plainly what's counted ("X of Y users said yes to something"), (b) drop the denominator/percent entirely and just show the raw yes-count, or (c) actually start recording real participation (write something even on a No tap) so true turnout becomes measurable — the biggest lift of the three, and not yet decided as worth it.
- **`DailyContestDayView` redesigned: winner-card + grid replaced with a swipeable one-doodle-at-a-time browser, most-voted first.** Per direct feedback, tapping the hero winner image or a Past Winners row (both already routed through the same `selectedPastDate` → `.navigationDestination`) no longer opens a screen with a spotlighted winner card above a grid of the rest — that layout "needs to go." It's now the same one-at-a-time swiping pattern as `DailyVotingBoothView` (`TabView(.page)`, prev/next chevrons overlaid on the image, a "N of M" counter), just read-only (no Yes/No buttons — these days are already closed, `toggleVote` would no-op on them per its window guard) and with the real per-entry vote count shown, since archive days are fully revealed. `entries` already arrives votes-descending/timestamp-ascending from `DailyManager.fetchEntries(for:)`, so index 0 is always the winner with no separate sort — it gets a small trophy badge (top-leading over its image) as the only visual distinction from the rest, no separate spotlight card. Unlike the Voting Booth (which always has a completion page to advance past the last entry), Next is disabled on the last entry here since there's nothing to advance to. `DailyEntryTile` and `DailyEntryDetailSheet` (the old grid-cell view and its detail sheet) are left in the file unused rather than deleted — same precedent as `PastWinnersView`/`CalendarTab.swift`.
- **Shared countdown clock added between the subject strip and the SUBMIT!/VOTE! CTAs.** Design discussion first: the submission window (today) and the voting window (yesterday) are two 24h windows permanently offset by exactly one day, so they always close at the *exact same instant* every day, by construction (see "Submission / voting window model" above) — showing that identical number twice, once per button, would just look like a duplicate-data bug. Decided: one shared ticking clock, not two, and no text explaining "this is for July 3 / this is for July 4" — the SUBMIT!/VOTE! buttons and their existing subtitles ("23 submitted so far" / "8 entries · 42 votes") already carry that context, so a bare countdown reads fine without it. Text format: `"HH:MM:SS"` under a "TIME REMAINING" heading (dropped the trailing "remaining"/"left" word entirely once the heading was in place — redundant with it right above). **`countdownStrip`** (`TodayTab.swift`, between `subjectStrip` and `ctaSection` in `body`) uses `TimelineView(.periodic(from: .now, by: 1))` — not a manual `Timer` + `@State` — for the per-second tick, the idiomatic SwiftUI way to drive a live-updating view. `secondsUntilContestBoundary(from:)` computes seconds until the next midnight in `DailyEntry.contestTimeZone` via `Calendar.startOfDay(for:)` + `.addingTimeInterval`/`.byAdding(.day, value: 1)`, matching the same boundary every other Daily Doodle rollover logic uses. `countdownText(_:)` formats it monospaced-digit (`design: .monospaced` on the `Text`'s font) so the ticking seconds don't jitter the layout width each time a digit changes. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same caveat as the frame/ribbon work above.

### "Game-chrome" pass — pushing SwiftUI shapes as far as they'll go

**Context/decision.** After the three-card layout above, Eddie's read was "not distinctive... not especially pretty... just don't know what to do with." He then shared two ChatGPT-generated mockup images of a much more game-like "carved wood/gold/parchment" skin — shaped banner labels, real beveled stone/gold panels, chunky 3D buttons, gold/silver/bronze rank medals, a painterly background. I confirmed those specific structural principles (material-based differentiation per section, genuine bevels/shadows instead of flat tints+strokes, shaped-chrome text labels instead of plain tracked caps, medal icons for rank instead of a number) while being upfront that this environment has no image-generation tool — the actual painted textures (wood grain, stone, parchment illustration, the background art itself) aren't reproducible, only the structural/shape logic is. Eddie's explicit call: **"Push SwiftUI shapes as far as they'll go."** Everything below chases the mockups' structural principles using only SwiftUI shapes/gradients — no image assets.

- **New reusable components** (`TodayTab.swift`, `// MARK: - Game-Chrome Components` section, right after `GradientFrame`):
  - **`BannerShape` / `BannerLabel`** — a pennant/nameplate shape (rectangle with a triangular notch cut into each end) so a section header reads as its own shaped object rather than text sitting on a tint. `BannerLabel(text:color:textColor:fontSize:)` wraps it with a subtle dark stroke + drop shadow.
  - **`RankMedal`** — small gold/silver/bronze radial-gradient disc (rank 2 = silver, 3 = bronze, 4+ reuses gold rather than inventing a 4th tier — there's no real "4th place" concept here) with a colored `RibbonTail` (reusing the existing hero-ribbon tail shape) hanging beneath it, plus a drop shadow. Rank 1 is never rendered by this component — the actual #1 winner is already the hero card, so `RankMedal` only ever appears at rank 2+.
  - **`Color.shaded(_:)`** — a brightness-adjust helper (blends a color toward white for positive amounts, toward black for negative), bridging through `UIColor.getRed` the same way `GradientFrame.lerp` already does. Lets the CTA buttons turn a single flat identity color (`Color.purple`, `Color.green`, etc.) into a lit-from-above gradient without hand-picking a second literal color at every call site.
- **Hero card (`heroWinnerCard`)** — the "Doodle of the Day · date" plain-text header replaced with `BannerLabel(text: "Doodle of the Day", color: purple)` plus the date as its own small capsule pill underneath (two-tier header/date, closer to the mockups' look than one crammed line). The card's flat 2pt yellow stroke replaced with a real gold/bronze bezel — reuses `GradientFrame` (the same concentric-ring technique already proven geometrically correct around rounded corners, unlike a flat stroke or a `RadialGradient`) at `thickness: 5`, `darkColor`/`lightColor` tuned to a gold identity rather than the hero image frame's bronze/gold pair.
- **Submit/Vote card (`submitVoteCard`)** — restyled as a "gem panel": the flat `Color.blue.opacity(0.12)` tint + 2pt stroke replaced with a deep indigo/violet `LinearGradient` fill (a jewel tone, not a pastel tint) plus a gold `GradientFrame` bezel (same component, warmer gold pair than the hero's). Added a `BannerLabel(text: "Today's Challenge", color: teal)` header above `subjectStrip`. Because the background is now dark, `subjectStrip`, `countdownStrip`, and the turnout-stat `Text` inside `ctaSection` all had their internal colors switched from `.secondary`/`.primary` (dynamic, assume a light-ish system background) to explicit white/opacity values — safe since none of those three views are reused anywhere outside this card.
  - **`ctaButton` (SUBMIT!/VOTE!) made "chunky"** — flat `color` fill replaced with a top-lit `LinearGradient` (`color.shaded(0.35)` → `color` → `color.shaded(-0.25)`, top to bottom — same lit-from-above logic as the medal discs and the hero bezel, just linear instead of radial/concentric), plus a bright top-edge-only highlight stroke (a full-perimeter stroke would read as an outline, not a raised edge catching light — so this one fades from white at the top to transparent by the vertical center) and a separate darker bottom/side stroke (`color.shaded(-0.45)`), plus a deeper colored drop shadow (`color.shaded(-0.5).opacity(0.6)`) so the button reads as a raised chip rather than a flat color swatch.
- **Past Winners card (`pastWinnersCard`/`pastWinnersSection`)** — restyled as a "parchment archive": the flat `Color.orange.opacity(0.12)` tint + 2pt stroke replaced with a tan/parchment `LinearGradient` fill (reads as an old ledger page, fitting for a historical record) plus a brown wood-tone `GradientFrame` bezel. The trophy-icon-plus-tracked-caps header replaced with a centered green `BannerLabel(text: "Past Winners", ...)`. Because the parchment background is a fixed light tint regardless of system light/dark mode (same reasoning as the other two cards), the empty-state icon/text and `PastWinnerRow`'s date/vote-count/entry-count text all switched from `.secondary` to an explicit fixed brown ink tone (`Color(red: 0.32, green: 0.20, blue: 0.09)` at varying opacities) — `.secondary` would lose contrast against this fixed background in dark mode.
  - **`PastWinnerRow` gained a `rank: Int = 2` parameter** and now shows a scaled-down `RankMedal(rank:)` (replacing the old plain yellow-circle trophy badge) in the thumbnail's top-left corner. `remainingPastWinners`'s `ForEach` now enumerates (`Array(remainingPastWinners.enumerated())`) and passes `rank: index + 2` — rank starts at 2, never 1, since the hero card above is always the actual most-recent decided winner. The `rank` parameter defaults to 2 rather than being required, specifically so the old, no-longer-linked-to standalone `PastWinnersView` screen (which still calls `PastWinnerRow` without a rank) keeps compiling unchanged, per this codebase's "leave orphaned code alone" convention.
- **Not yet visually confirmed on device/simulator** — same standing caveat as every other visual change this session: this environment can't compile, run, or render SwiftUI, so all of the above is correct by code review + a custom brace-balance check, not by actually looking at it. **Next step: build and look** — confirm the gem-panel/parchment contrast reads well, the bezels render without artifacts on both cards (not just the hero image), the medals are legible at their scaled-down row size, and the chunky CTA buttons' bevel doesn't look muddy against the dark gem-panel background.
- **`GradientFrame(...)` call sites had `thickness` out of order relative to `darkColor`/`lightColor` — real compiler errors, not just a style nit.** Swift requires keyword arguments at a call site to appear in the same order the parameters are declared (unlike some languages, where labeled args can be freely reordered) — `GradientFrame`'s declared order is `cornerRadius, thickness, darkColor, lightColor`, but all three new bezel call sites (hero card, submit/vote card, Past Winners card) had been written as `cornerRadius, darkColor, lightColor, thickness`. Xcode flagged all three with "Argument 'thickness' must precede argument 'darkColor'". Fixed by reordering each call site's arguments to match the declaration — no logic change, pure argument-order fix.
- **First round of feedback on the built game-chrome pass, all positive on 2 of 3 cards:** Past Winners card ("like a gold plaque, perfect") and Today's Challenge/submit-vote card both confirmed as-is — **explicitly leave both alone for now.**
- **Turnout stat reworded — dropped the denominator/percent entirely (option (b) from the list above).** "X of Y users voted (Z%)" still read as implying a real participation rate even after the earlier wording flag — reopened because it kept inviting the "well I voted no, why aren't I counted" question. Fixed to a plain vote-count statement with no comparison baked in: `"N vote(s) is/are in"` (singular/plural handled inline) — no total-user denominator, no percentage, nothing implying a tracked "didn't vote" population that doesn't actually exist (see `DailyVotingBoothView`'s forced Yes/No redesign elsewhere in this doc — a "No" tap writes nothing to Firestore, so there's genuinely no "no" count to divide against). Still uses the same underlying `daily.yesterdayUniqueVoterCount` number as before — this is a wording-only change, not a new data source. `daily.totalUserCount`/`yesterdayVoterTurnoutPercent` are left in `DailyManager` unused by this call site (still computed, just not read here) rather than removed, in case the wording gets revisited again later. (`TodayTab.swift`, `ctaSection`)
- **Hero image frame given a dark inner-edge line so it reads as beveled on a light interior, not just a dark one.** Feedback: all three cards' bezels look beveled on the *outside* edge, but only the submit/vote card's canvas-level frame (the one used on the hero **card's border**, not the image) reads as beveled on the *inside* too — because that card's interior is dark, so `GradientFrame`'s pale-gold `lightColor` end already creates a hard value-break against it "for free." On a light interior — the hero **image's own frame** (around the doodle photo itself) and the Past Winners card's parchment interior — the light end of the gradient is close in value to the interior color, so the ring just fades out instead of stopping, reading as smoothing rather than a bevel edge. Per direct instruction, **only touched the hero image's own frame — left the submit/vote card and Past Winners card bezels alone.** Fixed by adding an optional `innerEdgeColor: Color? = nil` (+ `innerEdgeWidth: CGFloat = 1.5`) to `GradientFrame`: when set, an extra thin solid stroke is drawn at the frame's innermost ring (same inset math as the `t == 1` ring, `cornerRadius - thickness` / `.padding(thickness)`), manufacturing the missing abrupt value-break artificially. `nil` (the default) leaves every other existing call site — the three card-level bezels — completely unchanged. Wired in only at the hero image's `GradientFrame(cornerRadius: 20, ...)` call with a near-black dark bronze (`Color(red: 0.20, green: 0.12, blue: 0.05)`). Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as everything else in this pass.
- **Second round of feedback: Past Winners card ("sweet... perfect") and Today's Challenge/submit-vote card ("love it") both reconfirmed — leave both alone.** One follow-up on the submit/vote card only: the turnout line at the bottom ("1 of 20 users voted (5%)") was still misleading — it's actually "1 of 20 voted **yes**," and "we're not keeping track of no's and we don't really want/need to." Reworded (again, this line keeps getting revisited) to a plain count with no denominator/percent: `"N vote(s) \(is/are) in"` — same underlying `daily.yesterdayUniqueVoterCount` number as before, wording-only change, condition simplified to just `!daily.yesterdayEntries.isEmpty` (dropped the `daily.totalUserCount > 0` guard along with the now-unused percent/denominator). (`TodayTab.swift`, `ctaSection`)
- **Hero card (#1) made deliberately dark, not just "a different tint."** Feedback: the card's previous light yellow/purple gradient sat at roughly the same *brightness* as a typical doodle photo (not the same hue — the brightness), so the card and the framed image visually blended into each other instead of reading as separate objects, like a plaque merging into the wall behind it. Since a doodle's own color palette varies completely from day to day, hue-matching the card to "whatever's popular" isn't a reliable fix, but going genuinely dark is — a near-black card will contrast against nearly any bright/colorful doodle, the way a gallery wall contrasts with the art on it. Background changed from `Color.yellow.opacity(0.24)/Color.purple.opacity(0.16)` to a fixed dark plum-to-near-black `LinearGradient` (`Color(red: 0.14, green: 0.05, blue: 0.14)` → `Color(red: 0.06, green: 0.03, blue: 0.08)`) — kept a faint plum undertone rather than pure black/gray, to stay consistent with this card's existing purple accents (the "Doodle of the Day" `BannerLabel`, the ribbon's purple tail).
  - **Two child views on this card still assumed a light background and had to be fixed alongside it.** The date pill under the banner used `Color(UIColor.secondarySystemBackground)` + `.foregroundColor(.secondary)` (dynamic system colors, fine on a light card, illegible/washed-out on a fixed dark one) — switched to an explicit cream pill + dark-ink text (`Color(red: 0.94, green: 0.87, blue: 0.68)` / `Color(red: 0.32, green: 0.20, blue: 0.09)`, the same parchment/ink pairing as `SubjectPlacard`, so the two "frame label" elements read as a matched family). The artist row's `DailyAvatarRow(entry: summary.winner)` defaults to `.primary` text (non-compact mode) — black in light mode, invisible against the new dark card. Rather than force this card to use `compact: true` (which also shrinks the avatar/font size, not just the color), `DailyAvatarRow` gained a new `textColor: Color? = nil` parameter that overrides the compact-linked default when set; every other existing call site is unaffected (`nil` preserves old behavior exactly), and the hero card now passes `textColor: .white`.
- **New: `OrnateGoldFrame` / `ScallopRingShape` — an elaborated, Bezier-curve version of the frame around the hero image specifically.** Per direct request ("make the inner frame... a bit more elaborate... some kind of bezier curve with the gold gradient") — scoped to *only* the hero image's own frame (card #1's canvas edge), not any card-level bezel; those stay as plain `GradientFrame` per the "leave 2 and 3 (and this card's own outer border) alone" feedback pattern established earlier in this pass.
  - **`ScallopRingShape: Shape`** traces the same rounded-rect perimeter `GradientFrame` rides, but instead of flat concentric offsets, walks it as 8 segments (top edge → corner arc → right edge → corner arc → ...) computing point + outward unit normal at each arc-length position from first principles (no SwiftUI primitive does this for a "wavy rounded rect"). Anchor points are sampled every half-`wavelength` and alternately pushed out/in along the local normal (peak/trough), then joined with real cubic Bezier curves (`Path.addCurve`) whose control points extend along each anchor's local tangent (tangent = normal rotated 90°, verified to match the loop's clockwise travel direction at every one of the 8 segments) — producing a smooth rope-twist/fluted molding profile instead of a flat band.
  - **`OrnateGoldFrame: View`** layers a `ScallopRingShape` (filled with a light→dark→light→dark diagonal gold gradient, a thin darker stroke outline, and a small drop shadow for depth) on top of a normal `GradientFrame` underneath — the plain frame is kept, not replaced, so the geometrically-correct bevel shading (and the `innerEdgeColor` fix above) still does its job; the scallop reads as ornamental trim riding on top of it, sized to `thickness * 0.85` / `amplitude: thickness * 0.22` so it stays within the band rather than poking past either edge.
  - Wired in at the hero image's frame call site only (`OrnateGoldFrame(cornerRadius: 20, innerEdgeColor: ...)`, replacing the plain `GradientFrame` that was there), same `innerEdgeColor` dark-bronze value as before.
  - **Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this pass; the geometry is correct by construction/code review (each segment's point/normal/tangent formula checked by hand against known values at segment boundaries), but an actual scalloped gold ring riding a bevel frame is exactly the kind of thing that needs a look on a real screen before calling it done.
- **Confirmed on device: "nailed it" on the gold zigzag edge and gradient on black — but the doodle itself was missing.** Real bug, not a style nit: `OrnateGoldFrame` used `.fill(...)` on `ScallopRingShape`. `ScallopRingShape.path(in:)` produces a single closed contour (the wavy centerline loop, `closeSubpath()`'d at the end) — it was never an outer+inner annulus with a hole cut out. Filling a single closed contour paints the *entire* area it encloses, and since that contour rides close to the full inset rectangle (just with a small ripple), the fill painted almost the whole photo area solid, hiding the doodle underneath completely — the "zigzag edge" that looked great was actually the *outer boundary* of that solid fill, not a thin decorative ring. **Fixed:** changed `.fill(gradient)` to `.stroke(gradient, style: StrokeStyle(lineWidth: thickness * 0.6, lineCap: .round, lineJoin: .round))` — a stroke paints only a fixed-width ribbon following the path, not the area it encloses, so everything inside it (the actual doodle image, still rendered by the `RetryAsyncImage`/`GradientFrame` layers underneath) is untouched. The thin dark "seam" overlay (previously `.stroke(darkColor.shaded(-0.35), lineWidth: 0.75)`) was already correctly using `.stroke`, just needed its own `StrokeStyle` for matching line caps/joins — now reads as a rope-twist seam down the center of the gold ribbon rather than an outline. (`TodayTab.swift`, `OrnateGoldFrame`)
- **Real bug found once the doodle was visible again: the sides of the hero image were cropped, not showing the complete doodle.** `RetryAsyncImage`'s success case renders `img.resizable().aspectRatio(contentMode: contentMode)`, defaulting `contentMode` to `.fill` — the hero call site never overrode this, so it was always cropping. The outer `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` chained onto the *view* only shapes the overall bounding box into a square; it has no effect on `RetryAsyncImage`'s own internal content mode, so a non-square doodle (canvas size varies by device — see `canvasSize`/`GeometryReader` note elsewhere in this doc) was being center-cropped to fill that square, cutting off whatever didn't fit. **Fixed:** pass `contentMode: .fit` explicitly at the hero card's call site (`RetryAsyncImage(url: ..., contentMode: .fit)`), so the complete doodle letterboxes inside the square instead of being cropped. Added a `.background(Color(red: 0.06, green: 0.03, blue: 0.08))` (the same dark tone as the card itself) directly behind it so any letterbox gap reads as an intentional "matte" — like the mat board around art in a real picture frame — rather than a transparency gap. This reverses an earlier documented decision ("Confirmed: hero image keeps cropping to fill, not letterboxed") — revisited and changed per direct request once the frame's other issues were fixed and cropping became the next visible problem. Other `RetryAsyncImage` call sites (grid thumbnails in `GalleryTab.swift`/`ProfileView.swift`, `PastWinnerRow`'s small thumbnail) are untouched — cropping to fill is still correct for small square grid cells, this was specifically about the large hero showcase image.
- **Added: slow rotating "shine" highlight on the hero frame — "what's missing... how about a slow moving glimmer... reflecting a flashlight or light source im moving around."** `OrnateGoldFrame` gained `@State private var shimmerAngle: Double = 0`, driving a `RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius:).stroke(AngularGradient(...))` overlay: a narrow bright band (`Color.white.opacity(0.55)`) at one position around the ring, transparent everywhere else, with `startAngle`/`endAngle` both offset by `shimmerAngle` and animated from 0→360° on a `.linear(duration: 8).repeatForever(autoreverses: false)` loop started in `.onAppear`. Deliberately animates the gradient's angle values directly rather than `.rotationEffect`-ing the whole view — a rounded *rectangle* isn't rotationally symmetric, so spinning the entire view would visibly swing the corners out of alignment with the frame underneath; only the highlight's position within the gradient needs to move, not the ring's actual geometry. `.blendMode(.screen)` used so the highlight only ever *adds* brightness (reads as a glint of light) rather than tinting/darkening the gold underneath. Tuned narrow + low-opacity + slow (8s per revolution) specifically to stay "subtle and tasteful," not read as a spinner/loading indicator.
- **Card #2 ("Today's Challenge") lightened.** Once card #1 went near-black (see above), card #2's original deep indigo (`Color(red: 0.24, green: 0.10, blue: 0.38)` → `Color(red: 0.13, green: 0.06, blue: 0.24)`) sat at close to the same brightness, so the two dark cards blended together instead of reading as distinct zones, and it muted the SUBMIT!/VOTE! buttons sitting on top of it. Brightened to `Color(red: 0.40, green: 0.20, blue: 0.58)` → `Color(red: 0.26, green: 0.13, blue: 0.42)` — same purple/violet jewel-tone identity, noticeably lighter, giving the buttons more contrast to stand out against. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as the rest of this pass.
- **Real bug found once the doodle was visible again: the sides of the hero image were cropped, not showing the complete doodle.** `RetryAsyncImage`'s success case renders `img.resizable().aspectRatio(contentMode: contentMode)`, defaulting `contentMode` to `.fill` — the hero call site never overrode this, so it was always cropping. The outer `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` chained onto the *view* only shapes the overall bounding box into a square; it has no effect on `RetryAsyncImage`'s own internal content mode, so a non-square doodle (canvas size varies by device — see `canvasSize`/`GeometryReader` note elsewhere in this doc) was being center-cropped to fill that square, cutting off whatever didn't fit. **Fixed (round one):** pass `contentMode: .fit` explicitly at the hero card's call site (`RetryAsyncImage(url: ..., contentMode: .fit)`), so the complete doodle letterboxes inside the square instead of being cropped. Added a `.background(Color(red: 0.06, green: 0.03, blue: 0.08))` (the same dark tone as the card itself) directly behind it so any letterbox gap reads as an intentional "matte" — like the mat board around art in a real picture frame — rather than a transparency gap. This reverses an earlier documented decision ("Confirmed: hero image keeps cropping to fill, not letterboxed") — revisited and changed per direct request once the frame's other issues were fixed and cropping became the next visible problem. Other `RetryAsyncImage` call sites (grid thumbnails in `GalleryTab.swift`/`ProfileView.swift`, `PastWinnerRow`'s small thumbnail) are untouched — cropping to fill is still correct for small square grid cells, this was specifically about the large hero showcase image.
  - **Round two, reported back: "the frame is wider than the canvas... a black strip on either side... inside the frame area."** Round one's `.fit` fix stopped the *cropping*, but the outer container was still forced into a fixed 1:1 square via `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` on the container itself — so a non-square doodle now showed uncropped, but letterboxed inside that square, with the matte color filling the gap on either side, inside the gold frame. Not what was wanted: the frame itself should hug the doodle's real shape, not stay a static square with matte bars. **Fixed:** removed the outer `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` entirely — with only `.frame(maxWidth: 380)` constraining width, `img.resizable().aspectRatio(contentMode: .fit)` (inside `RetryAsyncImage`) now sizes the whole view to the doodle's own real aspect ratio within that width, so the `GeometryReader`-sized `OrnateGoldFrame` overlay hugs the actual doodle rectangle exactly — no matte, no bars, for any doodle shape. Added `.aspectRatio(1, contentMode: .fit)` to `RetryAsyncImage`'s own `.failure`/loading-placeholder `ZStack`s (`GalleryTab.swift`) so those two transient states (before any real image/aspect ratio is known) still get a sane square footprint — harmless everywhere else, since every other `RetryAsyncImage` call site already imposes its own fixed `.frame(width:height:)` externally, which always wins regardless.
- **Shimmer highlight redesigned — first version looked like "a rat/rodent... creeping around the outside," not a shine.** The original shimmer (`RoundedRectangle.stroke(AngularGradient(...))`, a narrow bright band with `startAngle`/`endAngle` rotating via `shimmerAngle`) put one small bright dot in motion along the ring's *perimeter* — technically "moving," but read as a single point of light crawling around the edge rather than the whole frame catching light. Direct feedback: **"i was picturing the whole frame changing because you would move the points where the gradients would be marked."** Redesigned around that exact idea: `OrnateGoldFrame` dropped the separate `AngularGradient` overlay entirely, and instead the gold ribbon's own `LinearGradient` (previously a static `.topLeading`→`.bottomTrailing` diagonal) now has its `startPoint`/`endPoint` computed by a new `shimmerPoint(_:)` helper — two opposite points on a circle centered on the frame, `shimmerAngle` (still animating 0→360° on the same 8s linear repeat-forever loop) apart. As `shimmerAngle` advances, the *direction* the light→dark→light bands run in sweeps slowly around the whole ribbon at once — like turning a gold object under a fixed light source — rather than a single highlight orbiting the outside. The thin dark rope-seam overlay stroke is deliberately left un-animated, so the rotating light/dark bands have a fixed reference line to visibly sweep across. (`TodayTab.swift`, `OrnateGoldFrame`)
- **Card #1 background changed to a plain black-to-gray vertical gradient, per direct request — "black to a gray at bottom, as if light is being shined on the pic."** Replaced the diagonal plum-to-near-black gradient (`Color(red: 0.14, green: 0.05, blue: 0.14)` → `Color(red: 0.06, green: 0.03, blue: 0.08)`, `.topLeading`→`.bottomTrailing`) with a neutral vertical one (`Color.black` → `Color(white: 0.22)`, `.top`→`.bottom`) — reads more like directional stage lighting than the plum diagonal did, and sidesteps any future concern about the card's own hue clashing with a doodle's colors, since it's neutral now. Still dark at the bottom (`white: 0.22`, not a bright wash) — subtle, not a spotlight. The hero image's own `.background` matte color (`Color(red: 0.06, green: 0.03, blue: 0.08)`, added for the loading-placeholder/letterbox fix above) was left as-is rather than re-matched to the new gradient — it's close enough to the card's own near-black top region where the image actually sits, and this was a request about the *card's* background specifically, not the matte.
- **Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this pass; all three of the above (the aspect-ratio fix, the redesigned whole-frame shimmer, the black-to-gray card) are correct by code review only.
- **Reported: no shimmer animation visible at all, and the card #1 gradient not visibly reading as a gradient either.** Two separate issues:
  - **Shimmer:** the `@State private var shimmerAngle` + `withAnimation(.linear(duration: 8).repeatForever(...))` approach from the redesign above apparently never actually produced visible motion. Root cause (SwiftUI implicit-animation limitation): `withAnimation` reliably interpolates properties that are part of a view's recognized `Animatable` data — offsets, opacity, plain numeric frame/rotation modifiers — but a `UnitPoint` fed into a `ShapeStyle` parameter like `LinearGradient`'s `startPoint`/`endPoint` isn't guaranteed to be one of those; the state change can just jump with nothing rendered in between. **Fixed:** replaced the `@State`/`withAnimation` mechanism entirely with `TimelineView(.animation)`, which ticks on every display refresh and recomputes the shimmer angle directly from `context.date` (elapsed time modulo an 8-second period) rather than relying on SwiftUI to interpolate anything implicitly — guaranteed continuous motion regardless of gradient-animatability questions. This is the same pattern `countdownStrip` elsewhere in this file already uses (`TimelineView(.periodic(...))` instead of a manual `Timer` + `@State`) for exactly this class of problem — continuously-updating visuals should drive themselves from a time source, not from a single animated state transition. (`TodayTab.swift`, `OrnateGoldFrame`)
  - **Card #1 gradient:** code-reviewed and confirmed present and correctly wired (`LinearGradient(colors: [Color.black, Color(white: 0.22)], startPoint: .top, endPoint: .bottom)` on the card's `.background`) — not a missing-code bug. Bumped the bottom stop from `white: 0.22` to `white: 0.4` regardless, since the original value may simply have been too close to black to read as a gradient, especially now that the framed doodle (after the aspect-ratio fix above) fills most of the card's height and leaves little bare background exposed to show it off. A stale build remains a possible explanation too, given how many changes have landed on this screen this session, but the shimmer fix above was a genuine bug independent of that.
- **Shimmer asked to slow down and given wandering speed/direction instead of a steady clockwise sweep.** Per direct feedback: "randomize when it changes direction and its speed." Replaced the simple `(elapsed mod period)/period × 360` linear formula with `shimmerAngle(at:)`, the closed-form integral of a wandering *angular velocity* built from three sine waves at mutually unrelated frequencies (periods ≈ 80s/145s/250s): `velocity(t) = 7·sin(0.079t+0.4) + 5·sin(0.043t+2.6) + 4·sin(0.025t+5.1)`. Summing sines with unrelated periods means their combined value wanders unpredictably over a normal viewing session — sometimes near zero (the shimmer pauses), sometimes negative (reverses direction for a while), peak ≈16°/s (well under the old constant 45°/s, satisfying "slow it down" too) — without ever being genuinely random, which would jitter/stutter frame to frame instead of gliding. Each `a·sin(w·t+p)` term integrates in closed form to `-(a/w)·cos(w·t+p)`, so the *angle* itself (not just its rate of change) is still a pure function of elapsed time alone — no accumulated state, drops straight into `TimelineView`'s per-frame recomputation exactly like the old formula did. **Verified numerically** (not just by eye): a Python script confirmed the closed-form angle's numerical derivative matches the stated velocity formula exactly at several sample times, and that direction reverses (11 times over a simulated 10-minute span) with peak |velocity| ≈14°/s as expected. (`TodayTab.swift`, `OrnateGoldFrame.shimmerAngle(at:)`)
- **Reported again: still zero visible shimmer, even after the `TimelineView` fix above — so that fix's claim of "shimmer now visibly animates" was wrong.** Two back-to-back reports of no visible motion (before *and* after switching from `withAnimation` to `TimelineView`) pointed at something more fundamental than "too slow to notice": most likely that per-frame changes to a `ShapeStyle`'s own init parameters (`LinearGradient`'s `startPoint`/`endPoint`, fed a freshly-computed `UnitPoint` every tick) simply aren't reliably picked up by SwiftUI's renderer at all, regardless of how the new value is produced or how it's scheduled. **Rebuilt on a completely different, far more standard mechanism:** `.rotationEffect` driven by a `TimelineView`-sourced angle is the textbook pattern behind every SwiftUI "analog clock hand" example. Instead of rotating the *gradient's own coordinates*, `OrnateGoldFrame` now rotates a plain oversized `Rectangle` (filled with a fixed-direction gold gradient, scaled 1.8× so its corners stay covered at any angle) via `.rotationEffect(.degrees(angle))`, then `.mask()`s it down to just `ribbonShape`'s stroked outline. The ring's actual geometry (the mask) never rotates — only the gradient-colored rectangle visible through it does — so this sidesteps both the original "rounded-rect corners swinging out of alignment" concern (which ruled out rotating the whole shape) and the apparent non-animating-`ShapeStyle`-parameter issue. `ribbonShape` (previously duplicated 3×) was factored into a small computed property since the ring shape is now shared by the mask, the dark center seam, and the shadow. The dead `shimmerPoint(_:)` helper from the previous attempt was deleted outright — same-session, never-shipped code, not an established call site worth preserving. Same standing caveat as everything else in this pass: not yet visually confirmed on device, but this rests on a fundamentally more battle-tested SwiftUI mechanism than either of the previous two attempts. (`TodayTab.swift`, `OrnateGoldFrame`)
- **Reported yet again: "no frame animation" on the `.rotationEffect`+`.mask()` rebuild too — and the diagnosis above was wrong.** Direct correction that reframed the whole investigation: **"3 versions ago it was working fine. it was just a matter of implementing variable speed and randomly timed changes in direction. then the animation stopped."** This means the `TimelineView` + `shimmerPoint(angle)` → `LinearGradient` mechanism (the version right after the first "not seeing any shimmer" fix, using a *simple* linear `(elapsed mod 8s)/8s × 360°` angle) had in fact been visually confirmed working on device — "it goes steady in a clockwise motion at a steady speed" was direct positive confirmation of real motion, not a symptom report. The "`ShapeStyle` params don't animate" theory above, and the resulting `.rotationEffect`+`.mask()` rebuild built on that theory, were therefore chasing the wrong cause. **Reverted:** `OrnateGoldFrame` is back on the proven `shimmerPoint(angle)` → `LinearGradient(startPoint:endPoint:)` mechanism (the `.rotationEffect`/`.mask`/oversized-`Rectangle` approach removed, `shimmerPoint(_:)` restored). The actual suspected culprit for the break is the *other* change made in the same edit as "randomize speed and direction": swapping the angle function's input from `elapsed.truncatingRemainder(dividingBy: 8)` (always a small number, 0–8) to the raw `context.date.timeIntervalSinceReferenceDate` (a huge number — reference date is Jan 1, 2001, so as of 2026 this is ~8×10⁸ seconds) fed directly into `cos()` inside the new `shimmerAngle(at:)`. Fixed by adding `@State private var startTime: Date?`, captured once via `.onAppear` the first time the view renders, so `elapsed` is measured as "seconds since this card appeared" — small numbers again, matching the last known-working version's magnitude — rather than "seconds since the year 2001." The wandering-speed sine-sum formula itself is unchanged; only its time input changed. **Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this pass, but this is now built directly on the specific checkpoint the user identified as the last one that actually worked, rather than a fourth new theory.
- **Reported again: "still no animation" — even the revert above, back onto the exact mechanism identified as previously working, produced zero motion.** This is a meaningful escalation: reverting faithfully to a "confirmed working" checkpoint and still seeing nothing suggests the bug isn't in the shimmer's own formula/mechanism at all — something about how this specific call site composes now (the `GeometryReader` removed during the aspect-ratio fix, mask/animation interaction, or view-identity churn from `heroWinnerCard` re-rendering) is the more likely suspect. Rather than tweak the angle math a fourth time, **`OrnateGoldFrame` was split into two independent concerns:** (1) the gold ribbon itself is now fully static (fixed diagonal gradient, zero animation dependency) so the frame can never look broken/blank even if the animated layer fails again; (2) the moving highlight is its own separate, deliberately dead-simple layer — a plain `Rectangle` swept left-to-right via `.offset(x:)` (computed from `context.date.timeIntervalSinceReferenceDate` mod a 6s period, linear, no wandering-speed formula for now), masked to the ribbon's stroked outline. `.offset(x:)` on a plain view is the single most standard, battle-tested continuous-motion technique in SwiftUI — the same mechanism behind every "shimmer skeleton loader" tutorial — deliberately avoiding both previously-failed mechanisms (`ShapeStyle` gradient-point params, `.rotationEffect`+`.mask` on an oversized rectangle). The wandering-speed/randomized-direction refinement is intentionally *not* reapplied yet — priority is confirming ANY visible motion renders at this call site before layering that nuance back on. **If this still doesn't animate, the next step is investigating `heroWinnerCard`'s surrounding view identity/composition, not `OrnateGoldFrame` in isolation again** — three different internal mechanisms failing in a row (including one independently confirmed working elsewhere) points away from the shimmer code itself.
- **Backup made before the next round: `TodayTab.swift.bak`** (plain copy, not `.swift` extension so Xcode's folder-synced target doesn't pick it up as a duplicate/conflicting source file) sits alongside `TodayTab.swift` on disk — a snapshot taken right before the fix below, per direct request ("we should have made a backup") after this many consecutive shimmer rewrites. Not wired into the build or referenced anywhere; purely a manual restore point. Safe to delete once the shimmer is confirmed working and stable.
- **Reported: the offset-sweep rebuild did show *something* — "this white thing drop vertically in the middle of the canvas" — but the frame also "gets cut off by the bottom," i.e. rendered too tall.** Real, findable bug (not another "chase a new theory" situation): the shimmer's `Rectangle` is deliberately oversized (`height: geo.size.height * 2`, so it stays fully covering the ribbon at any rotation/slide position), but nothing was clamping that back down afterward. `.rotationEffect`/`.offset` don't change a view's *reported layout size* — only `.frame()` does — so this branch was reporting a layout size of `geo.size.height * 2` up to its parent `ZStack`, which sizes itself to its single largest child. That inflated the whole card's effective height (the "cut off at the bottom" symptom — something further up the hierarchy was clipping the overflow), and the oversized/rotated rectangle's own coordinate space no longer lined up with `ribbonShape`'s true position within that inflated box, so `.mask()` let a stray unmasked streak of the highlight show through in the middle instead of confining it to the ring outline (the "white thing drop vertically" symptom). **Fixed:** added `.frame(width: geo.size.width, height: geo.size.height).clipped()` on the shimmer branch, applied *before* `.mask(...)` — forces this branch's reported and visual size down to exactly the intended card size regardless of the oversized child inside it, and hard-clips any overflow right here rather than letting it leak out and get clipped unpredictably somewhere else. The oversized rectangle can still rotate/slide freely *within* that now-fixed box. Not yet visually confirmed on device.
- **Confirmed working on device — first real success for the animation.** The layout fix above resolved both symptoms; the sweep now visibly animates without breaking the card layout. Follow-up feedback: "the animated areas are a bit too white" — the highlight's `Color.white.opacity(0.9)` was swapped for a warm pale gold at much lower opacity (`Color(red: 1.0, green: 0.95, blue: 0.78).opacity(0.45)`), so it reads as a glint catching the gold rather than a bright white bar. Then: "make the shiny area thats animating bigger" — the sweeping rectangle's width was widened from `thickness * 1.5` to `thickness * 5`.
- **Direct side-by-side comparison (old iPhone build vs. new iPad build, screenshots) led to a style verdict, not a bug report: the wide horizontal sweep "looks too much like it's trying too hard."** The old build (still running an earlier shimmer version on Eddie's iPhone) reads "like a ball" of light — a single round glint that looks like a flashlight pointed at one spot on the frame. The new wide-band sweep instead makes a whole vertical slice of the frame look "discolored" as it passes — because a rectangle swept in a straight horizontal line and masked to a *ring* shape doesn't trace the ring's own path; it lights up wherever the rectangle happens to cross the ring at that x position (potentially the top and bottom edges at once), which reads as disconnected patches rather than one traveling point of light. **Rebuilt a fourth time using `.trim(from:to:)`** — the standard SwiftUI technique for animating a moving segment along a `Shape`'s own path (the same mechanism behind loading-spinner tutorials), instead of an independent shape that merely overlaps the ring.
