A short arc (5% of the perimeter) of `ribbonShape`'s own path is stroked in a warm near-white color and blurred for softness (`thickness * 0.35` radius) + `.blendMode(.screen)`; `from`/`to` both slide from 0→1 over a 7-second loop (same `context.date.timeIntervalSinceReferenceDate mod period` time source already proven to reliably drive visible motion at this exact call site, from the offset-sweep round above — de-risking whether `TimelineView` itself ticks here), with an explicit wraparound case (splits into two trims — tail of this lap + head of the next) so the glint doesn't pop when crossing the path's start/end seam. Since `.trim` operates in the shape's own normalized coordinate space, this is geometrically guaranteed to always sit exactly on the ring itself, all 4 sides and corners, unlike the previous independent-rectangle approaches — closer to the "ball of light circling the frame" that was confirmed to read well. The outer `GeometryReader` (no longer needed — nothing in this version needs pixel dimensions) was removed for simplicity. Not yet visually confirmed on device.
- **Confirmed animating and tracing the ring correctly, but reported as "a white worm crawling around the perim of the frame."** A single `.trim()` segment stroked in one uniform (near-opaque, near-white) color has a hard, flat-brightness fill along its whole length — reads as a painted-on stripe/snake, not a glowing point, regardless of the blur radius. Real point-source glints need brightness to fall off from a bright center outward, which a single solid-color stroke can't express on its own. **Added `glintLayer(center:halfLength:opacity:lineWidth:baseColor:)`** — a small helper that strokes one segment of `ribbonShape`'s path centered on a shared `center` position (0...1, with the same start/end wraparound handling as before, now expressed as `center ± halfLength`). The shimmer now layers 3 of these concentric rings at the same moving center — wide and very faint (`halfLength 0.05, opacity 0.10`), medium (`0.022, 0.30`), and short and bright (`0.007, 0.9`) — faking a radial glow falloff along the ribbon's inherently 1-D path. The brightness gradient between the three rings, not any single one of them, is what reads as a rounded ball of light rather than a flat-colored worm.
- **Confirmed better, but "still a bit of white in the middle... make that a bit darker gold."** `glintLayer` gained a `baseColor` parameter (previously hardcoded to the same near-white for all 3 layers); the bright core layer now uses an actual gold (`Color(red: 0.95, green: 0.72, blue: 0.25)`) instead of near-white (`1.0, 0.97, 0.85`), while the two faint outer layers keep a pale warm tone (`1.0, 0.95, 0.78`) — hue barely reads on those anyway given how transparent they are, so only the visible bright center needed to change.
- **Backup made again before the next round: `TodayTab.swift.bak2`** (alongside the earlier `TodayTab.swift.bak`, both plain copies, neither `.swift`-extended so Xcode's folder sync won't compile them) — per "let's make a backup of what we have and continue," since this next round bundles several changes at once (card color rework + a bigger shimmer redesign) and Eddie wanted a restore point before diving in.
- **Card #1 and #2 backgrounds switched from black/gray and purple to a shared dark-to-medium blue pair, reversed between the two cards.** Per direct request, replacing the black-to-gray hero card gradient and the purple `submitVoteCard` gradient with the same two blues (`Color(red: 0.03, green: 0.07, blue: 0.18)` darkest, `Color(red: 0.15, green: 0.35, blue: 0.62)` medium) — hero card goes darkest-to-medium top-to-bottom, `submitVoteCard` goes medium-to-darkest top-to-bottom (the reverse), and `submitVoteCard`'s gradient direction was changed from diagonal (`.topLeading`/`.bottomTrailing`) to vertical (`.top`/`.bottom`) to match the hero card's own direction. The intent (Eddie's words): "hoping this gives an illusion of a source pointing at the doodle but overflowing onto the 2nd card" — the two gradients now meet at the seam between the cards at the same medium-blue value and both fade to the darkest blue moving away from that seam (up in card #1, down in card #2), reading as one light source brightest between the two cards. Text/turnout colors inside `submitVoteCard` were already explicit white/opacity values from the earlier dark-background pass and needed no changes for contrast against the new blue.
- **Shimmer redesigned again, following a specific diagnosis from direct side-by-side comparison of an old iPhone build vs. the current build:** "it almost looks like the area travelling around is actually darker in the center than the gold in the frame... so it gives it this distortion thing that looks more realistic... the travelling area is darker in the middle and a tad lighter than the actual frame on the outside." This is a fundamentally different look from the bright-center "glowing ball" built in the previous round (3 concentric rings all *brighter* than the base ribbon) — more like a dent/emboss catching light, dark in the middle with a lighter rim flanking both sides. **New `glintGroup(center:)`** draws a wider, lighter halo first, then a narrower, genuinely darker-than-`darkColor` core on top — both using plain alpha compositing (no `.blendMode(.screen)`, which can only ever lighten and therefore can't produce a dark core at all). Since the core is narrower than the halo, a rim of the lighter halo shows through on both sides once the dark core is layered over it.
- **Added a second, counter-traveling glint, and reintroduced speed randomization** — both per direct request ("it needs to be more random and have another one going counter clockwise"). **New `wanderingPosition(at:direction:phaseOffset:)`** computes a closed-form looping position (0...1) as the integral of a constant directional bias (`+1/7` for clockwise, `-1/7` for counter-clockwise — same ~7s/lap pace as before) plus three small sine terms at unrelated frequencies, deliberately kept well under the bias in amplitude so velocity varies but never actually reaches zero or reverses sign — avoids the risk of a fully-random reversing formula being hard to reason about, while still giving an organically varying speed. `phaseOffset` decorrelates the two glints (`0` and `1.7`) so they don't speed up/slow down in lockstep. Both glints now run simultaneously via two `glintGroup` calls in the same `TimelineView`, one per direction. This reuses the same closed-form-integral-of-a-sine-sum technique from an earlier (reportedly non-animating) attempt, but that attempt's failure was ultimately traced to the *rendering* mechanism it was paired with (`LinearGradient` start/end points, later `.rotationEffect`+`.mask`), not the math itself — the current `.trim()`-based approach has already been confirmed working with a similarly huge `context.date.timeIntervalSinceReferenceDate` value in the plain single-glint version, so reintroducing this formula on top of `.trim()` is expected to be safe. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as this whole pass.
- **Voting Booth Yes/No buttons recolored** — `voteButtons(for:)` (`TodayTab.swift`) changed from plain gray (No) / purple-or-green (Yes) to a consistent red (No) and green (Yes) either way, per direct request ("no is a light or high opacity red, and yes is a light green"). Same selected/unselected dimming pattern as before (the currently-held answer shows at full color, the other dims to 0.35 opacity) — just recolored, no logic change: No uses `Color(red: 0.90, green: 0.35, blue: 0.35)`, Yes originally used `Color(red: 0.40, green: 0.80, blue: 0.45)`.
- **Yes button reported "way too pale... looks like it's disabled" next to the No button's "perfect off red."** The green's R/B channels (0.40/0.45) weren't pulled down as far below its dominant G channel (0.80) as the red's R/B-vs-dominant-channel ratio (0.90 dominant vs 0.35/0.35) — so it read as pastel/washed out rather than a punchy, equally-saturated counterpart. Fixed by pulling R/B down further to `Color(red: 0.20, green: 0.75, blue: 0.30)` — same dimming pattern (0.35 opacity when not selected) unchanged, just a more saturated base color.
- **Liked the two-glint animation, but "they are pretty close to white... I thought u were making them dark to light."** Then a much more precise description: the ribbon is visibly built from a row of little scalloped "circles" (exactly what `ScallopRingShape`'s bumps are), and the 2-layer halo+core version read as **3 flat bands** across ~9 visible circles — "3 whitish-gold, 3 darker gold, 3 more whitish-gold" — not a real gradient. The version that looked good had each individual circle progressively darkening toward the center and lightening (not whitening) toward the outer edges — a smooth per-bump gradient, not 3 stepped zones. **Rebuilt using the same technique `GradientFrame` already uses for its own smooth bevel:** `glintGroup` now draws 14 concentric `.trim()` segments (was 2), each shorter than the last, largest-to-smallest so each subsequent shorter one paints over the middle of the one before it — with 14 steps this reads as continuous rather than banded, the same principle behind `GradientFrame`'s 16-ring bevel. Colors interpolate (new `lerpColor` helper, mirroring `GradientFrame.lerp`) from a lightened version of the ribbon's own `lightColor` (edges — a *bit* lighter, deliberately not white) to a darkened version of its own `darkColor` (center), so the glint reads as "this same gold getting darker," not an unrelated white overlay. Blur cut from `thickness * 0.12` to `thickness * 0.03` — heavy blur was smearing the steps into indistinct bands instead of letting each little scalloped bump show its own place in the gradient.
- **Confirmed on device — screenshot showed the smooth per-scallop gradient working as intended.** Two follow-up tweaks from the same screenshot: (1) speed bumped up slightly — `wanderingPosition`'s bias denominator changed from `7.0` to `6.0` (was ~7s/lap on average, now ~6s/lap); (2) `glintGroup`'s gradient direction reversed — center is now the *lighter* gold (`lightColor.shaded(0.15)`) and the outer edge the *darker* gold (`darkColor.shaded(-0.25)`), the opposite of the first version (previously center was dark, edges light). Just swapping which color variable feeds `outerColor` vs. `innerColor`, no structural change.
- **Backup made again: `TodayTab.swift.bak3`** — per "maybe this one is good so I think I should save it," taken right before the color-range change below, since the *structural* approach (14-step smooth per-scallop gradient, two counter-traveling glints) was confirmed working well; only the color range itself needed another pass.
- **Color range narrowed way down — still "too much like 2 trains having a collision... not quite working... maybe it's just not subtle [enough]."** Both prior versions of `glintGroup` pushed *past* the frame's own actual color range in one direction or the other (darker than `darkColor`, or lighter than `lightColor`) — too much contrast against the static ribbon underneath, reading as a separate glowing/dark object rather than a highlight on the same gold. Eddie's own framing, verbatim: picture the frame's tones on a 1(lightest)–10(darkest) scale, where `lightColor`≈g1, `darkColor`≈g10, and the ribbon's own resting tone sits around g5 — the traveling highlight should stay entirely within **g4→g1→g4**, i.e. never darker than "a bit lighter than the frame's own base," never lighter than the frame's own defined lightest gold. Implemented directly: `outerColor` is now g4 (`lerpColor(lightColor, darkColor, 3.0/9.0)`), `innerColor` is g1 (`lightColor` itself, unchanged) — no darkening at all anymore, purely a gentle brightening that peaks at the center and fades back to just-a-bit-lighter-than-base at the edges. Same 14-step gradient/two-glint structure, only the two endpoint colors changed.
- **Shimmer animation abandoned entirely — "lets kill this animation... somebodys trying to tell me something."** After this many rounds (AngularGradient dot → LinearGradient-point rotation → `.rotationEffect`+`.mask` → `.offset`-swept rectangle → `.trim()` single glint → two counter-traveling glints with three different color-range attempts) never landing cleanly, `OrnateGoldFrame` is back to a plain static scalloped gold ribbon — `glintLayer`, `glintGroup`, `wanderingPosition`, and `lerpColor` all removed outright (same-session, never-shipped experimental code, per this codebase's usual convention of deleting rather than orphaning that kind of thing). All 6 `TodayTab.swift.bak*` files from this pass are left on disk as restore points but are no longer needed for anything active. **Card #1/#2's blue background gradient pair is explicitly confirmed as final/liked ("that blue background is perfect") — do not touch.**
- **New idea in its place: light fireworks behind the hero photo, not on the frame.** Discussed reusing fireworks code originally written for a different app ("Feddy") — turned out that code didn't exist (Eddie misremembered; the closest match was in one of "the 6 games," and it was React Native anyway, not portable). **Decided: no fireworks, no replacement animation.** Looking at the static frame fresh on iPhone, both the frame and the blue card backgrounds already read as strong on their own — motion isn't needed to call this card finished. Static is the final decision here, not a placeholder pending a future animation attempt.
- **Today tab visual pass considered complete; wrapped up with a batch of final polish items found during an iPad/iPhone device-pass sweep** (`TodayTab.swift`):
  - **`SubjectPlacard` border thinned** — `2.5pt` → `1.75pt` black stroke, per direct feedback ("a wee bit thinner").
  - **`DailySubmitScreen`'s "already posted" preview fixed** — was a fixed `220×220` square using `RetryAsyncImage`'s default `.fill` contentMode, which cropped every non-square doodle AND left most of the screen bare (~60% blank on iPad, ~50% on iPhone, since this screen has nothing else on it). Fixed the same way as the hero card's own crop fix: `contentMode: .fit` + only a `.frame(maxWidth: 500)` cap, no fixed height, so the real aspect ratio sets the height and the preview actually uses the room available.
  - **Main Today tab CTA colors swapped** — SUBMIT is now always purple (previously flipped to green once posted; the "SUBMITTED ✓" title + checkmark-seal icon already communicate the state change on their own, so the color didn't need to also carry it), VOTE is now green (previously purple).
  - **Voting Booth's Yes button still read as "too pale a green"** even after the previous saturation fix — instead of a third independent tuning attempt, per direct request it now uses the literal same `Color.green` as the main tab's VOTE! button, guaranteeing the two greens in the app are identical rather than two near-matches that can drift apart.
  - **Voting Booth completion page ("You're All Caught Up!") polish** — the line directly under the headline ("You've gone through every doodle...") bumped from 15pt to 19pt, per direct feedback ("we have lots of room"). The "HOW THIS WORKS" explanation paragraph (previously one dense sentence covering blind submission + next-day reveal + results-hidden-until-close all at once) rewritten into 3 short, plain-language beats, one per step of the cycle, per direct request to replace it with "something much more clear."
  - The screens reached by tapping a doodle or artist from the Past Winners section were confirmed fine as-is, no changes needed.
  - **With this batch done, Eddie confirmed the Today tab itself is finished for this release** — the device pass continues screen-by-screen into Gallery, New/Draw, Settings, and Profile next.
- **Voting Booth Yes/No selection indicator redesigned — opacity dimming replaced with a checkmark, post-release live device testing.** Found while doing final live-device testing (a seeded test post with its Firestore date hand-edited to simulate "yesterday"): tapping No, then swiping back to that entry, showed the Yes button in a pale/dimmed green that was still tappable — technically correct (mirrors the existing `entry.isVotedByMe ? fullColor : fullColor.opacity(0.35)` dimming pattern, same as the No button dims when Yes is picked) but per direct feedback, **"in their dimmed states both the no and yes look disabled."** Rather than tune the opacity value again, the whole mechanism was replaced: both buttons in `voteButtons(for:)` now render their background at full, undimmed color always (`Color(red: 0.90, green: 0.35, blue: 0.35)` for No, `Color.green` for Yes — same colors as before, just never dimmed), and a `checkmark` SF Symbol now appears next to whichever label matches `entry.isVotedByMe` (Yes when true, No when false) as the sole indicator of your current pick. Unambiguous, and neither button can be mistaken for disabled. The separate, unrelated `.disabled(isMe || !auth.isSignedIn).opacity(...)` on the whole `HStack` (for "can't vote on your own doodle" / "not signed in") is untouched. (`TodayTab.swift`)
- **Console log cleanup — routine/happy-path `print()` statements removed, error/warning ones kept.** Per direct feedback after reviewing a real console dump ("the ones that print out the artists isnt necessary i dont think... do we really need any of this?"), trimmed the noisy day-to-day chatter across `SnoodleFirebase.swift` and `snoodleApp.swift` while deliberately leaving every `❌`/genuine-`⚠️` diagnostic print in place (those still earn their keep when something's actually broken). Removed: `UserProfileManager.fetchProfiles`'s per-batch "looking up N uncached userIds" / "got N profile docs" / "resolved X → 'username'" (one line per artist resolved — the specific one flagged); `WorldGalleryManager.fetchLikedIds`'s "checking subcollection for N doodles" / "found N liked doodles"; `toggleLike`'s "doodleId=... currentlyLiked=..." and its write-success line (the write-failure print stays); `DailyManager.fetchPastWinners`'s three routine query/result lines ("querying date range...", "N raw doc(s) returned", "N date(s) present..." — its two `⚠️`/`❌` parse-failure and query-error prints stay); and the FCM/APNs happy-path prints in `snoodleApp.swift` ("Requesting notification authorization...", "Authorization result...", "Calling registerForRemoteNotifications", "Watchdog found APNs token after N attempts", "Still legacy token — deleting...", "Fresh FCM token"/"Real APNs-backed FCM token", "didRegisterForRemoteNotificationsWithDeviceToken fired", "FCM token refreshed", "Legacy APA91b token — watchdog will handle it") — kept the actual failure paths (`❌ FCM token error`, `❌ deleteToken error`, `❌ APNs registration FAILED`) and the one real problem signal (`⚠️ Watchdog timed out — APNs token never arrived`), since the FCM/APNs system's happy path is confirmed working and no longer needs to narrate itself every launch.
- **Main Today tab VOTE! button subtitle reworded "votes" → "yes votes."** Same underlying Yes/No ambiguity as the earlier turnout-wording fix (see "Turnout stat wording flagged as misleading" above), just a different call site that had been missed — `voteSubtitle` (`TodayTab.swift`, feeding the CTA button in `ctaSection`) showed e.g. "8 entries · 42 votes," and since a "No" tap writes nothing to Firestore, every one of those 42 is actually a Yes tap. Per direct feedback ("this yes no thing is confusing"), changed to "42 yes votes." Purely a string change — still reads `daily.yesterdayTotalVotes` unmodified.
- **`daily_gallery` reset for launch — July 5, 2026.** After the full iPad/iPhone device pass across all tabs (Today, Gallery, New/Draw, Settings, Profile) turned up nothing else needing changes since 2.6 (aside from the Calendar→Today tab swap), Eddie deleted the entire `daily_gallery` Firestore collection and every file in the `daily_gallery` Storage folder — clearing out all the test/seed data accumulated during this build so Daily Doodle launches with a genuinely clean, real history rather than fabricated content (see "how do we want to release this version, content-wise" discussion above — decided against seeding fake doodles/users; real activity only, starting with Eddie's own account). Confirmed safe beforehand: nothing in `users`, `world_gallery`, or local `SnoodleEntry` records references a `daily_gallery` doc by ID (all the cross-collection reads go the other direction — `daily_gallery` looks up `users` live, never the reverse), and `daily_prompts` is keyed only by date so it's entirely unaffected — the already-seeded subject assignments for today and upcoming days are all still intact, no re-seeding needed. Each doc's `votes` subcollection was recursively deleted along with it via the Firebase Console's collection-delete tool. **This is the point Daily Doodle's real, permanent history begins** — from here on, `daily_gallery` contains only genuine submissions/votes, no test data mixed in.

### Post-2.7-submission — daily_prompts overhaul (build 2, July 5, 2026)

2.7 was already archived and submitted when Eddie decided the existing 102-item `daily_prompts` pool ("sandwich"?!) needed a real redo, not a top-up — see `scripts/seed-daily-prompts.js` above for the general-purpose version of that tool. This section covers what came after: a design conversation about whether object prompts ("draw a cat") are the right call at all, which led to a genuine architecture change. **Eddie's call: stop 2.7, ship this as build 2 instead** — no urgency, but not worth holding back a real improvement either.

- **Moods over objects.** Discussion landed on: object prompts converge (a hundred "cat" drawings mostly look like cats), mood/feeling prompts diverge (a hundred "Chaos" drawings all look different) — and divergence is exactly what makes the blind-reveal swipe-through worth doing. Also more skill-blind: a stick figure nails "Cozy" as honestly as a rendered illustration does. Drafted a mood/feeling word list (Pure Happiness, Chaos, Cozy, Homesick, Déjà Vu, Stage Fright, Mischief, Restlessness, etc. — deliberately skewed toward textured/specific feelings rather than just the 6 basic emotions repeating) as the base pool for ordinary (non-holiday, non-seasonal) days.
- **"No subject at all, just best doodle of the day" — considered and rejected.** Eddie floated dropping the shared theme entirely. Rejected: the shared prompt is doing real work — the reveal is fun because everyone hit the *same* constraint and produced wildly different results (the same trick Wordle runs), not just because good doodles exist. Removing it would also mean ripping out already-shipped UI (`SubjectPlacard`, the "Today's Subject" strip, the countdown framing) for a real product downgrade, not a simplification.
- **Holidays, then a full 365-day calendar.** Once holidays came up as their own category, Eddie's next idea: do this for *every* day of the year, not just ~20 named holidays — non-holiday days get something seasonally relevant (Snow in January, not July; concrete seasonal objects are fine here even though the general pool skews mood-based, since "Popsicle" in July carries its own charm a generic noun doesn't) — and since it's a fixed calendar keyed by *year*, the same subject recurs every year automatically ("a 2nd chance at winning Christmas Day"). Confirmed as the direction (full 365, hand-picked, not holidays-only-with-random-gaps).
  - Real holiday dates for the 400-day horizon (today, July 5 2026, through ~Aug 9 2027) were computed programmatically (Python, `dateutil.easter` for Easter, manual "nth weekday of month" math for the rest) rather than recalled from memory, specifically because these are real dates going into production Firestore docs — got exact 2026/2027 dates for Labor Day, Halloween, Thanksgiving, Christmas Eve/Day, New Year's Eve/Day, MLK Day, Groundhog Day, Valentine's, Presidents Day, St. Patrick's, Easter, April Fools, Earth Day, Cinco de Mayo, Mother's/Father's Day, Memorial Day, Flag Day, and Independence Day.
  - **July drafted as the pilot month** (31 entries, July 4th pinned to Fireworks) to calibrate style before grinding through the other 11 months — reviewed and approved as-is ("you are dead on!! do it!!"). The other 11 months are not yet drafted — see Outstanding Items.
- **New script: `scripts/seed-calendar-prompts.js`** — separate from the general-purpose `seed-daily-prompts.js` above (that one shuffles a flat pool with no regard to calendar date; this one does exact MM-DD → subject lookups so holidays land on their real date). For each date in the horizon, computes MM-DD, looks it up, and writes `daily_prompts/{YYYY-MM-DD}` **only** if that MM-DD is in the map; every other date is left completely untouched (no deletion of the collection needed), so the app's existing fallback (or whatever the old flat-pool seeding already wrote there) keeps covering any month not yet drafted. Same "never touch today or the past" rule as the general script. Add more months to the calendar and re-run any time — safe to re-run repeatedly, it just overwrites the same matched dates again.
  - **Calendar data split out of the script into `scripts/daily-prompts-calendar.json`**, a plain `{"MM-DD": [subject, category]}` file sitting right next to the script — prompted by Eddie asking where the list actually lived, wanting to see the whole thing directly rather than dig through JS. The script now just `require()`s it; no logic changed by the split.
  - **Default horizon fixed to stop at Dec 31 of the current year, not a flat `--days=400`.** Caught by Eddie noticing the August seed run also wrote a chunk of *next* July/August (2027) and asking, correctly, why any future year needs writing at all given `fetchSubject(for:)`'s year-fallback (see above) already makes 2027+ inherit from this year automatically with zero extra writes. The 400-day default was a leftover from before that fallback existed — genuinely redundant now, and confusing to look at besides (2027 showed up "half-seeded" up to whatever date the fixed 400-day window happened to end on, which looked broken but wasn't). Fixed: default horizon is now computed as "days remaining in the current calendar year" (`daysRemainingInYear()`), so the script only ever writes the current year by default. `--days=N` still exists as an explicit override for the rare case of deliberately reaching further (e.g. a one-off future-date override), but is no longer the default behavior. The already-written 2027 entries from the old 400-day runs were left in place rather than cleaned up — harmless duplicates, same values either way, purely cosmetic to remove.
  - **Manually patched July 1–5, 2026** via Firebase Console by hand, since those dates were already in the past (or today) relative to when the script first ran and so were skipped by its "never touch today/past" rule. Safe to do since 2.7 (the only build that could show these to a real user) hadn't cleared App Store review yet — nobody had actually seen any of these dates in production. This wouldn't be safe to do once a build is actually live.
  - **Caching gotcha hit during this same-day testing:** `DailyManager.fetchTodaySubject()`'s UserDefaults cache (`cachedSubjectDate`/`cachedSubjectText`) short-circuits before ever re-hitting Firestore once a real assignment is cached for "today" — so a device that had already fetched-and-cached an old value for July 5 earlier that day wouldn't pick up a same-day Firestore edit until the date rolled over. Not a bug, just an easy thing to trip over while hand-editing "today"'s doc mid-session — the fix during testing was deleting and reinstalling the app (wipes UserDefaults). New installs are unaffected since they have nothing cached yet.
  - **New script: `scripts/delete-non-baseline-daily-prompts.js`** — one-off cleanup, not part of the regular workflow. After fixing the horizon default above, Eddie wanted the collection actually clean rather than just "harmless" with redundant 2027 leftovers sitting in it. Scans the whole `daily_prompts` collection and deletes any doc whose year isn't the baseline (`--keep-year`, default 2026) — this caught not just the known July/August 2027 entries but also a chunk of September and part of October 2027 nobody knew was still there, left over from the very first flat-pool debug seeding run (which filled ~400 days forward from whenever it was first tapped, long before this calendar system existed). Supports `--dry-run` same as the other scripts. Confirmed working: dry-run after the real delete showed `0 doc(s) outside 2026 found`.
  - **September drafted.** Labor Day (verified Monday, Sept 7, 2026, programmatically) plus six minor/pop-culture days: International Bacon Day (9/5, verified first-Saturday date), National Teddy Bear Day (9/9), National Video Games Day (9/12), International Talk Like a Pirate Day (9/19), the autumnal equinox / first day of fall (9/22, date confirmed via web search rather than recalled — EarthSky and Star Walk both give Sept 22, 2026 in US time zones), National Comic Book Day (9/25), National Coffee Day (9/29). **September 11th deliberately left as a plain seasonal day ("Quiet Morning"), not themed** — flagged explicitly rather than quietly decided, given the app's lighthearted tone isn't a fit for a doodle prompt tied to a tragedy's anniversary. Approved as-is, no changes requested. Checked for duplicate subjects across the whole calendar so far (July/August/September) — none found.
  - **Labor Day is the first "floating" (nth-weekday) holiday actually seeded, not just discussed.** Confirmed accurate for 2026 specifically, but same limitation flagged earlier for Beer Day/Friendship Day applies here with higher stakes, since Labor Day is a real federal holiday, not a novelty day — its real date moves every year, but the fixed-MM-DD system will keep showing "Labor Day" on September 7th every year forever unless that specific date gets manually recomputed and reseeded each year. Not solved yet, deliberately deferred — needs a real answer (likely a small yearly touch-up script, or eventually a code-level "floating holiday" special case) before this actually matters, i.e. before September 2027 rolls around.
  - **October drafted.** Halloween (10/31) is the month's obvious anchor, with the whole back half building Halloween atmosphere (Jack-o-Lantern, Graveyard, Witch's Brew, Ghost Story, Skeleton, Costume Party, Mischief Night, etc.) rather than spacing spooky content evenly across the month. Three named minor holidays: National Taco Day (10/4), National Pumpkin Day (10/26), National Cat Day (10/29 — the US version, distinct from International Cat Day 8/8, so no repeat of the conflict from August). **Columbus Day / Indigenous Peoples Day (2nd Monday, verified Oct 12, 2026) deliberately skipped as a themed day** — same reasoning as Youth Day and Women's Equality Day: no natural "fun to draw" hook, not a judgment about the holiday itself. Approved as-is. Checked for duplicate subjects across the whole calendar (July–October) — none found; deliberately varied near-synonym clusters that started piling up in early drafts (multiple "leaves," "morning," "pumpkin," and "costume" entries) rather than letting the month read repetitively.
  - **November drafted and approved** ("do nov" → "all good"). Thanksgiving (11/26) and Black Friday (11/27) verified programmatically as the 4th/5th Thursday+Friday of November 2026; Daylight Saving's end ("Fall Back," 11/1, 1st Sunday) also verified. Minor holidays: Sandwich Day (11/3), Nachos Day (11/6), Veterans Day (11/11 — kept as a plain named holiday, not softened, since it's a day of honor rather than tragedy and has an obvious respectful "flag/salute" drawing hook), World Kindness Day (11/13). Rest of the month builds a late-fall/pre-Thanksgiving mood arc (Bare Trees → Cold Snap → Hot Cocoa → Turkey/Cranberry Sauce/Pumpkin Pie/Stuffing the week of Thanksgiving itself → Leftovers/Cozy Sunday after).
  - **December drafted and approved via the "zip thru this" batch pass** (Eddie: "all good. lets just zip thru this and get all 12 months covered. i can check as we go and really check later" — so this and the remaining months were drafted in one pass rather than the earlier month-by-month back-and-forth, per that explicit instruction). Christmas Eve (12/24), Christmas (12/25), New Year's Eve (12/31) are the anchors; Kwanzaa pinned to its real fixed start date (12/26). Hanukkah's 2026 window was verified via web search (sundown Friday Dec 4 through nightfall Saturday Dec 12, 2026) and given a "Menorah" subject on 12/5, the first full day. Winter solstice/first day of winter verified via web search as Monday, December 21, 2026, 3:50 PM EST (Old Farmer's Almanac, EarthSky, timeanddate.com, USNO all agree). National Cookie Day (12/1) opens the month. **Pearl Harbor Remembrance Day (12/7) deliberately left as a plain seasonal day ("Long Night"), not themed** — same "flag a tragedy-anniversary rather than silently decide" treatment given to September 11th elsewhere in this doc; not raised with Eddie individually before this batch pass since it followed the same established precedent, but called out here for visibility.
  - **January drafted.** New Year's Day (1/1) and MLK Day (verified 3rd Monday, Jan 19, 2026, programmatically) are the anchors. A deliberately dense minor-holiday month, since January has very few natural "big" holidays otherwise: Trivia Day (1/4), Bird Day (1/5), Hot Tea Day (1/12), Hat Day (1/15), Winnie the Pooh Day (1/18), Cheese Lovers Day (1/20), Hugging Day (1/21), Pie Day (1/23), Peanut Butter Day (1/24), Blueberry Pancake Day (1/28), Puzzle Day (1/29), Croissant Day (1/30), Backward Day (1/31) — all real, fixed-date minor observances, deliberately picked for being genuinely fun/easy to draw rather than just filling space. Remaining days are deep-winter mood/object fill (Frozen Pond, Icicle, Snowball Fight, Polar Vortex, Snow Fort, Ice Fishing, etc.).
  - **February drafted.** Valentine's Day (2/14) and Presidents Day (verified 3rd Monday, Feb 16, 2026) are the anchors, with Groundhog Day (2/2), Mardi Gras (verified via `dateutil.easter`, Feb 17, 2026 — 47 days before Easter), Galentine's Day (2/13), National Pizza Day (2/9), Love Your Pet Day (2/19), Random Acts of Kindness Day (2/22), and National Polar Bear Day (2/27) as minor holidays. **Ash Wednesday (2/18, the day after Mardi Gras) deliberately left untied to any religious theme** ("Gray Skies," plain seasonal) — same reasoning as skipping Palm Sunday in December's month and keeping Christmas/Easter/Hanukkah/Kwanzaa themed only where they're broadly cultural/secular-enough celebrations with an obvious visual hook, not solemn observances. Only 28 entries (2/1–2/28) — 2026 isn't a leap year, so there's no 2/29 to fill for the baseline year (matches the `fetchSubject` leap-year-skip logic already built into the Swift code).
  - **March drafted.** St. Patrick's Day (3/17) and the first day of spring (verified via web search: the 2026 equinox falls Friday, March 20, 10:46 AM EDT — Old Farmer's Almanac, EarthSky, timeanddate.com, USNO) are the anchors, with Daylight Saving's start (verified 2nd Sunday, March 8, 2026), Pi Day (3/14), National Waffle Day (3/25), Read Across America Day (3/2), and Girl Scout Day (3/12, the organization's founding anniversary) as minor holidays. **Palm Sunday (3/29, 2026) and the Ides of March (3/15) both deliberately left unthemed** — Palm Sunday for the same religious-solemnity reasoning as Ash Wednesday above, the Ides for being more "historical trivia/mildly ominous" than "fun to draw." Month arc moves from late-winter mud/rain into first blooms (crocus, tulip, daffodil, robin's nest) as it progresses toward the 3/20 equinox anchor.
  - **April drafted.** Easter (verified via `dateutil.easter`, April 5, 2026) and Earth Day (4/22) are the anchors, with April Fools' (4/1), National Siblings Day (4/10), and National Grilled Cheese Day (4/12) as minor holidays. **Good Friday (4/3, 2 days before Easter) and Tax Day (4/15) both deliberately left unthemed** — Good Friday for the same reasoning as Ash Wednesday/Palm Sunday, Tax Day for being a stress-associated subject rather than a fun one (used "Bird Nest" instead, keeping the day's slot but not the theme). Easter itself gets a 3-day mini-arc: Egg Dyeing (4/4) → Easter (4/5) → Egg Hunt (4/6), rather than parking everything on the single anchor date.
  - **May drafted.** Mother's Day (verified 2nd Sunday, May 10, 2026) and Memorial Day (verified last Monday, May 25, 2026) are the anchors, with May Day (5/1), Star Wars Day ("May the 4th," 5/4 — big pop-culture minor holiday, easy and fun to draw), Cinco de Mayo (5/5), and National No Homework Day (5/6) as additional named days. Month arc is a garden/early-summer buildup (flower crown, lilac, rose garden, sunflower sprout, garden hose, water balloon) leading into Memorial Day as the unofficial "summer kickoff," priming the transition into June.
  - **June drafted.** Juneteenth (6/19), Father's Day (verified 3rd Sunday, June 21, 2026), and the summer solstice/first day of summer (verified via web search alongside December's winter-solstice check, same source set — June 2026 solstice falls June 21 in most US time zones, so the "First Day of Summer" subject was placed on 6/22 to keep it distinct from Father's Day landing the same day in 2026) are the anchors, plus World Oceans Day (6/8) and Flag Day (6/14) as minor holidays. Month arc is full pool/beach/backyard summer (sprinkler, corn hole, lightning bug, sunflower field, lake day, hammock), deliberately distinct in wording from July's own summer vocabulary even where the seasonal *feel* naturally overlaps (e.g. June's "Sidewalk Chalk"/"Beach Towel"/"Snow Cone" vs. July's "Sandcastle"/"Popsicle"/"Ice Cream Truck" — same vibe, no literal repeats). Closes on 6/30 with "Half Year Mark," a light, self-aware nod to the calendar's own halfway point.
  - **All 12 months now complete — full 365-day calendar finished** (`scripts/daily-prompts-calendar.json`, 365 entries, every MM-DD of a non-leap year covered, zero missing dates, zero duplicate subjects — verified programmatically after the final batch). This was the last content-drafting task on the `daily_prompts` overhaul list.
  - **New flag: `--allow-past` on `scripts/seed-calendar-prompts.js`.** Once all 12 months were drafted, a real gap surfaced: January through June 2026 are already in the past relative to "today" (July 6, 2026), so the script's existing "never touch today or the past" rule — which is exactly what protected July 1–5 from being clobbered while 2.7 was still in review — would silently skip all of them forever; there's no future date on which the normal forward-horizon loop would ever reach back and write them. Added `--allow-past`, which additionally backfills Jan 1 of the current year through (but never including) today, using the same CALENDAR lookup and the same "skip if no matching MM-DD" behavior as the normal path. This is safe specifically because Daily Doodle's real contest history begins July 5, 2026 (see the `daily_gallery` launch-reset entry above) — nothing before that date was ever shown to a real user as a live "today," so backfilling Jan–June rewrites nothing that actually happened; it's filling in blank canvas, not correcting the record. The header comment on the flag explicitly warns not to reuse this once the app has a real year-plus of user history, since at that point every past date either is already seeded or represents locked-in history that a backfill could wrongly overwrite. Confirmed via dry-run: `--allow-past --dry-run` matches 364 of 365 calendar dates (the only one correctly excluded is today itself, July 6).
- **`fetchSubject(for:)` rewritten to walk backward year-by-year (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) — the actual code change build 2 exists for.** Prompted by Eddie asking why `daily_prompts` needs full YYYY-MM-DD doc IDs at all instead of MM-DD-only, given the calendar is meant to repeat every year anyway. MM-DD-only keys would give the same "repeats forever" behavior in one lookup, but would permanently couple every occurrence of a calendar day together — no way to ever override one specific year's July 4th without changing every other year's too. Decided to keep full dates (preserves that override flexibility) but stop requiring the pool to be physically re-seeded every year to keep the horizon filled: `fetchSubject(for:)` now tries the exact date first, then the same month/day one year back, two years back, etc., before finally falling back to the local mod-cycle formula — so a date only ever needs to be seeded once, ever, and every later year inherits it automatically. Deliberately walks back one year at a time rather than checking exactly one year prior — checking only exactly one year back would fail if that specific intervening year was never reseeded, even though an earlier year's real assignment exists further back.
  - **First version capped the walk-back at a relative `yearsBack <= 10`, which was wrong** — caught by Eddie asking "so if we fill in 2026 with all days... no matter what year, it will always go back to 2026?" A relative 10-year cap would only actually guarantee that through 2036; any lookup happening after that would stop 10 years short of ever reaching 2026's real content and silently fall back to the generic formula instead, quietly breaking the exact "seed once, works forever" promise this was built for. **Fixed to `subjectLookbackFloorYear = 2026`, an absolute floor year, not a relative count** — the walk always continues down to the actual year `daily_prompts` was first built, however far in the future "today" is, so it can never come up short of the original baseline.
  - **Feb 29 correction: 2026 isn't a leap year**, so `daily_prompts/2026-02-29` can never exist — "fill in 2026 including Feb 29" isn't literally possible. If a leap-day subject ever gets seeded, it has to live in an actual leap year (2028 is the next one) for the walk-back to ever find it. The loop skips straight past any non-leap candidate year for a Feb 29 lookup rather than querying a doc ID that could never have been legitimately written.
  - **Candidate dates are now built from plain year/month/day integers (`String(format: "%04d-%02d-%02d", ...)`) instead of `Calendar.date(byAdding: .year, value: -yearsBack, to: date)`** — deliberately sidesteps needing to know Foundation's exact leap-day rollover behavior when subtracting a year from Feb 29 (e.g. whether it clamps to Feb 28 or does something else), which isn't verifiable in this environment (no Swift toolchain available here to test it). Building the string directly from integers, with an explicit leap-year check, makes the behavior fully deterministic and doesn't depend on an edge case that was never actually confirmed.
  - `hasRealAssignment` (governs the UserDefaults caching decision in `fetchTodaySubject()`) is true for a match at any lookback year, not just the exact date. Call site signatures (`fetchTodaySubject()`, `fetchYesterdaySubject()`, `fetchHeroWinnerSubject(for:)`) are all unchanged — this was an internal implementation change only. **Confirmed shipped in the approved 2.7 build.** Commit `1f516aa` ("...build 2") landed at 2026-07-05 16:45:19 -0400; the App Store submission that went on to clear review (Waiting for Review Jul 5 4:53 PM → Ready for Distribution Jul 6 5:37 PM) went in 8 minutes later — Eddie archived and submitted right after this fix was committed, not before. So the year-fallback lookup is live in production now, not deferred to a future build as originally assumed mid-session.

---

## Confirmed — Timelapse chapter break editor: apply-to-all

**Feature:** In the doodle canvas screen's video timeline (tap the video icon → `VideoTimelineView`), tapping an existing chapter break opens `ChapterBreakEditSheet` ("Chapter Pause") to set that break's hold duration. Added a checkbox — **"Apply this time to all chapter breaks,"** defaulted unchecked — so a duration change can optionally be synced across every break in one action instead of editing each one individually.

- **`ChapterBreakEditSheet`** (`VideoTimelineView.swift`) gained `@State private var applyToAll: Bool = false`, rendered as a plain `Button` (checkmark.square.fill / square SF Symbol, not a `Toggle` — a `Toggle` renders as an iOS switch, not a checkbox) between the duration-preset row and the divider above Save/Remove.
- **`onUpdate` closure signature changed** from `(ChapterBreak) -> Void` to `(ChapterBreak, Bool) -> Void`, passing the checkbox state alongside the updated break. Only one call site (`VideoTimelineView.body`'s `.sheet(item: $editingBreak)`), updated accordingly.
- **Bulk-apply logic lives in `VideoTimelineView`, not the sheet** — when `applyToAll` is true, every entry in `chapterBreaks` has its `holdDuration` set to the newly-chosen value (each break keeps its own `timestamp`/`id`, only the duration is synced); when false, behavior is unchanged from before (only the edited break is updated by matching `id`).
- **Sheet height bumped** `160` → `210` (`.presentationDetents([.height(210)])`) to fit the new checkbox row.
- **Confirmed working on device** — Eddie tested this "since day one," both the single-break edit and the apply-to-all checkbox.

## Fixed — World Gallery pagination could silently stop forever after ~19 entries

Eddie reported the Community tab showing only 19 doodles out of ~300 total. First ruled out data loss — a second device on an older build showed everything fine, confirming the docs were still in Firestore and this was a client-side pagination bug, not a deleted-data problem.

**Root cause:** `WorldGalleryManager.fetchNextPage()` (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) used `entries.count % pageSize == 0` as its "is there more to fetch" guard — a common pagination trick (a full page might mean more; a short page means the end was reached). But `parseDocuments()` drops any Firestore doc missing `userId`/`imageURL`/`timestamp` via `compactMap` — so the moment even one doc out of a batch of 20 fails to parse (old/malformed test data, a partial write, anything), `entries.count` lands on 19 instead of 20. `19 % 20 != 0`, so the guard silently refuses to fetch again for the rest of that session — permanently, even though Firestore's own cursor (`lastDocumentSnapshot`) is still valid and hundreds more docs exist server-side. The `.following` feed had a related version of the same problem: its initial fetch never capped `entries.count` to a clean multiple of `pageSize` at all (concatenates every followed-user batch with no final prefix), so it could desync from the very first load.

**Fixed:** replaced the local-count heuristic with an explicit `reachedEnd: Bool` flag, set directly from the *raw* Firestore response size (before any parsing/dropping) at every fetch site — `refresh()`, `simpleFetch()`, `fetchArtist()`, `fetchSearch()`, `fetchFollowing()`, and the shared `appendNextPage()` next-page handler. `.following` (which fans out across up to several 30-user-ID batches with no shared cursor) sets `reachedEnd` only when *every* batch's raw response came back short of `pageSize` — if any single batch was full, there's still more to page through for that batch. `reachedEnd` resets to `false` on every fresh query (`setQuery`, `refresh`). `fetchNextPage()`'s guard is now `guard !reachedEnd, entries.count > 0 else { return }` — driven by what Firestore actually returned, immune to any future parse failures ever desyncing it again.

**Confirmed on device** — Eddie has since scrolled the full Community feed and confirmed pagination now continues past 19.

---

## Fixed — Stamp picker's "Loading photos…" could hang forever on a multi-select import

Eddie reported the Photos tab of the stamp picker getting permanently stuck on "Loading photos…" after selecting 10 photos from the camera roll — reproduced live, twice. Console logs showed nothing at all at the time of the hang (just an unrelated pre-existing profile-fetch warning), which was the key clue: a thrown/caught error would have logged something, so this had to be a silent stall, not a failure.

**Root cause:** the `.onChange(of: selectedPhotoItems)` handler (`StampTools.swift`, `StampToolButton`) loads each selected `PhotosPickerItem` sequentially in a `for` loop via `try? await item.loadTransferable(type: Data.self)`. That call has no built-in timeout. If a selected photo is an iCloud Photo Library asset that isn't downloaded to the device yet (common with "Optimize iPhone Storage" on), `loadTransferable` has to fetch it from iCloud over the network first — and if that download stalls, the `await` can hang indefinitely with no error thrown at all. Since the loop is sequential, one stuck photo blocks every photo after it, and `isLoadingPhotos` never flips back to `false`. Fits the reported repro pattern exactly: 1 photo worked, 3 worked, and it was specifically a 10-photo batch that hung — more photos just means better odds one of them happens to be a not-yet-downloaded iCloud asset, nothing special about the count itself.

**Fixed:** added `StampToolButton.loadTransferableWithTimeout(_:seconds:)`, a static helper that races the real `loadTransferable` call against a plain `Task.sleep` timer using `withTaskGroup` — whichever finishes first wins, the loser gets cancelled via `group.cancelAll()`. A genuine load failure and a timeout both surface as `nil`, which the loop already treated identically (skip this photo, move to the next), so no other logic needed to change. Timeout set to 15 seconds — generous enough for a real slow-but-working iCloud download to still succeed, short enough that a stuck one can't leave the user staring at a spinner indefinitely. The existing "clear the stuck state" workaround (force-quit and relaunch) still applies to any build before this fix.

**Confirmed on device** — rebuilt and retested twice: a clean 10-photo batch worked immediately, and a second batch with multiple stuck photos "took forever but just came up" instead of hanging permanently, matching the expected behavior of the sequential per-item timeout.

**Follow-up: loads parallelized.** The confirmed "took forever" case was multiple stuck photos in one batch each eating their own 15s timeout back-to-back (3 bad photos = 45+ seconds), since the original fix kept the loop sequential. Changed the `.onChange(of: selectedPhotoItems)` handler to load all selected items concurrently via `withTaskGroup(of: (Int, UIImage?).self)` instead of a plain `for` loop — every item's 15s timeout clock now starts at the same moment, so the whole batch is bounded by ~15s total regardless of how many photos are stuck, not stacked per bad photo. Results are index-tagged so they can be reassembled in original selection order (`items.indices.compactMap { byIndex[$0] }`) even though concurrent tasks finish in unpredictable order. **Confirmed on device** — a batch with multiple stuck photos resolved in ~11-12 seconds, in line with the ~15s cap.

---

## New — Scroll position indicator (World Gallery + private gallery)

Prompted by scrolling through the ~300-doodle Community grid with no sense of "where am I" — Eddie's ask: something like Photos' floating date badge during scroll, but also showing a position count since the collection is big enough that a date alone doesn't answer "how far through am I." Built for World Gallery first, then extended to the private gallery grid too on request — same mechanism, parallel implementation (kept separate rather than a shared generic helper, since the two grids use different entry types — `WorldSnoodle` vs. `SnoodleEntry` — and different total-count sources — Firestore aggregation vs. just `filteredEntries.count` locally — so sharing would add more indirection than the small duplication saves).

**`GalleryTab.swift`** — a floating pill appears over the top of whichever grid is being scrolled and fades out ~0.9s after scrolling stops:
- **Which tile it reports** is tracked via `.onAppear`/`.onDisappear` on each grid tile (`visibleWorldIndices` / `visiblePrivateIndices`, both `Set<Int>`) — the same convention the World Gallery pagination trigger already uses on its tiles — rather than raw scroll-offset math, which would need to account for header/strip heights above the grid and isn't worth the complexity for an approximate indicator. `.min()` (topmost currently-visible tile) drives the pill's content in both cases.
- **Show/hide is driven by `.onScrollGeometryChange(for: CGFloat.self, of: { $0.contentOffset.y })`** (iOS 18+ API, safe here since this project's deployment target is 26.5) — any change in content offset calls `pokeScrollIndicator()` / `pokePrivateScrollIndicator()`, which shows the pill and (re)schedules a cancellable `Task` to hide it 0.9s later. Scrolling continuously keeps resetting the timer; stopping lets it fire.
- **Content:** date (`MMM d, yyyy`) + `#<position> of <total>`, 1-based. World Gallery's total is `worldManager.totalCount` (the real Firestore aggregation count), falling back to `displayedWorldEntries.count` if that hasn't loaded yet; private gallery's total is just `filteredEntries.count` (already the full local set, no separate count query needed).
- **Visible-index sets reset on whatever changes the underlying list** — World Gallery: `applyWorldQuery()` and the debounced search branch in `searchWorldDoodles()`; private gallery: `.onChange(of: query)` on the grid's `ScrollView`. Otherwise stale index bookkeeping from the previous list could briefly drive the pill before the new grid's tiles report in.
- Plain `.thinMaterial` capsule, matches the Layers panel header's existing material choice elsewhere in the app. `.allowsHitTesting(false)` so it never intercepts taps meant for the grid underneath.

**Confirmed on device** — Eddie has tested the scroll indicator on both grids.

---

## In Progress — Caption override + background-editing shortcuts (post-2.9, not yet versioned)

Three small features added in the same session, after 2.9 shipped. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as everything else in this environment.

### Hidden tap-to-edit caption override
No new buttons anywhere, per explicit request — a purely hidden interaction. On a doodle's detail page (private gallery `SnoodleDetailView.card(for:)` and world gallery `WorldSnoodleDetailView.worldCard(entry:)`, both in `GalleryTab.swift`), tapping the AI-generated caption text on your own doodle opens `CaptionEditSheet` — a small sheet (`.presentationDetents([.height(260)])`) with a `TextEditor` pre-filled with the current caption, Cancel/Save toolbar buttons. Save is disabled on an empty/whitespace-only string, deliberately — the caption `Text` itself is the only tap surface (it doesn't render at all when the caption is empty), so allowing an empty save would remove the one way back in to edit it again.

- **Ownership gating differs by gallery, on purpose.** Private gallery entries have no per-user ownership model yet (see "Deferred — Multi-user-per-device private gallery separation" below in Outstanding Items), so every entry visible there is already "yours" by construction — no check needed. World gallery entries do check, mirroring the existing pattern right below it in the same card: `auth.userId == entry.userId` (the same condition that already gates the trash-vs-report button split).
- **Sync is bidirectional and best-effort, mirroring the existing "Remove from Community" match logic exactly** (same card, a few lines below the new code): private→world uses `entry.worldGalleryId` when present; world→private matches by `worldGalleryId` first, falls back to timestamp proximity (`< 60s`) for older entries that predate that field. If no matching copy exists on the other side, only the side that was actually edited gets written — never an error, never a partial-failure alert, just a no-op for the missing half.
- **`WorldSnoodle.caption` changed from `let` to `var`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`) — required for the optimistic local-array update; every other field on the struct is untouched.
- **`WorldGalleryManager.updateCaption(snoodleId:keywords:newCaption:)`** (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`, alongside `toggleLike`) — rebuilds `searchIndex` the exact same way `submit()` does (lowercased caption words + keywords, punctuation-trimmed), so search stays accurate after an override instead of silently going stale. Takes `keywords` as a parameter rather than looking the doc up, since the caller (either detail view) already has the full entry in hand and this may be called for a doc that isn't in the currently-loaded `entries` feed (e.g. a profile-scoped detail view using `initialEntries`).

### Layers panel — "Edit Background" option on the BG chip
The background layer chip's `···` menu (`backgroundLayerChip` in `DrawScreen.swift`) had a single option, "Extract All as Stamps." Added a second, conditional on `canvasBackgroundImage != nil`: **"Edit Background"** — jumps straight to `BackgroundEditorView` (the Effects screen: opacity/blur/brightness/saturation sliders + Extract Objects), skipping the photo picker entirely. This reuses the exact same standalone-presentation path already wired up for long-pressing the canvas color button (`showBgEditor = true` + `saveBgStateForCancel()`) — no new sheet, no new state. Since `bgOpacity`/`bgBlur`/`bgBrightness`/`bgSaturation` are already the live values driving the current background's on-canvas appearance, `BackgroundEditorView` opens pre-loaded with the right settings automatically; nothing extra had to be threaded through.

### 3-finger tap on canvas → Extract All as Stamps (was: double-tap the stamp-mode toolbar button — reverted, didn't work)
**First attempt (shipped in this doc, never actually worked): double-tap the pen/stamp mode toggle button.** Tried replacing the toolbar `Button` with a plain `Image` + two chained `.onTapGesture(count:)` modifiers (count 2, then count 1) — a commonly-cited SwiftUI technique for disambiguating single vs. double tap on the same view without a custom UIKit `require(toFail:)` bridge. This was never actually tested on device before being written up as done; Eddie reported it wasn't firing at all. Root cause (most likely, never fully confirmed): stacked `.onTapGesture(count:)` modifiers are known to be unreliable specifically inside `ToolbarItem`/navigation-bar content, which SwiftUI hosts differently than a plain in-canvas view — the disambiguation trick that works fine elsewhere in this codebase doesn't reliably survive being placed in the nav bar.
- **Reverted:** the toolbar button (`DrawScreen.swift`'s trailing nav bar item) is back to a plain `Button` with only the single-tap toggle-stamp-mode action — identical to how it worked before this feature was ever attempted.
- **Replaced with a 3-finger tap anywhere on the canvas**, per Eddie's own suggestion once the double-tap was confirmed broken. Built using the same robust window-level `UIGestureRecognizer` infrastructure `WindowPinchView` already uses for every other canvas gesture (pinch, rotation, 2-finger pan, long-press, stamp pan, single-tap, and an existing-but-unwired double-tap) — a new `UITapGestureRecognizer` with `numberOfTouchesRequired = 3`, delegate = the same `Coordinator`, added alongside the others in `makeUIView`. Because it requires a distinct touch count (3) from every other recognizer here (1-finger draw/tap/stamp-pan, 2-finger pinch/pan/rotate), it needs no `require(toFail:)` or simultaneous-recognition juggling to avoid conflicts — UIKit won't even begin recognizing it until a third finger is down, so it structurally cannot interfere with drawing, single-tap-to-select, or 2-finger canvas gestures.
- New `onThreeFingerTap: (() -> Void)? = nil` closure property on `WindowPinchView`, new `handleThreeFingerTap(_:)` handler on `Coordinator` (mirrors `handleWindowDoubleTap`'s existing canvas-bounds + `!showLayersPanel` guard), wired at the `DrawScreen.swift` call site to `{ if !isExtractingLayer { extractAllLayersAsStamps() } }` — the identical function and guard the BG chip's "Extract All as Stamps" menu item already calls, so behavior is exactly identical between the two entry points. Automatically inherits the existing `shouldReceive touch` delegate blocks (`blockGestures`, Pencil/stylus rejection, List/CollectionView rejection for the layers panel) since it's added through the same `Coordinator` as every other recognizer — no new blocking logic needed.
- **Scoped to `DrawScreen.swift`'s canvas only.** `WindowPinchView` has a second call site in `CustomStampViews.swift` (the doodle-stamp-creator canvas) — left untouched; `onThreeFingerTap` defaults to `nil` there, so it compiles fine and simply does nothing on a 3-finger tap in that screen. Wasn't asked for there.
- **The old `onBackgroundDoubleTap` closure/recognizer pair (from the *original* Extract All build, already documented elsewhere in this file as abandoned "due to gesture conflicts") is untouched and still wired to `nil` at the call site** — genuinely dead/inert, left in place per this codebase's "leave orphaned code alone" convention rather than removed as part of an unrelated fix.
- **First on-device attempt: not firing.** Diagnosed with temporary `[3fingertap]`-prefixed `print()` logging at every step of the chain (recognizer attachment, `shouldReceive touch`, `handleThreeFingerTap`'s guards, `extractAllLayersAsStamps()`'s entry/no-op). Root cause was never actually pinned down via the logs — before a build with the logging was tested, a closer look/retest showed **the gesture itself works fine as originally built.** All five `[3fingertap]` print statements have been removed again (temporary diagnostic instrumentation, not meant to ship) — confirmed zero references remain via grep, braces still balance.
- **Confirmed working on device.** One known, accepted (not a bug) behavior: running the extraction a second time when the canvas already has a previously-extracted stamp on it doesn't do a fresh clean re-scan — it re-renders everything (drawing layers + all current stamps, including the earlier extracted one) into one flat image and runs Vision on *that*, so the already-placed stamp is now just rasterized pixels rather than a distinct object, and a second pass tends to produce a single new stamp rather than cleanly re-segmenting. Eddie's read: "but it's fine!" — not something to fix, just worth knowing why it behaves that way if it comes up again.

---

## In Progress — Community grid play button for your own posted doodles

**Revisited a prior deliberate decision.** World gallery tiles have never shown a timelapse play button — `world_gallery` Firestore docs only ever store the flattened image, never the `.skadoodle` layer/stroke data, so there was nothing to animate for someone else's post. That's still true for other people's doodles. But for a post that's *your own* — where the paired `.skadoodle` file still exists locally in `Documents/Doodles/` on this device (from when you originally drew and saved it privately, then posted to World Gallery) — the timelapse data has been sitting right there the whole time; the community grid just never checked for it.

- **`WorldSnoodleTile`** (`GalleryTab.swift`) gained `@EnvironmentObject var store: SnoodleStore` (confirmed safe — `GalleryTab()` receives `.environmentObject(store)` directly from `ContentView.swift`, so every descendant, however deeply nested, has it) and a `matchingLocalEntry: SnoodleEntry?` computed property — same match strategy already used by caption sync and "Remove from Community" a few hundred lines below in this same file: `worldGalleryId` match first, falls back to timestamp proximity (`< 60s`) for older entries that predate that field.
- The tile's image now has `.overlay(alignment: .bottom) { if let local = matchingLocalEntry, local.hasSkadoodleFile { TilePlayBadge(entry: local) } }` — reuses `TilePlayBadge` completely unmodified (it already just takes a `SnoodleEntry` and self-contains export + full-screen playback), same overlay alignment the private gallery's `SnoodleTile` already uses. If no matching local copy exists, or it exists but predates the `.skadoodle` re-editable format (no paired file on disk), the badge simply doesn't render — silent, no error state, matching the existing `hasSkadoodleFile` gating pattern everywhere else this flag is checked.
- **Scoped to the grid tile only, per what was asked.** The World Gallery detail screen (`WorldSnoodleDetailView.worldCard(entry:)`) does not yet get the equivalent `TimelapseButton` the private gallery's detail action bar has — same underlying data would support it (the matching-local-entry lookup pattern is identical), but wasn't part of this request. Natural, low-effort follow-up if wanted later.
- Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as everything else in this environment.

---

## Fixed — `joinedAt` never actually written to `users` docs

Eddie noticed while looking at a `users` doc in the Firebase Console: it has `updatedAt` but no signup/join date at all. `UserProfile.joinedAt` exists as a Swift model field and `UserProfileManager.parseProfile` reads it back from Firestore (falling back to `Date()` — i.e. "right now" — if the field is missing), but a full grep of the codebase for `joinedAt` confirmed it was **never written anywhere** — not in `saveProfile()` (runs on every profile edit), not in the actual new-user creation block (`UserProfileManager`, "No doc exists — new user" — the one real place a `users/{uid}` doc gets its first `setData`), not in the phantom-account debug tool. So every profile's `joinedAt` was silently defaulting to "now" on every read, forever — not a display bug (the field isn't referenced anywhere in `ProfileView.swift` yet, so nothing user-facing was ever wrong), just missing data-layer prep with a fallback that masked the gap instead of surfacing it.

**Fixed:** added `"joinedAt": Timestamp(date: Date())` alongside the existing `"updatedAt"` write in the new-user-creation `defaultData` dictionary (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`, `UserProfileManager`, ~line 382) — the one and only place a brand-new account's doc is created. Deliberately **not** added to `saveProfile()`'s update dictionary — that runs on every single profile edit, so writing `joinedAt` there would silently reset every user's join date back to "now" each time they touched their profile, defeating the whole point.

**Only fixes it going forward** — existing users who signed up before this fix still have no `joinedAt` field in their doc, and this change does nothing to backfill them (a genuinely new account creation event never fires for them again).

**Backfill script: `scripts/backfill-joined-at.js`** (new, standalone Node script, same `firebase-admin` + service-account-key pattern as `scripts/seed-daily-prompts.js`/`scripts/seed-calendar-prompts.js`/`scripts/delete-non-baseline-daily-prompts.js`). Scans the whole `users` collection; for any doc missing `joinedAt`, sets it to that doc's own `updatedAt` value (not exact — an early edit event, not the true signup moment — but the best available approximation, since `updatedAt` has been ticking since close to when each account was created). Docs that already have `joinedAt` are left untouched, so it's safe to re-run. Docs missing *both* `joinedAt` and `updatedAt` (shouldn't happen, but handled defensively) are skipped and logged rather than guessing a fake date. Supports `--dry-run` (prints the first 10 planned writes, nothing committed) same as the other scripts. Batched in chunks of 400 (Firestore's batch cap is 500). `node backfill-joined-at.js <service-account.json> [--dry-run]`, run from Eddie's own terminal — needs the same service-account key file (kept outside git) the other scripts use.

**Note: signing out and back in on an existing account does NOT test the new-user-creation fix.** `UserProfileManager`'s "no doc exists — new user" branch only fires when the Firestore `users/{uid}` doc doesn't exist yet; an existing account's doc already exists, so re-signing-in just re-fetches it (the `else` branch), never recreates it. The backfill script covers getting `joinedAt` onto *existing* accounts (including Eddie's own) without needing to exercise that code path at all. To actually live-test the creation code path itself, the safe option is a phantom test account (`SnoodleFirebase.swift`'s `PhantomAccounts.all`, DEBUG-only) with its Firestore doc manually deleted first via Console, then signed into via the debug tool — that forces a real "no doc exists" run without touching Eddie's real profile data (which would otherwise get reset to random defaults if his own doc were deleted for this purpose).

---

## Fixed — `.skadoodle` file leaks + oversized embedded backgrounds

Surfaced while investigating a completely different question — whether `.skadoodle` files (the re-editable layer/stroke format, see "Architecture" below) would be worth syncing to the server. Two real, unrelated bugs turned up along the way.

**1. Single-doodle delete leaked `.skadoodle` files.** `SnoodleStore.delete(_:)` (`Models.swift`) only ever removed `entry.imageURL` (the flattened image) — it never touched `entry.skadoodleURL`. Deleting doodles one at a time (as opposed to "Clear Local Doodles," which wipes the entire `Documents/Doodles/` directory indiscriminately via `contentsOfDirectory` and so never had this problem) silently orphaned a `.skadoodle` file on disk every time. Harmless — wasted space, no crash risk, nothing reads a `.skadoodle` file whose paired `SnoodleEntry` no longer exists — but real. **Fixed:** `delete(_:)` now also removes `entry.skadoodleURL`.

**2. `canvasBackgroundImage` was never resolution-capped, unlike every other image path in the app.** Found by adding temporary `#if DEBUG` sizing instrumentation to `saveSkadoodleData()` (`DrawScreen.swift`) to answer the original size question — a real device test came back `total=4747337B background=3421164B` for one doodle (a ~3.4MB *raw* background alone, ~4.56MB once base64-encoded into the JSON, since `Data` fields always inflate ~4/3 through base64). Root cause: `ImagePickerCallback` (`DrawScreen.swift`, the picker used specifically for canvas backgrounds — confirmed via grep to be its only call site) handed the picker's `.originalImage` straight to `canvasBackgroundImage` with no downscaling at all, unlike stamps (capped 600px, `CustomStampManager.addStamp`), gallery thumbnails (capped 400px, `Models.swift`), or even `BackgroundPhotoHistory`'s own recents cache for the *same* image (capped 1600px, right there in the same file) — the live canvas background was the one place that convention was skipped. A modern iPhone photo picked at native resolution (4032×3024-class) landed in the `.skadoodle` file at full size for no visible benefit, since the canvas only ever displays it at a few hundred points wide.

Not just a file-size problem — `canvasBackgroundImage` is the live in-memory bitmap the eraser's `_BgEffectsImageCache`, the opacity/blur/brightness/saturation CIFilter sliders, and the timelapse video exporter all operate on every time they touch the background, so this was real, ongoing CPU/memory overhead during normal drawing too, not just a one-time save-time cost.

**Fixed:** `ImagePickerCallback.Coordinator.imagePickerController(_:didFinishPickingMediaWithInfo:)` now returns `img.downsampled(toMaxDimension: 1600)` instead of the raw picker image — reuses the existing `UIImage.downsampled(toMaxDimension:)` extension already defined in `CustomStampManager.swift` for stamps, same 1600px convention `BackgroundPhotoHistory` already uses. Single fix point since `ImagePickerCallback` has exactly one call site in the whole codebase. Every other place `canvasBackgroundImage` gets assigned (undo/redo restore, the effects-screen "baked" result, extraction) reads from this same already-capped value as its starting point, so the cap cascades through without needing to touch each of those individually.

**Added a safety net for doodles saved before this fix:** `restoreSkadoodleData(_:)` now downsamples the decoded background image the same way (`UIImage(data: imgData)?.downsampled(toMaxDimension: 1600)`) before assigning it to `canvasBackgroundImage`. This doesn't shrink anything already sitting on disk — the `.skadoodle` file itself is untouched unless the doodle gets resaved — but it keeps memory sane the moment an old oversized doodle is reopened, and if the user then edits/resaves it (or it just auto-saves), the smaller version is what goes back out, so re-editing an old bloated doodle cleans it up as a side effect.

**Scope check, since this came up mid-investigation:** confirmed this only ever affected local `Documents/Doodles/*.skadoodle` files — the flattened images that actually reach Firebase Storage (`world_doodles/`, via `renderCanvasWithStamps`) are rendered at canvas point-size × screen scale, not the background photo's raw source resolution, so a huge source photo was always being composited down to canvas size for the community/export image regardless of this bug. Not independently verified that every *other* image write path into Storage (profile photos, etc.) is free of a similar unbounded-source-resolution issue — this was specifically about `canvasBackgroundImage`, not a full audit.

**Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as all the visual/perf work in this doc; this environment can't compile or run the app. Worth a real before/after comparison next time a background photo is used: check the `[Skadoodle size]` DEBUG console line and confirm `background=` now lands in the low hundreds of KB instead of multiple MB.

**Follow-up fix — the downsample cap had a real gap: `bakeBgTransform()` bypassed it entirely.** Real-device testing (`[Skadoodle size]` log) showed `background=2734392B` (~2.73MB) — essentially unchanged from the pre-fix ~3.4MB baseline, not the expected low-hundreds-of-KB. Root cause: `BackgroundEditorView.bakeBgTransform()` (`DrawScreen.swift`) — the function that flattens a pinch-zoom/pan commit in the Effects screen into a new image on Done — renders via `UIGraphicsImageRenderer(size: CGSize(width: cW, height: cH))` with no explicit format, and `cW`/`cH` are canvas *point* size, not pixel size. With no format specified, the renderer defaults to the device's screen scale (2x/3x), so the baked image's real pixel buffer is `canvasSize(points) × deviceScale` — on a 3x device with a few-hundred-point canvas, comfortably over 1600px. This bake path was the one background-image entry point that never got the `downsampled(toMaxDimension:)` cap every other path (`ImagePickerCallback`, `BackgroundPhotoHistory`, `restoreSkadoodleData`'s safety net) already has — so a plain photo pick without touching zoom/pan stayed correctly capped, but the moment the Effects screen's pinch-zoom or drag was touched before tapping Done (normal, expected usage of that screen), the already-capped background got silently re-inflated back up to full device-scale resolution. **Fixed:** `bakeBgTransform()`'s return now runs through `.downsampled(toMaxDimension: 1600)` before being handed back, matching every other entry point. Single fix point — both `onDone` call sites in `DrawScreen.swift` (the picker-flow `NavigationDestination` and the standalone `showBgEditor` sheet) already just assign whatever `bakeBgTransform()` returns to `canvasBackgroundImage`, so neither needed its own change.

**Confirmed on device.** A fresh background image with an actual pinch-zoom action, no drawing on the canvas, came back `background=570403B` (~570KB) — down from the ~2.7-3.4MB baseline, squarely in the expected low-hundreds-of-KB range. Two earlier retests in between had shown an unchanged `2734392B` across three separate "Done" taps despite growing stroke/point counts — the identical byte count made clear those were all still reading the same in-memory background object carried over from before this fix, not a fresh test of it; once a genuinely new photo + zoom was used, the fix showed up immediately.

---

## Fixed — Timelapse stamp fade-in ignored a stamp's real position when reordered behind other layers

Eddie reported: a stamp added last, then manually dragged down in the Layers panel so it sits *behind* other layers on the live canvas (correctly), showed up wrong in its exported timelapse — it flashed on top of everything during its fade-in, then "suddenly retreated" to its real (behind) position partway through the video. A worse version of the same thing: sometimes it stayed on top the whole video and never corrected itself.

**Root cause, found by code review (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`'s `buildVideo`, the real exporter — not `buildStates`, the separate unused function elsewhere in this file):** a stamp's fade-in has always been a fast O(1) shortcut — paint the stamp image directly on top of `runningComposite` (everything composited so far), increasing alpha each frame. That's correct 99% of the time, since new content is almost always added on top. But it never actually checks the stamp's real position in `zLayerOrder` — it just assumes "new = topmost" unconditionally. The moment a stamp is deliberately reordered to sit *behind* already-visible content, the fade-in still paints it on top regardless, which is the "flash on top" bug. The "sudden retreat" is a *separate*, correctly-working mechanism doing its job: when the reorder event (`LayerOrderChange`, recorded with its own timestamp whenever the user drags in the Layers panel) is replayed at its point in the timeline, `.reorder`'s handler does a full, genuinely z-order-correct `rebuildComposite()` — that's what visually snaps the stamp into its real position. The worse "never corrects" case is the same root bug, just without a later reorder event around to accidentally paper over it.

**Fixed:** the `.stamp` case in `buildVideo` now checks `hasContentAbove(layerId: stamp.id)` (the same helper the `.stroke` case already uses to detect a non-topmost layer) before choosing how to composite the fade. If nothing's above it (the common case), behavior is byte-for-byte unchanged — fast path, paint on top. If something *is* above it in `zLayerOrder`, it now uses the same below/above split technique the `.stroke` case already uses for strokes on a non-topmost layer: render everything below the stamp's position once (opaque) and everything above it once (transparent), then sandwich the fading stamp between them at every step, instead of painting on top of `runningComposite`. The final "bake into runningComposite" step also branches the same way — fast path stays a simple paint-on-top; the corrected path uses a full `rebuildComposite()` instead, so `runningComposite` itself is genuinely correct going forward from that point, not just during the fade animation (previously, even after the fade, the underlying composite stayed wrong until the next incidental reorder event happened to fix it).

**Backed up first:** `DoodleVideoExport.swift.bak` was made before this change, per Eddie's own ask ("should I back up first?") — plain copy, non-`.swift` extension so Xcode's folder-synced target doesn't pick it up as a duplicate source file, same convention as the `TodayTab.swift.bak*` files made earlier this session. Safe to delete once this fix is confirmed working on device.

**Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as everything else in this doc; this environment can't compile or run the app. Verified by code review (the new branch reuses the exact `hasContentAbove`/`rebuildComposite` helpers and below/above split pattern already proven correct for the `.stroke` case) and by brace/paren balance count.
