Next step: re-export the exact doodle that surfaced this (stamp placed last, then dragged behind other layers) and confirm it now renders correctly-positioned for the entire fade-in, with no flash-then-retreat.

**Re-tested: better but not fully fixed — "the stamp fades completely in and is on top of all layers, then immediately goes behind the layers."** The fade itself is no longer flashing wrong-then-right mid-animation the way it was, but something is still causing the fully-faded-in stamp to render on top for a beat before snapping behind — meaning either `hasContentAbove` isn't finding the already-existing content above it at the moment this stamp's event is processed (so the fast/wrong path is still being used for the whole fade + bake), or something in the below/above split itself isn't capturing that content correctly. Reasoning through the timing by hand didn't converge on a single confirmed cause, so **added temporary `[stampz]`-prefixed diagnostic logging** (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`, same throwaway-debug convention as the earlier `[3fingertap]` gesture logging elsewhere in this doc — meant to be removed once this is resolved, not shipped): one-time dump of `document.layerOrder`, every `document.layerOrderChanges` entry, and the full sorted event list (index/type/timestamp) right after `events.sort`; per-stamp-event logging of the live `zLayerOrder`, which drawing-layer IDs and stamp IDs are already "active" at that exact moment, and the resolved `hasContentAbove`/`stampNeedsFull` values; and a log line on every `.reorder` event showing its timestamp and the order it applies. Next step: re-export the same doodle, pull the `[stampz]` lines from the Xcode console, and use them to see exactly why the stamp isn't being treated as needing the full below/above composite at the moment it fades in.

**Real root cause found from the `[stampz]` logs on a genuine 15-layer, 9-stamp, 6-reorder doodle: `hasContentAbove`/`zLayerOrder` is fundamentally the wrong thing to check a stamp's position against.** `zLayerOrder` only updates when a `.reorder` event actually fires during replay, and it's seeded from whichever historical `LayerOrderChange` snapshot was most recently replayed — a snapshot that only ever lists whatever existed *at the moment that specific reorder was recorded*. In the logged doodle, every one of 8 later stamps got created *between* an earlier reorder and the final catch-all one, so at the exact moment each was placed, `zLayerOrder` was still sitting on an older snapshot that didn't list them at all — `stampIdx in zLayerOrder: NOT FOUND` for every single one, `hasContentAbove` correctly (given what it was checking) returning `false` every time, so the fast/wrong path fired for nearly every stamp in the doodle, not just an edge case.

**Fixed** by checking a stamp's position against `document.layerOrder` (the one true, final arrangement — stable and unchanging throughout the whole export) instead of the mutable `zLayerOrder`. New `hasContentAboveInFinalOrder(id:)`, scoped locally inside the `.stamp` case (deliberately *not* touching the shared `hasContentAbove(layerId:)` used by the `.stroke` case — no report of strokes having this problem, and correcting it there wasn't part of what was asked), walks `document.layerOrder` from the stamp's position onward and checks the same already-drawn-so-far bookkeeping (`layerLines`, `doneStamps`) — this correctly answers "will there be already-drawn content above this stamp" regardless of which historical reorder snapshot `zLayerOrder` happens to be resting on at that instant. The below/above split (`belowEntries`/`aboveEntries`/`stampIdx`) was updated to slice `document.layerOrder` the same way.

**The bake step also had to change, not just the check.** The first version's "slow path" baked the stamp in via the existing `rebuildComposite()` helper — but that helper filters through the same mutable `zLayerOrder`, which (per the bug above) frequently doesn't list a just-placed stamp yet. Calling it would have silently *dropped the stamp out of the composite entirely* rather than merely mis-positioning it — worse than the original bug, since the stamp would vanish until some later reorder event happened to reintroduce it. Fixed by baking from the same `belowComp`/`aboveComp` images already built for the fade (both already derived from `document.layerOrder`) instead of calling `rebuildComposite()`.

**Confirmed safe against a follow-on concern:** could a later `.reorder` event's own `rebuildComposite()` call still drop this stamp, since it also filters through `zLayerOrder`? No — every `LayerOrderChange` is recorded live, as a snapshot of whatever `layerOrder` looked like *at that exact moment*, which by construction already includes anything created before it. So any reorder event with a timestamp after a given stamp's creation is guaranteed to already list that stamp in its own snapshot; there's no path where a stamp this fix correctly renders can later vanish when an unrelated reorder replays. Verified this holds for the actual logged doodle (no intermediate reorder falls between any of the 8 affected stamps and the final catch-all one).

**Diagnostic `[stampz]` logging left in place for this next round** (not yet removed) — if this still isn't fully fixed, the existing one-time `document.layerOrder`/`layerOrderChanges`/sorted-event dump plus the per-`.reorder`-event log are still there to look at, without needing another round of guessing. The per-stamp `zLayerOrder`-based log block (tied to the now-replaced check) was removed since it no longer reflects what the code actually does. Not yet re-tested on device — same standing caveat as this whole investigation.

**Confirmed fixed on device** — Eddie re-tested the same 15-layer/9-stamp/6-reorder doodle and reported back "perfect!" All `[stampz]` diagnostic logging (the one-time `document.layerOrder`/`layerOrderChanges`/sorted-event dump after `events.sort`, and the per-`.reorder`-event log line) has been removed now that it did its job — same throwaway-debug lifecycle as the earlier `[3fingertap]` gesture logging elsewhere in this doc. The `shortId`/`describeOrder` helpers that only existed to support those prints were removed along with them (confirmed via grep — zero remaining references to either). The explanatory code comment on `hasContentAboveInFinalOrder` that referenced "`[stampz]` logging" was reworded to say "confirmed via diagnostic logging during development," since the logging itself no longer exists in the file. Brace/paren balance verified clean after the removal. `DoodleVideoExport.swift.bak` (the pre-fix backup made before this investigation started) is still sitting on disk — safe to delete whenever, no longer needed now that the fix is confirmed working.

---

## Fixed — Layers panel "+" always inserted the new layer at the top

Eddie's workflow for a doodle built layer-by-layer *between* existing content: hit "+" (new layer always landed at the absolute top of the stack), then long-press-drag it back down to wherever it was actually needed — every single time. Changed the "+" button in `layersPanelView` (`DrawScreen.swift`) to insert the new `DrawingLayer` right *above* the currently selected drawing layer (`userSelectedLayerId`) instead of always appending to the top of `layerOrder`. Falls back to the old top-of-stack behavior when nothing's selected (e.g. a freshly cleared/empty canvas, where there's nothing to insert "above" yet). The new layer still becomes the active selection afterward, same as before — only its *starting position* changed. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as the rest of this doc.

---

## v3.1 (shipped — in App Store distribution)

### New Feature: Target video length for timelapse export

**Context.** Grew out of a real product push: Eddie wants to seriously start producing his own TikTok content built around Skadoodle exports (doodle timelapse synced to music — either self-recorded public-domain-song covers or genuine pre-1926 public-domain recordings, worked out in the same conversation this feature came from). The existing exporter always produced a fixed ~16-20 second video (fixed ~300-frame/~10s draw reveal + fixed 2s hold + fixed 4.5s outro, regardless of how much or how little was drawn) — fine for quick TikTok posts, but TikTok's own data favors 60-90s for storytelling content specifically, and a minute-plus narrative synced to a song chorus was flatly impossible before this: drawing more or less never changed the reveal's length, only its speed.

**Design decision (discussed before building): duration is the exposed control, not playback speed.** When matching a video to a song, the natural unit is "how long is my audio clip" — nobody thinks in "2.3x speed." So the UI exposes a target *length in seconds*; the app works out internally what reveal speed makes that true. This mirrors how a movie's stated runtime works: it doesn't include the credits rolling at the end, so the target duration here governs only the *content* portion (draw reveal + chapter pauses + stamp fades combined) — the fixed 2s finished-doodle hold and the ~4.5s branded Skadoodle outro always play afterward, unaffected by the slider, exactly as before.

**The interaction problem and its resolution.** Chapter breaks (existing feature — user-placed pause markers with their own hold duration) and the new duration target both consume the same time budget, which could easily conflict (e.g., stacking pauses that add up to more than the chosen target). Resolved as: **the target governs the total; chapter-break pauses are carved out of it first, and whatever's left over is exactly how long the draw reveal takes** — so dragging a pause longer visibly shrinks the reveal to compensate, and the number the user set is always the number they get. If pauses (+ the small fixed stamp-fade cost) alone exceed the chosen target, the target **auto-bumps up** to fit rather than erroring or silently clamping — surfaced to the user as an inline note ("Your pauses need more room than Xs — length increased to Ys to fit them"), never a silent surprise.

**`ContentDurationBudget` / `computeContentDurationBudget(...)`** (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`, top of file) — the single formula both the live UI estimate and the actual export call, so the number shown before exporting can never drift from what the export actually produces. Takes an optional target duration, the live chapter breaks, and stamp count; returns the resolved draw-frame budget, pause/stamp frame counts, the actual resolved total (post-auto-bump), and a `wasBumped` flag. `nil` target → legacy fixed 300-frame (~10s) draw budget, byte-for-byte the same behavior as every build before this one — nothing changes for a doodle that never touches the new control.

**`SkadoodleDocument.targetContentDurationSeconds: Double?`** (`DoodleFormat.swift`) — new optional field, default `nil`. Since `SkadoodleDocument` uses synthesized (not custom) `Codable` conformance, an `Optional` stored property is handled automatically by Swift's synthesis (missing key on decode → nil, nil on encode → key omitted) — no custom `CodingKeys`/`init(from:)` work needed, unlike several other fields in this file that required hand-written Codable for exactly this kind of backward-compat reason. Old `.skadoodle` files decode this as `nil` with zero special-casing.

**`DoodleVideoExport.swift`'s `buildVideo(...)`** — the old hardcoded `pointsPerFrame = max(3, totalPoints / 300)` replaced with a call to `computeContentDurationBudget(...)`, feeding `durationBudget.drawFrames` into the same `pointsPerFrame` formula. Everything downstream (the progress-tracking `estimatedContentFrames`, the actual per-chunk stroke-reveal loop) already read `pointsPerFrame` as a variable, so no other changes were needed there — the new budget just changes what that one variable resolves to. **`buildStates(...)`, a second, entirely unused private function in the same file (zero call sites anywhere in the codebase — confirmed via grep) was deliberately left untouched**, same "leave orphaned code alone" precedent as `PastWinnersView`/`CalendarTab.swift` elsewhere in this doc.

**`VideoTimelineView.swift`** — new `durationSection` at the top of the chapter-break editor sheet (the "obvious home" per direct discussion, since it's already where pause markers are edited): a toggle ("Set a target video length," off by default = `nil`/legacy behavior) that, when turned on, seeds the slider at whatever the *current* legacy total would be (so opting in never causes a surprise jump), then a 1s-step slider bounded between the true minimum (pauses + stamps + a 1s reveal floor) and a generous 120s ceiling. Live breakdown shown beneath: `Pauses: Xs + Draw: Ys = Total: Zs` — deliberately a two-part breakdown, not three; stamp fade time (0.27s each, real but not something anyone's tuning individually) is folded into the "Draw" number via `ContentDurationBudget.displayDrawSeconds` rather than shown as its own line. The auto-bump note appears inline directly beneath when triggered. `VideoTimelineView` gained a new `@Binding var targetContentDurationSeconds: Double?` parameter (mirrors the existing `chapterBreaks` binding pattern exactly) threaded from `DrawScreen.swift`'s own new `@State private var targetContentDurationSeconds: Double? = nil` — round-trips through `currentSkadoodleDocument()` / `restoreSkadoodleData(_:)` the same way `chapterBreaks` already does, and resets to `nil` alongside `chapterBreaks = []` at all four existing clear-canvas sites (Clear Drawing, Clear Stamps, Clear All, and the single-item-clear shortcut when only one thing exists on the canvas). `VideoTimelineView`'s own `exportDocument` computed property (already responsible for overlaying live-edited `chapterBreaks` onto the snapshot `document` before export) was extended to overlay the live `targetContentDurationSeconds` too — otherwise the toolbar's export/play button would've exported against a stale nil snapshot captured when the sheet first opened, ignoring whatever the user had just set.

**Explicitly out of scope for this pass, deferred:** no change to the gallery-side quick-export paths (`TimelapseButton` in a doodle's detail view, `TilePlayBadge` on gallery tiles) — those read `entry.skadoodleURL` and decode whatever `targetContentDurationSeconds` was saved with that doodle (nil for anything saved before this feature, or whatever was last set via the Video Timeline editor for newer ones) rather than exposing their own duration control; setting/changing the target duration is only available through the Video Timeline sheet's new UI. This matches the existing precedent that detailed video-timing control lives in one place (the timeline editor), not duplicated across every export entry point.

**Not yet visually confirmed on device** — same standing caveat as every other visual/UI change in this doc; this environment can't compile or run SwiftUI. Correct by code review and by-hand brace/paren-balance verification (all four touched files balanced before/after). Next step: build, set a target duration with and without chapter breaks stacked on top, confirm the resolved total in the UI actually matches the real exported file's length, and confirm the auto-bump path triggers and reads sensibly when pauses are deliberately over-stacked.

**Bug found immediately during first real test: a sparse doodle (3 scribbles) ignored the duration slider entirely.** Root cause: `pointsPerFrame = max(3, totalPoints / drawFrames)` — the floor of 3 (never reveal slower than 3 points/frame) meant that with few total points, `totalPoints / drawFrames` always rounded to 0 regardless of how large the requested `drawFrames` budget was, so `pointsPerFrame` pinned at exactly 3 no matter what duration was asked for — the reveal always finished in `totalPoints / 3` frames, completely deaf to the target. Underneath that, there's also a genuine physical ceiling: a point-by-point reveal can't go slower than 1 point/frame (nothing more granular exists to show once every point already has its own frame), so a doodle with only ~90 total points has a hard ~3-second ceiling on how long its reveal can honestly be, no matter what's requested — stretching further than that needs an actual chapter pause, not a slower reveal.

**Fixed two ways:** (1) `computeContentDurationBudget` now takes `totalPoints` and caps `drawFrames` at `max(minDrawFrames, totalPoints)` when a target is set — if the requested draw budget exceeds what the content can actually support, it's capped down to the achievable maximum and a new `wasCapped: Bool` flag is set (mirrors `wasBumped`, just the opposite direction — too little content instead of too many pauses). (2) `buildVideo(...)`'s `pointsPerFrame` floor is now conditional: stays at 3 for legacy/nil-target doodles (byte-for-byte unchanged from before this feature existed), drops to 1 when a target is actively set, so sparse content can stretch as far as it honestly can rather than being artificially capped at the old floor. `VideoTimelineView`'s `durationSection` gained a second inline warning next to the existing pause-overflow one: "Not enough drawing detail to fill Xs — reveal will only take Ys. Draw more, or add a chapter pause to reach your target." All three `computeContentDurationBudget` call sites in `VideoTimelineView.swift` and the one in `DoodleVideoExport.swift` updated to pass `totalPoints` (`VideoTimelineView` computes its own from `document.drawingLayers`, mirroring the exporter's own calculation). Not yet re-verified on device — same standing caveat, but this was caught and fixed same-session, before ever being called "done."

**UI redesigned from toggle+slider to a preset picker row, per direct feedback.** The on/off toggle framed "no target set" as an absent state, but every video has *some* length — even the legacy/default one — so "off" was a misleading frame from the start; a free-drag slider also implied more precision than actually mattered for picking a TikTok-length target. Replaced with a row of tap targets — **Default / 20s / 30s / 45s / 60s / 90s** — mirroring the exact chip-button pattern `ChapterBreakEditSheet` already uses for its own duration presets a few hundred lines down in the same file, so the one screen now has one consistent interaction for "pick a duration" instead of two different ones. "Default" sets `targetContentDurationSeconds = nil` (the untouched legacy path); the five presets set an explicit value. The `Pauses + Draw = Total` breakdown is now shown unconditionally (previously only appeared once the toggle was flipped on) — since a length exists either way, hiding the breakdown behind a toggle no longer made sense once "Default" became just another selectable option rather than an absence of one. `minAllowedTarget` (the slider's lower bound) is now dead with the slider gone — removed outright rather than left orphaned, since this was same-session, never-shipped code. A **10s** chip was added to the preset row shortly after (`durationPresets` now `[10, 20, 30, 45, 60, 90]`) per direct request, for the shortest quick-post TikTok length.

**Bug: real-device test showed the exported video consistently overshooting its target — 20s requested → 29s actual, 30s → 42s, 60s → 1:43.** Root cause was a structural integer-division problem in `buildVideo(...)`, not the budget math itself (the budget's own `resolvedTotalSeconds` was correct — this was purely an execution-side bug in how the reveal was actually chunked into frames). `pointsPerFrame` was computed **once**, as a floored `Int` (`totalPoints / durationBudget.drawFrames`), then reused unchanged to chunk *every stroke independently* via `let end = min(cursor + pointsPerFrame, line.points.count)`. Two compounding problems: (1) flooring the divisor before dividing systematically inflates the frame count you get back out — e.g. 1000 points over a 300-frame budget floors to `pointsPerFrame = 3`, but `1000 / 3` re-chunked is 334 frames, not 300, and the relative error gets worse the smaller the divisor; (2) each individual stroke's *last* chunk rounds up to finish that stroke (can't leave a partial stroke undrawn), and that per-stroke rounding waste is additive — a doodle with many short strokes accumulates far more overshoot than one long stroke with the same total point count, which lines up with why the overshoot scaled up disproportionately at higher targets (a 60s target implies a slower reveal, i.e. a larger `pointsPerFrame`, i.e. more strokes finishing with an oversized final chunk each).

**Fixed** with a Bresenham/error-diffusion-style fractional carry, active only when a target duration is actually set (nil/legacy behavior is byte-for-byte unchanged): a `pointsPerFrameCarry: Double` accumulator persists across the *entire* reveal (not reset per stroke), incremented each chunk by the true fractional rate `totalPoints / drawFrames` (no premature flooring), floored to get that chunk's integer step size, with the leftover fraction carried into the next chunk rather than discarded. This is the same technique that keeps a line-drawing algorithm from drifting off its true slope — errors get carried forward and corrected on the next step instead of silently accumulating. New `nextChunkEnd(_:_:)` local function inside `buildVideo(...)` (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`, right after the `durationBudget`/`pointsPerFrame` setup) wraps this; the 3 real per-stroke chunking sites (`needsFull` eraser/non-eraser branch, the incremental-eraser-delta branch, the incremental-stroke-delta branch) now call `nextChunkEnd(cursor, line.points.count)` instead of the old inline `min(cursor + pointsPerFrame, ...)`. The identical-looking line inside `buildStates(...)` (the separate, entirely unused, zero-call-site function elsewhere in this same file) was deliberately left untouched — required doing this as 3 individually-scoped edits rather than a `replace_all`, specifically to avoid touching that dead function's matching string. Verified via brace/paren count that the file is still balanced after the edit. **Confirmed working on a real re-test** — Eddie reported back "now its working" after this fix, before moving on to the UI feedback below.

**"Default" chip removed from the duration picker — per direct feedback: "i think i understand but the user wont [understand what Default means]. can we get rid of it?"** `targetContentDurationSeconds = nil` (the pre-3.1b1 fixed-~10s-draw legacy path) is still fully supported structurally — `computeContentDurationBudget`'s nil branch is untouched, and old `.skadoodle` files still decode the field as nil with zero errors — but nil is no longer something any part of the UI sets on purpose. Three coordinated changes: (1) `VideoTimelineView.swift`'s `durationSection` — the "Default" `durationChip` (which set `targetContentDurationSeconds = nil`) removed from the row entirely, leaving just the six numbered presets; the breakdown text's comment updated from "Default is a real length too" to "every choice here is a real length," since there's no longer a Default option to explain away. (2) `DrawScreen.swift`'s `@State private var targetContentDurationSeconds: Double? = nil` changed to `= 20` — a brand-new doodle now starts with a concrete 20s target (close to the old ~17s legacy total) rather than nil, so the very first time the Video Timeline sheet opens, a chip is already highlighted. All 4 existing clear-canvas reset sites (Clear Drawing, Clear Stamps, Clear All, and the single-item-clear shortcut) changed from resetting to `nil` to resetting to `20`, matching the new default — same reasoning, a clear should land you back at a normal state, not an unrepresentable one. `restoreSkadoodleData(_:)` now coalesces `doc.targetContentDurationSeconds ?? 20` instead of passing the raw (possibly-nil) decoded value straight through, so re-editing an old pre-3.1b1 doodle immediately gets a real value instead of carrying nil forward silently. (3) `VideoTimelineView.swift` gained a defensive `.onAppear { if targetContentDurationSeconds == nil { targetContentDurationSeconds = 20 } }` as a second safety net for any nil that reaches this screen despite the above (belt-and-suspenders — with (2) in place there shouldn't be a live code path that still produces nil, but this guarantees the row is never rendered with nothing selected regardless). Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as the rest of this feature.

**Next, reported but not yet addressed: on iPhone the duration chip row is squished — the six preset buttons wrap awkwardly ("secs" text clipping) rather than fitting the screen width.** Eddie's own suggested fix: convert the row from a fixed `HStack` to a horizontally scrolling row of pills, same interaction pattern already used elsewhere in this file for the content timeline itself (`ScrollView(.horizontal)` wrapping the layer/stamp/chapter-break chip strip a bit further down in `VideoTimelineView.body`). Not yet built — next item to pick up.

**Second, smaller re-test after the "Default" removal: "10 secs yielded a 22 sec video, 90 secs is 1:40" — much closer than before, but still a real few-second overshoot, worse at the low end.** Root cause was a genuine residual bug in the Bresenham carry fix above, not a new issue: `nextChunkEnd(_:_:)` decremented `pointsPerFrameCarry` by the raw, unclamped `step` value even when the actual chunk got clamped shorter by `min(cursor + step, total)` (i.e. a stroke's last chunk, where there aren't `step` points left to consume). Charging the carry ledger for points that were never actually revealed silently "loses" that fraction forever — it's not refunded to the next stroke — so the carry depletes faster than real progress warrants, and the reveal ends up needing more total calls (frames) than `drawFrames` intended. This scales with how big `step` typically is: at a **low** target (10s), `pointsPerFrameF` is large (revealing many points per frame), so each clamped stroke-ending wastes a large chunk of carry — bigger overshoot. At a **high** target (90s), `pointsPerFrameF` is small (often close to 1), so a clamped tail wastes very little — smaller overshoot. Matches exactly what was reported: a bigger relative miss at 10s than at 90s, and much smaller in absolute terms than the original bug (which scaled multiplicatively with target, not just with stroke count). **Fixed:** `nextChunkEnd` now computes `end` first, then decrements the carry by the *actual* points consumed (`end - cursor`), not the nominal `step` — any leftover from a clamped step now correctly stays banked in the carry for the next stroke instead of evaporating. Verified via brace/paren count that the file is still balanced. Not yet re-tested on device — same standing caveat, but this closes the specific mechanism identified from Eddie's own numbers, and the math checks out arithmetically (constant tail is `holdFrames(60) + outroFrames(24+45+36+30=135)` = 195 frames = 6.5s, so a target `T` should now produce a total close to `T + 6.5s`).

---

## In Progress — v2.9 b1

### New Features — v2.9 b1
- **New pen attempt: Gold Trim, built as a standalone 13th `PenType`, then reverted and rebuilt as a Dual Tone style instead.** First version (`PenType.goldTrim`) was Eddie's own idea after seeing the Daily Doodle hero card's ornate gold frame (`GradientFrame`/`OrnateGoldFrame`/`ScallopRingShape`, all in `TodayTab.swift`): "can you draw with that?" That version drew every stroke in a fixed bronze/gold palette via three techniques ported from the frame code — a 7-step nested-stroke bevel (dark-to-light concentric rings, mirroring `GradientFrame`'s 16 rings), a thin rope-twist center seam (mirroring `OrnateGoldFrame`'s seam), and small scalloped highlight dots at regular arc-length intervals (standing in for `ScallopRingShape`'s bulges, since a true parallel-offset curve for an arbitrary open path was judged not worth the complexity). It was wired in as the 13th pen icon in the main `PenStudioSheet` grid (which was also given a scroll-tolerant rewrite — see below).
  - **Reverted and redesigned per direct feedback, before ever reaching a device.** Eddie's call after seeing the concept described back to him: drop the standalone pen icon entirely, fold it into **Dual Tone** as a new named style instead (`DualToneStyle.trim = "Trim"`, inserted between `.braid` and `.hairy` — both in the enum declaration, which drives `DualToneStyleChip`'s row order via `allCases`, and in `drawDualToneLine`'s switch). The whole fixed-bronze-palette/bevel-rings/seam/bump-dots mechanic was thrown out along with it — `PenType.goldTrim` and its `drawGoldTrimLine(_:in:)` function were deleted outright (not left as dead code), and every touch point that had been added for it (`PenType.displayName`/`.icon`, `renderLine`'s switch, `DoodleFormat.swift` encode+decode, `DrawScreen.swift`'s `allPens`+`penTypesMatch`+restore-switch, `CustomStampViews.swift`'s restore-switch) was removed again — confirmed clean via a repo-wide grep for `goldTrim`/`gold trim` turning up zero remaining references.
  - **New `.trim` mechanic:** three parallel adjacent lines instead of a scalloped bevel ring. The middle line uses the user's live canvas pen color (`line.color`), the two outer lines use the second color set in Pen Studio (`line.colorB`) with a soft blur — "a little blur on the outside colors may work" — and, per a same-session follow-up ("get rid of the little circles"), there are no highlight dots at all in this version. Perpendicular offset direction for the two outer lines uses the same wider lo/hi window (`points[i-1]` to `points[i+1]`) as `.braid`/`.hairy`/`.thorns`, avoiding the raw-adjacent-point jitter that Calligraphy hit earlier this same version. The blur itself is real `GraphicsContext` filtering, not a fake — both outer lines are drawn inside one `context.drawLayer { ... }` scope with `.addFilter(.blur(radius:))` applied once to the whole layer, so all their overlapping per-segment strokes composite into one solid shape *before* the blur runs, rather than blurring each short round-capped segment individually (which would show visible seams/scalloping at segment boundaries). The crisp middle line is stroked separately, outside the blur layer, on top.
  - Since `DualToneStyle` already conforms to `Codable` via its raw `String` value, `.trim` needed no `DoodleFormat.swift` changes at all — unlike `PenType`, which has a hand-written `Codable` conformance. `DualToneStyleChip`'s icon switch (`DrawScreen.swift`) got one added case (`line.3.horizontal`, evoking the three parallel lines).
  - Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as all pen work in this environment. Two math-accurate SVG previews were built to sanity-check this feature: one for the original gold-frame version (nested rings + seam + bumps), and a second, replacing it, for the final three-line-plus-blur version once the design changed — both generated from the same width/color/offset formulas as the real Swift code.
- **Hairy (Dual Tone style) hairs shortened.** `hairBaseLen` in `drawDualToneLine`'s `.hairy` case (`DrawingEngine.swift`) reduced from `baseW * 1.1` to `baseW * 0.4`, per direct feedback that the hairs were too long. Every other hair parameter (core width, hair width, spacing, the sin-hash jitter formulas for length/angle variation) is unchanged — this was a single-constant tweak, not a mechanic change.
- **New Dual Tone style: Tube, rebuilt once after a real miscommunication about the technique.** `DualToneStyle.tube = "Tube"` (appended after `.stars`) — Eddie's idea: a symmetric center-to-edge color gradient across a stroke's width, giving a shaded-3D-cylinder/pipe illusion.
  - **First version used the nested-concentric-stroke technique** (many different-width strokes stacked on the same centerline per segment, dark/edge-color outermost down to light/center-color innermost) — the same mechanism the (already-abandoned) Gold Trim pen bevel had used, just generalized from a fixed bronze/gold palette to `line.color`/`line.colorB`. Described back before building anything further: **rejected** — "what youre doing is totally different. it looks like overlapping circles." Root cause: stacking differently-sized round-capped/joined strokes per segment produces visible layered-ring artifacts at every segment boundary and doesn't nest cleanly around bends, which reads as circles, not a smooth cylindrical fade.
  - **Rebuilt on `.trim`'s footing instead** — genuinely separate parallel lines at fixed perpendicular offsets (same wider lo/hi direction-sampling window as `.trim`/`.braid`/`.hairy`/`.thorns`), each a single flat color, no stacking. Line count is odd and scales with the stroke's actual thickness (`Int(baseW.rounded())`, bumped up by one if even, clamped to 3...25) — directly matches Eddie's own framing, given unprompted and confirmed by repetition rather than assumed: "a line with a thickness of 7... 7 adjacent lines... 1 and 7 [the outer two] would be the pen studio color, and colors move step by step towards the middle color [the live canvas color]." The exact center line (always present, since the count is forced odd) is pure `line.color`; the two outermost lines are pure `line.colorB`; every line in between blends between the two by `blendColors`, keyed on how many slots it sits from center (`t = |lineIdx| / half`). Adjacent slot lines are stroked slightly wider than their exact slot width (`× 1.15`) so there's no hairline gap between them.
  - Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as all pen work this session. Two SVG previews were built for this feature specifically because the visual mechanism changed mid-conversation: the first (nested rings) is what got correctly identified as "overlapping circles" and rejected; the second (seven true parallel lines, matching Eddie's own example count) reflects the rebuilt version.
  - **Real performance problem: the "N parallel lines" version above still restroked all N lines at every point-to-point segment** — up to `lineCount × count` separate `context.stroke` calls for a single pen stroke (e.g. a 25-line-wide tube over a 300-point stroke is 7,500 draw calls). Flagged directly: "your line consists of a zillion lines that are perpendicular along the line... if you do a lot of it the app will become less and less responsive. its kinda dangerous." **Confirmed as a real, not just theoretical, problem** — Eddie separately reported actually seeing it lag on device on a long freehand squiggle (enough points that the per-segment redraw cost became noticeable), not just a concern raised from the code description alone. Eddie's own proposed fix — build each of the N lines as one continuous line for the whole stroke, manually coloring each line to its correct gradient step, rather than re-deriving it segment by segment — is what got built. `drawDualToneLine`'s `.tube` case now precomputes every point's outward normal once (same lo/hi window as before), then for each line index builds a single continuous offset `Path` spanning every point in the stroke and strokes it exactly once. Total stroke calls for the whole style dropped from `lineCount × count` to just `lineCount`, independent of how long the stroke is.
    - **Trade-off, surfaced rather than hidden:** a single `Path`+`StrokeStyle` stroke can't vary its width along its own length without building a custom filled variable-width shape (which would reintroduce the same per-point cost this fix exists to remove) — so Tube no longer tapers to a point at the stroke's start/end, and no longer reacts to live pressure along the stroke, the way every other per-segment pen in this file still does. Width is now fixed per line for the whole stroke. Not yet flagged as a problem by Eddie — noting it here so it isn't forgotten if the flat ends end up looking wrong on a real stroke.
  - **Confirmed on device: no more lag on a long squiggle, and the visual result itself was well received** ("the new pens really nailed it"). First real on-device confirmation for any of this session's pen work.
- **Trim's outer two lines brought closer to the middle line.** `trimSpacing` in `drawDualToneLine`'s `.trim` case (`DrawingEngine.swift`) reduced from `baseW * 0.55` to `baseW * 0.36`, per direct feedback. Line width and blur radius unchanged — spacing only.
- **Confirmed on device: Trim also looks good, no changes requested.**
- **Pen studio grid: stopped chasing exact row-count divisibility.** While Gold Trim was still a standalone pen (13th), it broke the 6-columns/exactly-2-rows fit that Confetti's addition (the 12th) had been tuned for. Rather than re-solve that math again every time a pen gets added, per Eddie's explicit call — "we can just keep adding icons, even if we have to scroll" — the grid was left at 6 columns with no further changes, and the stale in-code comment claiming "6 columns keeps this at exactly 2 rows" was rewritten to describe this scroll-tolerant approach instead. This works because the grid, the dual-tone sub-picker, and `PenPreviewStrip` all already live inside one shared `ScrollView` with a `.large` fallback `.presentationDetents` option (confirmed by reading `PenStudioSheet`'s actual structure before touching anything) — a partial extra row just means slightly more scrolling to reach the preview, not clipped/unreachable content the way the original 9th/10th-pen bug was. This comment/approach stands even though Gold Trim itself ended up not staying in the main grid — the underlying scroll-tolerance is still the right call for whatever pen 13 actually ends up being.

---

## v2.8 b1 (shipped — in App Store distribution)

### Fixes — v2.8 b1
- **Voting Booth / Contest Day archive: doodle image box overflow with tall doodles** — `DailyVotingBoothView.boothPage(for:)` and `DailyContestDayView.dayPage(for:rank:)` (`TodayTab.swift`) both used `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity, maxHeight: .infinity)` directly on `RetryAsyncImage`, with no `GeometryReader` in between, intending a fixed "cover crop" box like the private/public gallery detail screens. That modifier alone doesn't actually decouple the box's size from the image's own content: without a `GeometryReader` breaking the link, `RetryAsyncImage`'s aspect-ratio-driven ideal size still bubbles up through the frame modifier into the VStack's layout pass, so a tall/portrait doodle inflated the whole page's required height and pushed the avatar/question/vote-buttons (Voting Booth) or caption/vote-count (Contest Day archive) off the bottom of the screen. Reported directly: "my doodle areas are diff sizes and are displayed as diff sizes... one of mine is very tall and pushes the voting buttons under the viewing area off the bottom of the screen." **Fixed** in both `boothPage(for:)` and `dayPage(for:rank:)` by wrapping the image (plus its overlaid prev/next arrows, and the rank-0 trophy badge in `dayPage`) in a `GeometryReader`, with `RetryAsyncImage` given an explicit `.frame(width: geo.size.width - 48, height: geo.size.height - 24)` instead of the maxWidth/maxHeight-infinity pair. A `GeometryReader` has no ideal size that depends on its child, so it behaves like a `Spacer` in the VStack's layout — the fixed elements below get sized first, and the image box gets the guaranteed remainder, no matter how tall the source doodle is. Not yet visually confirmed on device — same standing caveat as all the other Today-tab visual/layout work; this environment can't compile or run SwiftUI.

### Polish — v2.8 b1
- **Today tab screen background — light gold.** `TodayTab.body`'s outer `ScrollView` (`TodayTab.swift`) had no explicit background, so it fell through to the plain system background (stark white in light mode) showing between/around the three cards. Added `.background(Color(...).ignoresSafeArea())` — a warm light-gold tint, clearly off-white, so the three (already dark/tinted) cards have some warmth to sit on rather than a stark gap. First pass (`0.99, 0.97, 0.89`) was reported "too light" — barely distinguishable from white. Bumped to `Color(red: 0.98, green: 0.91, blue: 0.72)`, a noticeably more saturated champagne-gold while still reading as a light background, not a fourth competing card color. Fixed color, not a dynamic system one — same reasoning as the fixed tints already used inside the hero/submit/past-winners cards themselves. Not yet visually confirmed on device.
- **Today tab game-chrome/gold motif — decided: keeping it.** Eddie lived with the ornate gold/game-chrome Today tab treatment (bevels, ribbons, medals, parchment) alongside the rest of the app's plainer screens for a while, as planned, and settled the open question: going with gold on Today + normal/plain styling everywhere else, not touching either. No code changes needed — this closes out the open design question above.

### New Features — v2.8 b1
- **New pen: Calligraphy.** `PenType` gained a `.calligraphy` case (`DrawingEngine.swift`) — the first pen in the app whose width is driven by *travel direction* rather than pressure. Every existing pen (including all ten `DualToneStyle` variants) varies width by how hard you press; Calligraphy simulates a flat nib held at a fixed 45° angle instead: width = `baseW * max(minWidthFraction, |sin(travelAngle − nibAngle)|) * taper * pressure`, computed per segment the same way `.braid`/`.hairy` already compute per-segment direction. Full width when travel is perpendicular to the nib edge, near-zero when travel runs along it — the actual mechanic that produces the signature bold-diagonal/thin-vertical calligraphy look, not just another pressure taper. `drawCalligraphyLine(_:in:)` added alongside the other `draw*Line` functions, wired into `renderLine`'s switch. Icon: `signature` (SF Symbol, not used by any other pen). Wired into every place `PenType` is constructed from a string or compared: `PenType`'s `Codable` conformance (`DoodleFormat.swift`, both encode and decode — required for `.skadoodle` file save/load), `DrawScreen.swift`'s `allPens` picker array + `penTypesMatch` equality switch + the persisted-last-pen-type restore switch (`UserDefaults` key `lastPenTypeName`), and `CustomStampViews.swift`'s separate persisted-pen-type restore switch for the doodle stamp canvas (`doodleLastPenTypeName` — a second, independent copy of the same decode logic, confirmed and updated too).
  - **Bug reported on device: "the angle doesn't matter. the width is the same no matter what (unless i press with pen)."** Root cause: the first version computed travel angle from the tight adjacent-point delta (`points[i-1]` to `points[i]`). That two-point delta is dominated by natural hand jitter between consecutive raw touch samples, which swings the local angle around somewhat randomly regardless of the stroke's actual macro direction — a rapidly, near-randomly fluctuating width across many short overlapping round-capped segments visually averages out to what looks like one constant medium width, exactly matching the report. This is a known pitfall this same file had already solved elsewhere: `.braid`/`.hairy`/`.thorns` all sample local direction from a *wider* window (`points[i-1]` to `points[i+1]`, i.e. `lo`/`hi` a full point apart on each side) specifically to smooth out this jitter — Calligraphy just hadn't followed that established convention yet. **Fixed** by switching to the same `lo = max(0, i-1), hi = min(count-1, i+1)` window for `travelAngle`, matching the rest of the file.
- **New pen: Confetti.** `PenType` gained a `.confetti` case (`DrawingEngine.swift`) — small rotated pieces (mix of rounded rects and circles) scattered along the path, no core stroke, same "the pieces ARE the stroke" convention as `.bubble`/`.stars`. Colors cycle through 4 deterministic variants built from the two colors the user actually picked — `line.color`, `line.colorB`, and a lightened blend of each via the existing `blendColors` helper — rather than arbitrary random RGB, so confetti always relates to the chosen palette instead of looking unrelated to it. Rotation, size, and a perpendicular/along-path jitter offset (so pieces don't sit in a perfectly straight line) all use the same sin-hash deterministic pseudo-random technique already established by `.hairy`/`.thorns` (`fabs(sin(seed * constant + offset))`, seeded by an incrementing piece index — stable frame to frame, not re-randomized on every redraw). New `confettiPiece(center:size:rotation:)` helper builds the rotated rounded-rect shape via `Path.applying(_:)`, mirroring the `starPath(...)` free-function pattern already used by `.stars`. Icon: `sparkles`. Wired into the identical 9 touch points as Calligraphy (`PenType.displayName`/`.icon`, `renderLine`'s switch, `DoodleFormat.swift` encode+decode, `DrawScreen.swift`'s `allPens`+`penTypesMatch`+restore-switch, `CustomStampViews.swift`'s restore-switch) — verified 1:1 by grep after the fact.
- **Pen picker grid: 9th/10th tile broke the sheet layout, fixed by going to 6 columns + a 12th pen.** Reported directly: "a 9th style totally screws up the dialog so that the pen preview gets cut off." Root cause: `PenStudioSheet`'s grid was hardcoded to 5 columns, and its `.presentationDetents` (427/643pt on iPad, 0.57/0.83 fraction on iPhone) were tuned for exactly 2 rows — the original 10 items (9 single-color pens + 1 "Dual Tone" tile) divided evenly into 5×2. Adding Calligraphy as an 11th item left a stray 3rd row with a single tile, pushing total content height past the tuned detent budget and cutting off `PenPreviewStrip` (the live pen preview) at the bottom. Eddie's own proposed fix — round out to an even 12 and switch to 6 columns so it's still exactly 2 rows (12/6 = 2, same row count as the original 10/5 = 2) — is what got built, using Confetti (see above) as the 12th tile alongside Calligraphy as the 11th. `LazyVGrid` column count changed from 5 to 6 (grid spacing 12→8), and `PenTypeCard` shrunk proportionally (icon box height 68→56, corner radius 14→12, icon size 28→22, label 12→10 with `lineLimit(1)`/`minimumScaleFactor(0.75)` added since longer names like "Watercolor"/"Calligraphy"/"Confetti" are tighter in a narrower column) so 12 tiles read comfortably rather than cramped. Since row *count* is unchanged (still 2), the existing `.presentationDetents` values were left untouched — the per-row height actually shrank slightly with the smaller card, so the original budget still has margin.
  - Not yet visually confirmed on device for any of the three items above — same standing caveat as everything else in this environment; math-accurate SVG previews (Calligraphy's angle-vs-width rose + a sample flowing stroke; Confetti's scattered-piece stroke) were generated separately to sanity-check both formulas using the exact same code, but that's not a substitute for seeing the real pens on canvas and the real sheet layout at 6 columns.

---

## v2.4 b7 (submitted June 30, 2026)

### Fixes — v2.4 b7
- **Eraser wrong color when canvas color has opacity < 100%** — `DrawingCanvas` in DrawScreen received `canvasColor` as its `.background()`, creating a double-layer: the `canvasColor` fill at the top of the ZStack body (line 3173) PLUS `DrawingCanvas.background(canvasColor)` on top of it. Two semi-transparent layers stacked to a more-saturated composite; the eraser only accounted for one layer and painted a lighter color. Fix: `DrawingCanvas` in DrawScreen now receives `canvasColor: .clear` — its background is invisible; the ZStack-level `canvasColor` fill is the sole canvas background. Added `opaqueCanvasColor` computed property to DrawScreen (canvas color pre-composited over white, same formula as video export) and used it in `drawingLayerView` so eraser paints the visually-correct fully-opaque composited color. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Eraser wrong color when background image has opacity < 100% AND canvas color has opacity < 100%** — `processedBackgroundForEraser` passed `UIColor(canvasColor)` (possibly semi-transparent) as the base fill to `_BgEffectsImageCache.get`. The UIKit bitmap context composites a semi-transparent fill slightly differently than SwiftUI (color-space / P3 vs sRGB path), producing a "darker shade" mismatch. Fix: `processedBackgroundForEraser` now pre-composites canvas color over white in sRGB (same formula as `opaqueCanvasColor`) before passing to the cache, guaranteeing a fully opaque base and eliminating the UIKit/SwiftUI discrepancy. Also added `UIColor.white` pre-fill in `_BgEffectsImageCache.get` (opaque context initializes to black, not white). (`DrawingEngine.swift`)
- **Timelapse video shows black/wrong background with semi-transparent canvas color** — `runningComposite` and `belowComp` renders in `DoodleVideoExport` used `canvasUIColor` directly. If canvas color had alpha < 1, `imgFormat.opaque = true` composited over black. Fix: added `opaqueCanvasColor` pre-composite (same formula) in the video export; all render calls use the opaque version. (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
- **Timelapse video colors lighter than live canvas** — H.264 encoder was blindly converting RGB → YCbCr without color space tagging, causing iOS to apply incorrect transfer curves. Fix: added `AVVideoColorProperties` (ITU-R BT.709 primaries, transfer function, and YCbCr matrix) to both the `AVAssetWriterInput` video settings and the `CVPixelBuffer` attributes. (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
- **No share button in video player** — `AVPlayerViewController.customOverlayViewController` is tvOS-only. Fix: wrapped `AVPlayerViewController` in a `VideoPlayerContainerVC` (UIViewController child), which adds a share button (↑ icon) as a sibling view on top of the player. Tapping opens `UIActivityViewController` for AirDrop, save, messages, etc. (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
- **AI processing slow (waiting for Gemini)** — Two-phase AI: Apple Vision (`VNClassifyImageRequest`) runs on-device instantly (~50ms), shows caption and tags immediately, then Gemini runs concurrently and silently upgrades the result when it finishes. No spinner shown to user; the result card appears immediately with Vision results. Added `VisionProvider` class implementing `AIProvider` protocol; `handleDone` runs both phases in a single `Task`. (`DrawingEngine.swift`, `DrawScreen.swift`)

## v2.4 b4 (submitted June 30, 2026)

### Fixes — v2.4 b4
- **Color picker `+` button stuck after cancelled swipe + X tap** — `presentationControllerWillDismiss` sets `interactiveDismiss = true` when a swipe starts. If the user cancelled the swipe (no delegate callback exists for swipe-cancel) and then tapped X, `colorPickerViewControllerDidFinish` early-returned on `!interactiveDismiss`, leaving `picker` non-nil and `isPresented` stuck true. Next `+` tap was a no-op (no state change). Fix: (1) reset `interactiveDismiss = false` in `colorPickerViewControllerDidSelectColor` so any color interaction after a cancelled swipe clears the flag; (2) added stale-picker check at top of `presentIfNeeded` — if `picker.presentingViewController == nil`, clear all stuck state before attempting re-presentation; (3) `+` button action now forces `showPenColorPicker = false` then `async true` to guarantee `updateUIView` fires even if state was stuck. (`StampTools.swift`, `DrawScreen.swift`)
- **"Resume Last Doodle?" alert appearing on re-edit** — On first launch after restart, `entryToEdit` was a `let` property frozen at DrawScreen's creation time. SwiftUI sometimes creates the sheet content before the `entryToEdit = entry` render cycle fully commits, so DrawScreen was created with `entryToEdit = nil`. `.onAppear` then hit the `else` branch and showed the resume alert (since `current.skadoodle` existed from the last session). Fix: changed `let entryToEdit: SnoodleEntry?` to `@Binding var entryToEdit: SnoodleEntry?` so `.onAppear` reads the live value from ContentView's state rather than the snapshot at creation time. ContentView now passes `$entryToEdit`. (`DrawScreen.swift`, `ContentView.swift`)
- **Processing time logging added** — `handleDone` and `saveEntry` print timing for `renderCanvasWithStamps` and `callSnoodleAI`. Confirmed: render is ~0.05s; slowness is entirely Gemini API retries on 503 (server load), not a code issue. Logs are intentionally left in for ongoing diagnostics. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

## v2.4 b3 (submitted June 29, 2026)

### Fixes — v2.4 b3
- **Stamp drag blocked when another stamp was selected** — `gestureRecognizerShouldBegin` and `handleLongPress.began` were blocking ALL stamp drags when `selectedStampId != nil`. Narrowed the guard: only blocks instant-pan and LP on the stamp that currently has the magic menu open (by checking `hit?.id == selectedStampId`). Other stamps can still be dragged freely while one is selected. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **LP/pan race causing snug rect flash during instant drag** — `UILongPressGestureRecognizer` (0.05s in stamp mode) could fire before the pan recognized movement, briefly setting `isLongPressing = true` and flashing the snug rect. Fix: raised LP minimum press duration in stamp mode from 0.05s to 0.3s, giving the pan time to own the touch first. Also: in `handleStampPan.began`, if LP already fired and set `selectedStampId` on the panned stamp, call `onCanvasTap()` to deselect immediately. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Canvas defaults to pen mode** — `isStampMode` initial value changed from `false` to `true`. Stamp mode is the primary interaction mode; drawing still works in stamp mode on empty areas. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Pen studio second color not showing as selected in recent list** — `dualToneColorB` was initialized from a legacy palette-index key and never persisted as RGBA, so custom colors were lost on relaunch and the swatch selection highlight failed. Fix: load/save `dualToneColorB` using `"dualToneColorB_rgba"` key (RGBA `[Double]` array). On sheet open, ensure `colorB` is in `recentColors` so the correct swatch is highlighted. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

## v2.4 b2 (submitted June 29, 2026)

### Fixes — v2.4 b2
- **Magic palette drag triggering stamp LP when finger over stamp** — `UILongPressGestureRecognizer` (0.05s stamp-mode LP) could fire while the user dragged the palette with a finger over a selected stamp, causing the stamp to highlight (`isLongPressing = true`) and `showStampMagicMenu = false` (palette disappears). Fix: added `guard parent.selectedStampId == nil else { return }` to `handleLongPress.began` — LP drag is fully blocked while any stamp has the magic menu open. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

## v2.4 b1 (submitted June 29, 2026)

### Fixes — v2.4 b1
- **Timelapse needsFull path now O(all_layers) + O(current_layer × chunks)** — Previously, strokes on non-topmost layers called `rebuildComposite(overrideLines:)` per chunk: O(all_layers × chunks), ~130ms/chunk. Now pre-renders `belowComp` (opaque: canvas + bg + everything below the layer) and `aboveComp` (transparent: everything above the layer) once per stroke, then per chunk renders only the current layer in isolation with `canvasColor=.clear, backgroundImage=nil` and composites `belowComp → currentLayer → aboveComp`. Eraser with `.clear` canvas color punches transparent holes → `belowComp` shows through correctly. `aboveComp` always stays on top. (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
- **Background picker long-press: Use as Stamp + Extract Objects** — Long-pressing a background thumbnail now shows three options: "Use as Stamp" (places full image as inline stamp, centered, magic menu opens), "Extract Objects" (runs Vision segmentation, same as before), "Remove". Previously only "Remove" was available. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Precision tweak panel dismissing on button tap (main canvas)** — `TweakRepeatButton` uses `DragGesture`, not a UIKit Button, so `shouldReceive`'s class-name check didn't block it. The window-level tap recognizer fired, found no stamp hit, and called `onCanvasTap()` → deselect. Fix: added `blockCanvasTap: Bool` to `WindowPinchView`; set to `showMenuTweak` in DrawScreen. `handleWindowTap` skips `onCanvasTap()` when `blockCanvasTap` is true. Pinch/rotation unaffected. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Black canvas on gallery re-edit** — SwiftUI split `entryToEdit = entry` and `showingDraw = true` across render cycles, presenting the sheet before the entry was committed. Fix: `DispatchQueue.main.async` between the two assignments guarantees one run-loop separation. (`ContentView.swift`)
- **`restoreSkadoodleData` deleting valid entry files** — empty-doc guard was also firing for gallery re-edits (which legitimately restore from the entry's `.skadoodle`). Fix: guard only deletes `current.skadoodle` when `entryToEdit == nil`. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Use as Stamp (background picker) not registering in tray / not placing on canvas** — `onUseAsStamp` handler now calls `CustomStampManager.shared.addStamp` to register the image in the photo tray, sets `stamp.customImageId`, calls `appendStampToLayer`, opens magic menu, and schedules snug scan. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Stamp picker: selected stamp not moving to most-recent position** — `autoPlaceStamp()` now calls `CustomStampManager.shared.moveToTop(id:)` before placing. `moveToTop` added to `CustomStampManager`. (`DrawScreen.swift`, `CustomStampManager.swift`)
- **Background extract placing 7 duplicate stamps** — `ObjectSegmentationSheet`'s `.task` was firing once per ForEach history item as the sheet dismissed, auto-confirming single-object segmentations 7 times. Fix: added `bypassSingle: Bool` param (default `true`); background-extract path passes `false`. Added `didAutoSelect` guard to prevent multiple fires. (`CustomStampViews.swift`, `DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Snug rect smaller than "Use as Stamp" stamp** — `inlineImage` was rendered with `.scaledToFill().clipped()` while `customImageId` path used `.scaledToFit()`. Snug scan measured the fit area but the stamp displayed fill, causing mismatch. Fixed both render paths to `.scaledToFit()`. (`StampCanvas.swift`, `StampTools.swift`)
- **Stamp mode: only pen button switches to pen mode** — Removed `isStampMode = false` from `onStampModeDragOnEmpty`. Drawing on empty canvas in stamp mode now draws without switching mode. The pen button is the only way to exit stamp mode. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Stamp palette drifting off-screen** — `@AppStorage("stampPanelOffsetX_v3")` / `stampPanelOffsetY_v3` could accumulate to an off-screen value across sessions. Fix: `clampedMenuOffset` computed var in DrawScreen clamps saved offset to keep panel on-canvas. Live drag in `StampMagicMenu` also clamped in `.onChanged` so the panel can't be dragged off during a gesture. (`DrawScreen.swift`, `StampTools.swift`)
- **Stamp palette: drag-and-release firing button action** — `StampMagicMenu` drag gesture sets `isDragging = true` on first movement; all `sideButton` and `sideButtonLP` / `_SideLPButton` actions guard against `isDragging`. Dragging and releasing over flip/rotate/trash/dismiss no longer triggers the action. (`StampTools.swift`)
- **Stamp palette default position too close to canvas edge** — base position moved from 6pt to 16pt right margin. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Instant stamp drag (colorforms feel)** — Added `UIPanGestureRecognizer` (`stampPanRecognizer`) to `WindowPinchView`. `gestureRecognizerShouldBegin` returns false unless in stamp mode and touching a stamp — empty-canvas touches fall through to drawing normally. Dragging a stamp is now instant (zero delay, no snug rect, no selection). `handleStampPan.began` clears any LP state that fired before movement was detected; `handleLongPress.began` skips if stamp pan already owns the touch. Long-press (0.05s) still selects stamps and opens the magic menu. `WindowPinchView` call extracted to `var windowPinchView: some View` to avoid Swift type-check timeout. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

## In Progress — v2.3 b7

### Fixes — v2.3 b7
- **Text stamp composer colors/shadow not persisting** — `selectedTextColor`, `selectedTextBgColor`, `shadowEnabled`, `shadowColor`, `shadowBlur`, `shadowOffsetX/Y` were all `@State` in `TextComposerSheet`, resetting to defaults on every open. Fix: added `_tcLoadColor`/`_tcSaveColor` private helpers (RGBA stored as `[Double]` in UserDefaults). State vars now load from UserDefaults at init. Values are written back to UserDefaults in the `onPlace` closure. Edit-stamp path (`onAppear` overrides) unchanged. (`StampTools.swift`)
- **Eraser opacity ignored on live canvas** — When a background image was set at opacity < 1, the eraser painted a semi-transparent version of the image onto the drawing layer, which then double-composited with the background image layer below in the ZStack, making erased areas appear more opaque than undrawn regions. Fix: `_BgEffectsImageCache` now produces a **fully opaque** pre-composited image (image at bgOpacity over the base canvas color) instead of a semi-transparent one. `DrawingLayerCanvas` gains a `baseCanvasColor` param (the actual selected canvas color, not `.clear`); `renderLine` and `drawEraserLine` gain the same param and forward it to the cache. (`DrawingEngine.swift`, `DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Video shows black in erased areas** — In the export/video path, `renderLine` was called with `canvasColor = canvasSwiftUI` (solid, e.g., black). `drawEraserLine`'s condition checked `canvasColor != .clear` first, so it painted the solid canvas color instead of the background image. Fix: `drawEraserLine` now checks for `backgroundImage` first (before `canvasColor`), so the image path is always used when a background image is present regardless of `canvasColor`. `renderCanvasWithStamps` computes `eraserBgImage` — a fully opaque pre-composited image — and passes it as `backgroundImage` to `renderLine` for drawing layers, fixing the double-opacity issue in the export path too. (`DrawingEngine.swift`, `StampTools.swift`)

## In Progress — v2.3 b5 (submitted)

### Fixes — v2.3 b5
- **Canvas gestures bleed through text composer and color pickers** — `WindowPinchView.shouldReceive` now checks `blockGestures` flag (passed from DrawScreen); true whenever any sheet/picker is open over the canvas. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Layer up/down buttons dim on press + selection haptic** — `sideButtonLP` extracted to private `_SideLPButton` struct with `@State isPressed` + `DragGesture(minimumDistance:0)` for press state; `UISelectionFeedbackGenerator` fires on each tap. (`StampTools.swift`)
- **extractAllLayersAsStamps firing accidentally on rapid layer-button taps** — disconnected `onBackgroundDoubleTap` from `extractAllLayersAsStamps`; now accessible only via BG chip `···` menu in layers panel. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Timelapse plays in creation order, not z-order** — `createdAt: Date` added to `DrawingLayer` and `PlacedStamp`; encoded as `timeIntervalSince1970` with `decodeIfPresent` fallback to epoch for old files (stable sort preserves z-order for them). `DoodleVideoExport` sorts `layerOrder` by `createdAt` before building state list. (`DrawingEngine.swift`, `StampTools.swift`, `DoodleFormat.swift`, `DoodleVideoExport.swift`)

### Notes — v2.3 b5
- Timelapse creation-order playback requires strategic layer creation to work well — especially around erasing. Acceptable as a power-user quirk for now; video feature is additive, not core. Will revisit.

## In Progress — v2.3 b4 (submitted)

### New Features

#### Recent Colors System (all color pickers)
Every horizontal color picker now uses a shared persistent recent-colors list instead of the fixed palette.

- **`RecentColors`** (DrawingEngine.swift) — static struct; key `"recentColors_v1"`; max 20; seeded from `paletteColors` on first run; `load()` / `add(_:)` / `save(_:)`; `add` deduplicates with 0.002 RGBA tolerance before prepending.
- **`RecentCanvasColors`** (DrawingEngine.swift) — same pattern for canvas background; key `"recentCanvasColors_v1"` + separate `"selectedCanvasColor_v1"` for the most-recently-chosen canvas color. `loadSelected()` migrates from old `"lastCanvasColorIndex"` AppStorage key on first run.
- **`Color.isApproximatelyEqual(to:)`** (DrawingEngine.swift) — 0.002 RGBA tolerance; used for dedup and swatch selection highlighting.
- **`ColorSwatchView`** (DrawingEngine.swift) — circular swatch of given size; shows `CheckerboardView` behind color when alpha < 1 (standard iOS transparency convention); draws selection ring when `isSelected`.
- **`CheckerboardView`** (DrawingEngine.swift) — `Canvas`-based gray/white tiled checkerboard; was previously duplicated in `CustomStampViews.swift` (removed there).

Color pickers upgraded to recent-colors + `+` button:
- **Pen color row** (DrawScreen.swift) — `+` → `ColorPickerSheet`; `ColorSwatchView` replaces raw `Circle`; `isApproximatelyEqual` for selection.
- **Pen studio second color** (DrawScreen.swift `PenStudioSheet`) — same upgrade.
- **Canvas background color row** (`CanvasColorPickerView` in DrawScreen.swift) — `+` → `ColorPickerSheet`; `ColorSwatchView` with 42pt size; `RecentCanvasColors` list.
- **Text stamp foreground, background, shadow color rows** (StampTools.swift `TextStampComposer`) — all three rows upgraded.
- **Doodle stamp canvas pen color row** (CustomStampViews.swift `DoodleStampCreatorView`) — upgraded; `colorCircle()` rewritten to use `ColorSwatchView` + `isApproximatelyEqual`; `+` button added.

#### `ColorPickerSheet` (StampTools.swift)
Wraps SwiftUI's `ColorPicker` in a sheet with a large tappable row ("Open Color Wheel / Tap to pick any color"). Uses SwiftUI's internal `ColorPicker` — **not** `UIColorPickerViewController` directly (attempting to present `UIColorPickerViewController` as sheet content crashes with "tried to present a nil modal view controller" because it tries to present sub-controllers on SwiftUI's presentation host). The `ColorPicker` row shows the current color swatch + instructions + chevron. Done button commits and dismisses.

#### Text Stamp Shadow (PlacedStamp)
- **`PlacedStamp` new fields** (StampTools.swift): `shadowEnabled: Bool = false`, `shadowColor: Color = .black`, `shadowBlur: Double = 4.0`, `shadowOffsetX: Double = 2.0`, `shadowOffsetY: Double = 2.0`.
- **Shadow in all 4 render paths:**
  - **Live canvas** (`StampTextRenderView.updateUIView` in StampCanvas.swift) — `label.layer.shadowColor/Opacity/Radius/Offset`; `container.layer.masksToBounds = false` when shadow enabled (must not clip shadow).
  - **UIKit image cache** (`StampCanvas.emojiImage(for:)`) — `NSShadow` added to `NSAttributedString` attrs; cache key includes shadow params; `fmt.opaque = false` when shadow enabled.
  - **Export** (`renderCanvasWithStamps` in StampTools.swift) — SwiftUI `.shadow()` modifier on text stamp view.
  - **Layers panel / StampRenderView** (StampCanvas.swift) — SwiftUI `.shadow()` modifier on `StampTextRenderView`.
- **Shadow UI in `TextStampComposer`** — Toggle (on/off) + color row + Blur slider (0–20) + Offset X/Y sliders (−15 to 15) appear when enabled.
- **`DoodleFormat.swift`** — 5 new `CodingKeys` (`shadowEnabled/Color/Blur/OffsetX/OffsetY`); encode writes all 5; decode uses `decodeIfPresent` with defaults for backward compat with old `.skadoodle` files.

#### Canvas Background Color — Color-based (not index-based)
- Removed `@AppStorage("lastCanvasColorIndex")` and dead `lastNonWhiteColorIndex` from DrawScreen.
- Added `@State private var selectedCanvasColor: Color = RecentCanvasColors.loadSelected()`.
- `var canvasColor: Color { selectedCanvasColor }`.
- `SkadoodleDocument` (DoodleFormat.swift) — added `canvasColorRGBA: CodableColor? = nil`; `canvasColorIndex: Int = 0` kept with default for backward-compat decode. New saves write `canvasColorRGBA`; old files fall back to `canvasColorOptions[canvasColorIndex]`.
- `CanvasColorPickerView` interface changed: `currentIndex: Int` / `onSelect: (Int)` → `currentColor: Color` / `onSelectColor: (Color)`.

### Compiler fixes (v2.3 b1)
- **`CheckerboardView` redeclaration** — removed duplicate from `CustomStampViews.swift`; canonical definition in `DrawingEngine.swift`.
- **`DoodleStampCreatorView` type-check timeouts** — extracted `doodleToolbarRow2()` `@ViewBuilder` func and `handleDoodleTextPlace(...)` + `doodleTextComposerSheet()` helpers to break up expressions the Swift compiler couldn't type-check in reasonable time.
- **`ColorPickerSheet(selection:)` wrong param name** — correct param is `color:`.

#### Doodle Timelapse Video Export (new file: `DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
Fully self-contained. Reads `SkadoodleDocument`, generates an MP4 timelapse, and presents it via share sheet or inline player. No changes to any other existing file except two additive lines in `GalleryTab.swift`.

**Video structure:**
1. Drawing revealed stroke-by-stroke (point-by-point in chunks of `pointsPerFrame = max(3, totalPoints/300)` — ~300 render steps; simple doodles are short, complex ones longer)
2. Stamps fade in over 8 frames each
3. 2-second hold on finished doodle (60 frames)
4. Outro: dark overlay dissolves in (24f), branding card holds centered (45f) — app icon + "Skadoodle" + "skadoodle.nyc" + doodle date — then shrinks/slides to small footer at bottom (36f), footer zooms from scale 0.28 → 0.44 over 15f then holds (30f total)

**Key classes/structs:**
- `DoodleTimelapseExporter` (`@MainActor` class) — builds state list, drives AVAssetWriter loop, yields every 10 frames to avoid watchdog kill
- `OutroFrameView` — SwiftUI view rendered via `ImageRenderer` for each outro frame; uses `smoothstep` easing for shrink animation
- `TimelapseButton` — in `SnoodleDetailView` action bar (film icon); exports → iOS share sheet
- `TilePlayBadge` — in `SnoodleTile` bottom-right corner (play circle); exports → full-screen `AVPlayerViewController` auto-play
- `VideoPlayerView` — `UIViewControllerRepresentable` wrapping `AVPlayerViewController`

**Canvas size:** saved JPEG has `scale=1`, so `img.size` is physical pixels. Divide by `currentScreenScale()` to get point size for `renderCanvasWithStamps`; multiply back for pixel buffer dimensions.

**Pixel buffer:** `kCVPixelFormatType_32BGRA` + `noneSkipFirst | byteOrder32Little`. No coordinate flip — CVPixelBuffer-backed CGBitmapContext stores row 0 at the top of the visual frame; `ctx.draw(cgImage, in:)` maps correctly without any additional transform.

**`UIScreen.main` deprecation fixed** — uses `currentScreenScale()` / `currentScreenBounds()` helpers that go through `UIWindowScene`.

**GalleryTab.swift changes (additive only):**
- `SnoodleTile`: `.overlay(alignment: .bottomTrailing)` with `TilePlayBadge` when `entry.hasSkadoodleFile`
- `SnoodleDetailView.card(for:)`: `TimelapseButton(entry: entry)` added to action bar HStack

### Fixes — v2.3 b2
- **Timelapse outro zoom pop** — after branding card shrinks to footer position (scale 0.28), it zooms to 0.44 over 15 frames with smoothstep easing, then holds. (`DoodleVideoExport.swift`)
- **Eraser thickness independent from pen** — `otherWidth: CGFloat` state (persisted as `"lastEraserWidth"`, default 20) swaps with `lineWidth` when toggling eraser on/off. `ThicknessPanel` gains `storageKey` param and saves to the correct key. (`DrawScreen.swift`, `StampTools.swift`)
- **Eraser chip in layers panel** — drawing layers whose lines are all eraser strokes show a faded `eraser.fill` icon in their chip thumbnail instead of a blank white rectangle. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

### Fixes — v2.3 b3
- **Eraser now covers stamps** — `drawEraserLine` changed from `.clear` blend mode (punches transparent holes) to normal blend painting solid `canvasColor`. The eraser now works exactly like the pen but paints the canvas background color — covering stamps and anything below. (`DrawingEngine.swift`)
- **`EraserSolidView`** added to `DrawingEngine.swift` — transparent-background Canvas that renders eraser paths as solid canvasColor strokes. Available for future use.
- **Drawing after stamp now creates new layer above it** — `appendStampToLayer` now sets `userSelectedLayerId = nil` after placing a stamp. On the next stroke, `needsNewLayer` evaluates true (topIsStamp && userSelectedLayerId == nil) and a fresh drawing layer is created above the stamp. Previously this only worked when the layers panel was open. (`DrawScreen.swift`)

### Fixes — v2.3 b4
- **Two-finger gestures no longer target stamp outside its content** — removed selected-stamp priority from `handlePinch` and `handleRotation`; all stamps now use pure alpha-aware `topmostStampHit`. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Eraser on image background paints image pixels** — `drawEraserLine` uses `GraphicsContext.Shading.tiledImage` with cover-fit math matching the SwiftUI background layer exactly. (`DrawingEngine.swift`)
- **Auto-switch to draw mode when dragging on empty canvas in stamp mode** — `onStampModeDragOnEmpty` callback on `DrawingCanvas` returns `Bool`; first stroke draws immediately without waiting for SwiftUI re-render, via `DrawGestureState` reference-type class. (`DrawingEngine.swift`, `DrawScreen.swift`)
- **Auto-switch to stamp mode when placing from tray** — `autoPlaceStamp()`, `placeFullPhotoStamps()`, `placeMultipleEmojis()` set `isStampMode = true`. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **`needsNewLayer` no longer creates a new layer on every stroke** — `onBeforeDraw` sets `explicitLayerSelection = true` after auto-creating a layer. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **iPad stamp-mode auto-switch** — `PencilInputView` overlay always shown on iPad (was `isIPad && drawingEnabled`); `drawingEnabled` guards inside callbacks handle pen-vs-stamp routing. (`DrawingEngine.swift`)
- **Long press drag in draw mode shows snug rect** — `snugRectOverlay` condition simplified from `isLongPressing && showSnugDuringDrag` to `isLongPressing`. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **After long press drag in draw mode, single-finger touch no longer drags stamp** — `onStampDragEnd` clears `selectedStampId` when `showSnugDuringDrag` is false, preventing `StampContainerView.hitTest` from handing the stamp to its `UIPanGestureRecognizer` on the next touch. (`DrawScreen.swift`)
- **`consolidateDrawingLayers()` confirmed not called in any delete path** — dead code; comment documents it as available for a future "Merge Layers" feature. No code change needed.

### Pending
- **Website Firebase deploy** — Skadoodle website (skadoodle.nyc, Firebase Hosting) was updated with v2.2 marketing content and committed to GitHub (username: `eddienorton`, repo: `skadoodle-website`). Firebase deploy must be run from Eddie's terminal (`npx firebase deploy --only hosting` from `/Users/edwardbrayman/Development/Website/skadoodle`).
- ~~**Timelapse eraser optimization**~~ — **Done (v2.3 b8).** Eraser strokes now use incremental delta rendering: `bgBaseImage` (canvas + processed background, captured before the event loop) is painted into a transparent delta image clipped to each new stroke segment, then composited onto `runningComposite` with source-over. O(1) per chunk. `makeFullRender` removed.
